الناصية وهو ربع الرأس لما روى المغيرة بن شعبة ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم اتي سباطة قوم فبال وتوضأ ومسح على الناصية وخفيه (۵) وسنن الطهارة (٦) غسل اليدين بلکہ مستحب ہے۔ کیونکہ پورے سر کا مسح فرض ہوتا تو صرف پیشانی کی مقدار یا اگلے حصے پر مسح کرنا کافی نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک چوتھائی سر یا پیشانی کی مقدار پر مسح کرنا فرض ہے۔ اور پورے سر پر مسح کرنا سنت ہے۔ (۲) آیت میں سر کا مسح کرنا فرض ہے لیکن کتنی مقدار فرض ہے آیت سے اس کا پتہ نہیں چلتا ہے۔ آیت اس بارے میں مجمل ہے۔ اب حدیث نے اس کی تفسیر کی ہے کہ کم سے کم مقدار پیشانی کے برابر ہے۔ اس سے کم مقدار کا کسی حدیث سے پتا نہیں چلتا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ کم سے کم مقدار فرض ہوگی (۳) ستر عورت چو تھائی کھل جائے تو نماز ٹوٹ جائے گی۔ حج کے موقع پر احرام کی حالت میں چوتھائی سرمنڈوادے تو دم لازم ہوتا ہے۔ جس طرح پورے سر منڈوانے سے دم لازم ہوتا ہے۔ تو ان مقامات پر چوتھائی کل کے قائم مقام ہے اس لئے سر کے مسح میں بھی چوتھائی پورے سر کے قائم مقام ہوگا (۴) قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ ب حرف جر آلہ پر داخل ہو تو اس کا بعض مراد ہوگا اور محل کا کل، اور محل پر داخل ہو تو محل کا بعض مراد ہوگا۔ یہاں بسر محل پر داخل ہے اس لئے سر کا بعض حصہ مراد ہوگا کہ بعض سر کا مسح کرنا کافی ہوگا۔
نا امام شافعی کے نزدیک چند بال کو مسح کرنے سے فرض کی ادائیگی ہو جائے گی۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مسح کرنا مطلق ہے اور مطلق میں دو چار بال مسح کرنا کافی ہو جاتا ہے۔ امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ پورے سر کا مسح کرنا فرض ہے ۔ وہ ان احادیث سے استدلال کرتے ہیں جن میں پورے سر پر مسح کرنا ثابت ہے۔ یہ احادیث بخاری شریف باب مسح الرأس کلہ ص ۳۳ نمبر ۱۸۵ اور باب مسح الرأس مرۃ ص۳۲ نمبر ۱۹۲ پر مذکور ہیں ۔ عن عبد الله بن زيد ... ثم مسح رأسه بيديه فاقبل بهما وادبر بدا بمقدم رأسه حتى ذهب بهما الى قفاه ثم ردهما الى المكان الذى بدا منہ ۔ ہم اس کا جواب دیتے ہیں کہ وہ احادیث سنیت پر محمول ہیں۔ اور ہم بھی ایک مرتبہ پورے سر پر سح ۔ کرنا سنت قرار دیتے ہیں۔ ان الناصیہ : پیشانی یہاں پیشانی کی مقدار مراد ہے کیوں کہ صرف پیشانی پر مسح کرنے سے کسی کے یہاں مسح ادا نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ آیت میں سر پر مسح کرنے کا حکم دیا گیا ہے۔ مغیرہ بن شعبہ مشہور صحابی ہیں غزوہ خندق کے سال اسلام لائے ہیں اور ۵۰ھ یا ا۵ھ میں وفات پائی ہے۔ ان سے ایک سو چھتیں حدیثیں مروی ہیں۔ سباطۃ : کوڑا ، پھر پھینکنے کی جگہ۔ بال : پیشاب کیا۔
(4) And the obligatory in wiping the head is the amount of the forehead, and that is one quarter of the head. Because it is narrated from Mughirah ibn Shu'bah that the Prophet came to the garbage dump of a people, urinated, performed wudu, and wiped his forehead and his two khuffs. This hadith of Mughirah is mentioned in Muslim in the chapter... On this page is another hadith: 'The Prophet wiped over the khuffs, the front part of his head, and his turban.' Since he wiped only the front part of the head, it is understood that wiping the entire head is not obligatory. An-nasiyah is one quarter of the head, as narrated by Mughirah... And the sunnan of purification: washing the hands is actually mustahabb. Because if wiping the entire head were obligatory, then merely wiping the amount of the forehead or the front part would not suffice. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, wiping one quarter of the head or the forehead area is obligatory, and wiping the entire head is sunnah. (2) The verse makes wiping the head obligatory, but it does not specify the amount; it is mujmal. The hadith explains that the minimum is the forehead. No hadith indicates a smaller amount, so this minimum is fard. (3) If one quarter of the private parts becomes uncovered, the prayer is invalidated. During ihram, if one quarter of the head is shaved, a dam is due, just as for shaving the entire head. In both cases, one quarter stands in place of the whole. So in head wiping, one quarter stands for the whole. (4) The principle is: if the preposition 'ba' enters upon an instrument, it means a part of it and the whole of the place; if it enters upon a place, it means a part of the place. Here 'ba' enters upon 'head' (place), so it means a part of the head, so wiping a part suffices.
Imam Shafi'i holds that wiping a few hairs fulfills the obligation. He says wiping is absolute, and in absolute terms, wiping two or four hairs suffices. Imam Malik says wiping the entire head is obligatory, citing hadiths that prove wiping the entire head, e.g., from Abdullah ibn Zaid: '...then he wiped his head with his hands, bringing them forward and backward, starting from the front of his head until he reached the nape, then returning them to where he started.' Our response: Those hadiths are interpreted as supererogatory. We too consider wiping the entire head once as sunnah. An-nasiyah: forehead; here it means the forehead area, because merely wiping the forehead does not render the wiping valid for anyone, since the verse commands wiping the head. Mughirah ibn Shu'bah is a famous companion who embraced Islam in the year of the Trench and died in 50 AH or 51 AH. He narrated 136 hadiths. Sabatah: garbage dump. Bal: urinated.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage discusses the obligatory amount for wiping the head in wudu, a classic inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi position is that wiping one quarter of the head (approximately the forehead area) is obligatory (fard). This is derived from the hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah where the Prophet wiped only his forehead (an-nasiyah). The text also provides rational argument: if the entire head were fard, then a smaller amount would not suffice. Using qiyas from 'awrah (one-quarter exposure invalidates prayer) and hajj (shaving one-quarter requires dam), one-quarter is deemed equivalent to the whole. Additionally, the Arabic grammar principle regarding the letter 'ba' is invoked: when 'ba' enters upon a place (here 'head'), it indicates a part of that place. The Hanafis respond to Imam Shafi'i (who holds that any wiping, even a few hairs, suffices) by arguing that the absolute command requires at least a meaningful part, and no hadith indicates less than the forehead. They respond to Imam Malik (who requires full head) by interpreting the hadiths of full head wipe as supererogatory (sunnah), not obligation. Thus, the Hanafi middle position is that one quarter is fard, and the full head is sunnah.

Key Terms
الناصية (an-nasiyah): The front part of the head, specifically the forehead area; amount equivalent to one quarter of the head.
ربع (rub'): One quarter; here the minimum obligatory part of the head to be wiped.
فرض (fard): Obligatory; non-fulfillment invalidates the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the primary source for the Hanafi ruling that one quarter of the head must be wiped?
A) Quran 5:6 alone
B) Hadith of Mughirah
C) Qiyas on awrah
D) Ijma of the Companions

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, wiping one quarter of the head (forehead area) is obligatory in wudu; less than that invalidates the wudu.

Sunnah and Mustahabb: Washing Hands Before Wudu After Sleep
Introduces sunan of wudu and defines sunnah vs mustahabb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sunnah and mustahabb in Hanafi fiqh and state the ruling for washing hands before wudu after sleep.

Core Idea
Washing hands thrice upon waking is sunnah, not wajib; knowing the difference between sunnah and mustahabb is key to Hanafi legal categories.

This passage defines the sunan of purification and introduces the first sunnah of wudu: washing hands three times before putting them into the water vessel after waking from sleep. It also clarifies the distinction between sunnah (worship-based habitual act) and mustahabb (customary habitual act). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly prioritizing acts in wudu and other worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling category
The act is washing hands before inserting into vessel when waking from sleep. It is classified as sunnah mu'akkadah in Hanafi fiqh, not wajib or fard.
Sunnah mu'akkadah is a stressed sunnah; omission is not sinful but disliked.
2
Distinguish sunnah from mustahabb
The text defines sunnah as an act done consistently as worship, occasionally omitted. Mustahabb is a habitual act (like starting from the right) done consistently but not as worship.
This distinction affects the ranking of legal categories: sunnah > mustahabb.
3
Apply the ruling to a scenario
A person wakes and wants to perform wudu. He should wash his hands thrice before dipping into the water. If omitted, wudu is valid but reward is missed.
The condition is waking from sleep; this ruling does not apply to every wudu.
4
Check cross-madhhab usage
Note that Shafi'is may call both sunnah and mustahabb as 'sunnah'; Hanafis maintain the distinction based on the nature of the Prophet's consistency (worship vs. habit).
This difference can create confusion when reading works from other schools.

Commentary
This passage defines the sunan of wudu (the recommended acts) and provides the first sunnah: washing the hands three times before inserting them into the water vessel when waking from sleep. The text also distinguishes between sunnah (an act performed consistently as worship, sometimes omitted) and mustahabb (habitual acts performed regularly, like starting from the right). This distinction is important in Hanafi fiqh: sunnah mu'akkadah is higher than mustahabb. The ruling here is that washing hands before dipping into water on waking is sunnah, not obligatory. The wisdom is to ensure cleanliness before using the water, especially after sleep when hands may have touched impurities.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): An act consistently performed by the Prophet as worship, occasionally omitted; its performance is rewarded, omission is not sinful.
مستحب (mustahabb): An act the Prophet consistently did out of habit (not worship), like starting from the right; rewarded but not emphasized.

Taharah — Purification

Wiping a Quarter of the Head: Obligation and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Defines al-nasiyah and presents proofs for wiping a quarter as fard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the minimum fard amount of head wiping in wudu, explain the proofs (hadith, qiyas, linguistic), and compare it with the Shafi'i and Maliki positions.

Core Idea
Wiping a quarter of the head is fard; the entire head is sunna.

The Quran commands 'wipe your heads,' but how much is obligatory? The Hanafi school answers: a quarter (the forelock area). This lesson unpacks the proofs from hadith, analogical reasoning, and Arabic grammar, and shows how the Shafi'i and Maliki schools differ. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate ikhtilaf in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State the minimum obligatory amount for wiping the head according to the Hanafi school. Is it a quarter or the whole head?
Also note that wiping the whole head is sunna, not fard.
2
Analyze the primary dalil
Examine the hadith of Mughira ibn Shu'ba. How does it support the quarter? Identify the key action and its implication.
The Prophet wiped only his forelock (nasiyah).
3
Understand the linguistic proof
The particle 'ba' in the verse indicates a part of the head. Explain the grammatical rule and how it leads to a part being sufficient.
When 'ba' enters on a locus, it signifies a part.
4
Trace the qiyas arguments
Two analogies: 'awra exposure and shaving the head in ihram. How does the quarter rule apply there and then analogize to wiping?
A quarter exposure breaks prayer; shaving a quarter requires dam.
5
Compare with opposing schools
State the Shafi'i and Maliki positions and their proofs. Then evaluate the Hanafi response.
Shafi'i: any wiping suffices (absolute). Maliki: entire head must be wiped (based on hadith of full wiping). Hanafi: those hadiths indicate sunna.

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الأوّل
كتاب الطهارة
الناصية وهو ربع الرأس لما روى المغيرة بن شعبة ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم اتي سباطة قوم فبال وتوضأ ومسح على الناصية وخفيه (۵) وسنن الطهارة (٦) غسل اليدين بلکہ مستحب ہے۔ کیونکہ پورے سر کا مسح فرض ہوتا تو صرف پیشانی کی مقدار یا اگلے حصے پر مسح کرنا کافی نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک چوتھائی سر یا پیشانی کی مقدار پر مسح کرنا فرض ہے۔ اور پورے سر پر مسح کرنا سنت ہے۔ (۲) آیت میں سر کا مسح کرنا فرض ہے لیکن کتنی مقدار فرض ہے آیت سے اس کا پتہ نہیں چلتا ہے۔ آیت اس بارے میں مجمل ہے۔ اب حدیث نے اس کی تفسیر کی ہے کہ کم سے کم مقدار پیشانی کے برابر ہے۔ اس سے کم مقدار کا کسی حدیث سے پتا نہیں چلتا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ کم سے کم مقدار فرض ہوگی (۳) ستر عورت چو تھائی کھل جائے تو نماز ٹوٹ جائے گی۔ حج کے موقع پر احرام کی حالت میں چوتھائی سرمنڈوادے تو دم لازم ہوتا ہے۔ جس طرح پورے سر منڈوانے سے دم لازم ہوتا ہے۔ تو ان مقامات پر چوتھائی کل کے قائم مقام ہے اس لئے سر کے مسح میں بھی چوتھائی پورے سر کے قائم مقام ہوگا (۴) قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ ب حرف جر آلہ پر داخل ہو تو اس کا بعض مراد ہوگا اور محل کا کل، اور محل پر داخل ہو تو محل کا بعض مراد ہوگا۔ یہاں بسر محل پر داخل ہے اس لئے سر کا بعض حصہ مراد ہوگا کہ بعض سر کا مسح کرنا کافی ہوگا۔
نا امام شافعی کے نزدیک چند بال کو مسح کرنے سے فرض کی ادائیگی ہو جائے گی۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مسح کرنا مطلق ہے اور مطلق میں دو چار بال مسح کرنا کافی ہو جاتا ہے۔ امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ پورے سر کا مسح کرنا فرض ہے ۔ وہ ان احادیث سے استدلال کرتے ہیں جن میں پورے سر پر مسح کرنا ثابت ہے۔ یہ احادیث بخاری شریف باب مسح الرأس کلہ ص ۳۳ نمبر ۱۸۵ اور باب مسح الرأس مرۃ ص۳۲ نمبر ۱۹۲ پر مذکور ہیں ۔ عن عبد الله بن زيد ... ثم مسح رأسه بيديه فاقبل بهما وادبر بدا بمقدم رأسه حتى ذهب بهما الى قفاه ثم ردهما الى المكان الذى بدا منہ ۔ ہم اس کا جواب دیتے ہیں کہ وہ احادیث سنیت پر محمول ہیں۔ اور ہم بھی ایک مرتبہ پورے سر پر سح ۔ کرنا سنت قرار دیتے ہیں۔ ان الناصیہ : پیشانی یہاں پیشانی کی مقدار مراد ہے کیوں کہ صرف پیشانی پر مسح کرنے سے کسی کے یہاں مسح ادا نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ آیت میں سر پر مسح کرنے کا حکم دیا گیا ہے۔ مغیرہ بن شعبہ مشہور صحابی ہیں غزوہ خندق کے سال اسلام لائے ہیں اور ۵۰ھ یا ا۵ھ میں وفات پائی ہے۔ ان سے ایک سو چھتیں حدیثیں مروی ہیں۔ سباطۃ : کوڑا ، پھر پھینکنے کی جگہ۔ بال : پیشاب کیا۔
The commentary al-Thamiri, first part. Book of Purification. Al-Nasiyah is a quarter of the head because of what Mughira ibn Shu'ba narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) came to a garbage dump of some people, urinated, performed wudu, and wiped over his forelock and khuffs. (5) The sunan of purification (6) Washing the hands is mustahabb. Because if wiping the entire head were fard, then wiping only the amount of the forehead or the front part would not suffice. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, wiping a quarter of the head or the amount of the forehead is fard. Wiping the entire head is sunna. (2) The verse makes wiping the head fard, but the amount is not known from the verse; the verse is mujmal. The hadith explains that the minimum is the extent of the forehead. No hadith indicates less than that. So this minimum is fard. (3) If a quarter of a woman's 'awra is exposed, the prayer is invalidated. During hajj, if one shaves a quarter of the head in ihram, a dam is required, just as shaving the whole head requires a dam. So in these places, a quarter stands for the whole. Therefore, in wiping the head, a quarter also stands for the whole head. (4) The rule is that when the letter 'ba' enters upon an instrument, it indicates a part of it and the whole of the locus; when it enters upon a locus, it indicates a part of the locus. Here 'ba' enters upon 'head' which is a locus, so a part of the head is meant, so wiping a part of the head suffices. Now, according to Imam al-Shafi'i, wiping a few hairs fulfills the obligation. He says that wiping is absolute, and with absoluteness, wiping a few hairs suffices. Imam Malik says wiping the entire head is fard. He argues from hadiths that prove wiping the entire head, such as those in Sahih al-Bukhari (chapter on wiping the whole head, p.33 no.185, and chapter on wiping the head once, p.32 no.192) from Abdullah ibn Zaid: '... then he wiped his head with his hands, bringing them forward and backward, starting from the front of his head until he reached the back, then he returned them to where he started.' We respond that these hadiths are interpreted as sunna. We also consider wiping the entire head once as sunna. An-nasiyah: forehead; here it means the amount of the forehead, because wiping only the forehead does not fulfill the wiping according to anyone, since the verse commands wiping the head. Mughira ibn Shu'ba is a famous companion; he embraced Islam in the year of the Battle of the Trench and died in 50 AH or 51 AH. 136 hadiths are narrated from him. Sabata: a place for garbage and trash. Bal: urinated.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the obligation of wiping the head during wudu. The author begins by defining 'al-nasiyah' as a quarter of the head, citing the hadith of Mughira ibn Shu'ba. The Hanafi position is stated clearly: wiping a quarter of the head is fard (obligatory), while wiping the entire head is sunna. The proof is drawn from the hadith where the Prophet wiped only his forelock (nasiyah), indicating that the minimum obligation is a quarter. The verse (5:6) commands 'wipe your heads' but is mujmal (ambiguous) regarding the extent; the hadith specifies the minimum. Additional qiyas (analogical reasoning) is presented: just as a quarter exposure of 'awra invalidates prayer and shaving a quarter of the head in ihram necessitates a dam, so a quarter stands for the whole in head wiping. Also, a grammatical rule about the particle 'ba' is invoked: when 'ba' enters upon the locus, it signifies a part. Then the author presents the Shafi'i view: wiping any few hairs suffices because the command is absolute. The Maliki view: the entire head must be wiped, based on hadiths showing the Prophet wiping his whole head. The Hanafi response is that those hadiths indicate sunna, not obligation. The passage concludes by emphasizing that the term 'nasiyah' here means the forehead area, not just the forelock. This is a classic example of Hanafi usul: using hadith and qiyas to derive the minimum obligation, and defending it against other schools.

Key Terms
الناصية (an-Nasiyah): The forelock or front part of the head, identified as a quarter of the head.
ربع الرأس (rub' ar-ra's): A quarter of the head, the minimum area for wiping according to Hanafis.
مسح (mash): Wiping, a legal action involving passing a wet hand over a member or object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A quarter of the head
C) Any part of the head
D) Only the forelock

Key Takeaway
Wiping a quarter of the head is fard in the Hanafi school; the entire head is sunna, and this is supported by hadith, qiyas, and linguistic analysis.

The Sunnahs of Wudu: Washing Hands, Basmalah, and Siwak
Enumerates three sunnah acts with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunnah acts of wudu according to the Hanafi school, explain their proofs, and distinguish between sunnah and mustahabb.

Core Idea
Three sunnah acts in wudu: washing hands after sleep, basmalah (mustahabb), and siwak—each backed by hadith.

In this lesson, we explore three recommended acts in wudu that the Prophet consistently performed. Understanding their status as sunnah (or mustahabb) helps us perfect our wudu without confusion. We'll see how the Hanafi school handles the hadith evidence and where intra-madhhab differences exist.

Guided Path
1
Define sunnah and mustahabb
Identify the distinction: sunnah is an act performed consistently as worship with occasional omission; mustahabb is a habitual act not specifically worshipful.
Key example: starting from the right is mustahabb, not sunnah.
2
Identify the first sunnah and its proof
Recognize that washing both hands three times before dipping into the water vessel after sleep is sunnah, supported by the hadith of Abu Huraira.
Even if not asleep, it is still sunnah to wash hands before wudu.
3
Analyze the basmalah ruling
Note the hadith 'لا وضوء لمن لم يذكر اسم الله عليه' and how the Hanafi school interprets it as recommending basmalah (mustahabb), not obligating it.
Ishaq ibn Rahawayh disagrees, considering it wajib; the mufta bihi is mustahabb.
4
Examine the siwak sunnah
The hadith shows the Prophet's eagerness to command siwak at prayer times, implying it is sunnah at wudu for each prayer.
Siwak is considered sunnah muakkadah.
5
Summarize the hanafi positions
Consolidate: washing hands is sunnah, basmalah is mustahabb, siwak is sunnah muakkadah. Note the tarjih in al-Hidayah for basmalah.
All these rulings are from Zahir al-Riwayah.

حدیث میں ہے کہ جس نے بسم اللہ نہیں پڑھی اس کا وضو ہی نہیں ہے۔ ابی سفیان بن حـويـطـب عن جدتة عن ابيها قال سمعت رسول الله الله اليله يقول لا وضوء لمن لـ رء لمن لم يذكر اسم الله عليه (ب) ( ترمذی شریف ، باب فی التسمیۃ عند الوضوء ص۱۳ نمبر ۲۵ را بو داؤد شریف، باب فی التسمیۃ علی الوضوء ، ص ۱۵ نمبر ۱۰۱) حدیث میں یہ ذکر ہے کہ بغیر بسم اللہ کے وضوء ہی نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن یہ فی کمال پر محمول ہے اور حدیث کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بغیر بسم اللہ کے وضوء کامل نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدا یہ فرماتے ہیں بسم اللہ پڑھنا مستحب ہے نانه اسحاق بن راهو یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جان کر بسم اللہ چھوڑ دے تو وضو لوٹائے گا اور بھول کر یا حدیث کی تاویل کرتے ہوئے بسم اللہ چھوڑ دے تو وضو ہو جائیگا ان کی دلیل اوپر والی حدیث ہے۔ (۸) تیسری سنت مسواک کرنا ہے۔
ج (1) حدیث میں ہے عن ابي هريرة رضى الله عنه عن النبى الله الله قال لولا ان اشق على المؤمنين و في حديث زهـيـر عـلـى امتى لامرتهم بالسواك عند كل صلوة (ج) (مسلم شریف ، باب السواک ص ۱۲۸ نمبر ۲۵۲ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی السواک ص ۱۲ نمبر ۲۲ / بخاری شریف ، باب السواک ص ۳۸ نمبر ۲۴۴) اس حدیث سے اگر چہ یہ ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ نماز کے وقت مسواک سنت ہے۔ لیکن یہاں ایک عبارت محذوف ہوگی عند وضوء كل صلوۃ یعنی ہر نماز کے وضو کے وقت مسواک کرنا سنت ہے۔ (۲) عن حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا جب تم میں سے کوئی نیند سے بیدار ہو تو اپنے ہاتھ کو برتن میں نہ ڈالے، یہاں تک کہ اس کو تین مرتبہ نہ دھو لے۔ (ب) اس کا وضوء کامل نہیں جس نے بسم اللہ نہیں پڑھی۔ (ج) آپ نے فرمایا میری امت پر مشقت کا خوف نہ ہوتا تو ہر نماز کے وقت مسواک کا حکم دیتا۔
Statement of the sunan of wudu. (5) Sunan al-taharah: The sunan of purification. A path or way is called sunna. In the Shariah, an act that the Prophet (peace be upon him) consistently performed as an act of worship and occasionally omitted is called sunna. If he consistently did something out of habit, not as worship, it is mustahabb, like starting good deeds from the right side. (1) The sunan of wudu: Washing both hands three times before inserting them into the vessel, when the person performing wudu has woken from sleep. If a person wakes from sleep and wishes to perform wudu or ghusl, he should wash his hands three times before putting them into the water vessel. This is sunna. Because it is possible that during sleep his hand touched an impure place and there is impurity on the hand without his knowledge. If he then dips his hand into the water, the water becomes impure. Therefore, he should wash his hands three times before putting them in the vessel. If there is a strong presumption that the hand is impure, washing is necessary; if only doubt, washing is sunna. The proof that this is sunna is the hadith of Abu Huraira (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When one of you wakes from sleep, do not dip his hand into the vessel until he washes it three times, for he does not know where his hand spent the night.' (Muslim, Bab Karahiyat ghams al-mutawaddi'...). The author wrote that washing hands after waking from sleep is sunna. Scholars have written that even if not waking from sleep, it is sunna for the one performing wudu to wash his hands. Al-ina': vessel, istaqadha: woke up, nawm: sleep. (7) The second sunna: Reciting 'Bismillah' at the beginning of wudu. The hadith states: 'There is no wudu for the one who does not mention the name of Allah upon it.' (Tirmidhi, Bab al-tasmiya 'ind al-wudu', and Abu Dawud). This hadith mentions that without Bismillah, wudu is not valid. But this is interpreted as 'complete', meaning that without Bismillah, wudu is not complete. The author of al-Hidayah says that reciting Bismillah is mustahabb. Ishaq ibn Rahawayh says that if one deliberately abandons Bismillah, he must repeat wudu; if forgetful or interpreting the hadith, his wudu is valid. (8) The third sunna is using the siwak. The hadith: 'If I did not fear hardship for my ummah (or in another version: for my community), I would have ordered siwak with every prayer.' (Muslim, Tirmidhi, Bukhari). This hadith proves that siwak at prayer time is sunna. But here an omitted phrase would be 'at the wudu of every prayer', i.e., using siwak at the time of wudu for every prayer is sunna. Footnotes: (a) He said: When one of you wakes from sleep, do not dip his hand into the vessel until he washes it three times. (b) His wudu is not complete if he does not say Bismillah. (c) He said: If I did not fear hardship for my ummah, I would have ordered siwak at every prayer.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof enumerating three sunnah acts of wudu. The author first defines sunnah and mustahabb: sunnah is an act performed consistently as worship with occasional omission; mustahabb is a habitual act. Then he lists three sunan: (1) washing both hands three times before dipping them into the water vessel when waking from sleep. The wisdom is to avoid contaminating the water if the hand inadvertently touched impurity during sleep. The proof is the hadith of Abu Huraira. The author notes that even if one did not sleep, it is still sunnah to wash hands before wudu. (2) Reciting Bismillah at the start of wudu. The hadith 'لا وضوء لمن لم يذكر اسم الله عليه' is interpreted to mean that wudu is not complete without it, not that it is invalid. The Hanafi position, as per al-Hidayah, is that it is mustahabb. Ishaq ibn Rahawayh holds it is wajib. (3) Using the siwak (toothstick) during wudu. The hadith shows it is sunnah at prayer times, and by implication, at wudu for each prayer. This passage illustrates how the Hanafi school derives sunnah from hadith and distinguishes between fard, wajib, sunnah, and mustahabb.

Key Terms
سنت (sunnah): An act performed consistently by the Prophet as worship, occasionally omitted, not obligatory.
مستحب (mustahabb): An act performed habitually by the Prophet, not as worship, such as starting from the right.
بسم الله (basmalah): The phrase 'In the name of Allah' recited at the start of wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, what is the ruling on reciting Bismillah at the beginning of wudu?
A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah)
C) Mustahabb (recommended)
D) Fard (obligatory)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers washing hands after sleep, basmalah (mustahabb), and siwak as recommended acts in wudu, with clear hadith evidence.

Washing Hands Before Dipping into Water After Waking from Sleep
Ruling with proof on washing hands after waking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing hands upon waking from sleep (sunnah) and explain when it becomes wajib due to ghalib al-zann.

Core Idea
Washing hands three times upon waking is sunnah; it becomes wajib only if there is a strong presumption of impurity.

This passage addresses a common situation: you wake up from sleep and want to perform wudu. Should you wash your hands before dipping them into the water vessel? The answer depends on the level of certainty about impurity on your hands. In this lesson, we examine the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Washing hands three times before inserting them into the water vessel after waking from sleep. What is the default ruling? Sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Abu Hurairah (RA) in Muslim and Tirmidhi: 'When one of you wakes from his sleep, do not dip his hand into the vessel until he washes it three times, for he does not know where his hand spent the night.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith contains both a prohibition (do not dip) and a command (wash). Hanafi usul interprets a prohibition as indicating karahah (dislike) not tahrim (prohibition), and a command as sunnah not wajib, especially when there is other evidence that the act is not obligatory.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., Zahiris) consider washing wajib due to the apparent command. The Hanafi school holds it is sunnah, as supported by other ahadith showing permissibility of dipping without prior washing.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is sunnah; however, if there is a strong presumption (ghalib al-zann) that the hand is impure, washing becomes wajib because the harm of contaminating the water is certain.

سنت ہے۔ کیونکہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ نیند کی حالت میں اس کا ہاتھ نجاست کی جگہ پر گیا ہو اور ہاتھ پر نا پا کی موجود ہو اور وضو کرنے والے کو اسکا پتہ نہ ہو ۔ اب اس ہاتھ کو پانی میں ڈالے گا تو پانی ناپاک ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے برتن میں ہاتھ ڈالنے سے پہلے ہاتھ کو تین مرتبہ دھو لے۔ اگر ہاتھ پر ناپا کی ہونے کا ظن غالب ہو تو دھونا ضروری ہے۔اور صرف شک ہوتو دھونا سنت ہے۔
ے اس کے سنت ہونے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابي هريرة رضى الله عنه ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال اذا استيقظ احدكم من نومه فلا تغمس يده في الاناء حتى يغسلها ثلاثا فانه لايدری این باتت يده (الف) ( مسلم شریف، باب کراہیتہ شمس المتوضی و غیرہ ید و المشکوک فی نجاستھانی الاناء قبل غسلها ثلا خاص ۱۳۶ نمبر ۲۷۸ / ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء اذا استيقظ احدکم من منامه فلا تنمسن يده في الا ناراحتی تغسلها ملا خاص ۱۳ نمبر ۲۴) مصنف نے نیند سے بیدار ہونے کے بعد ہاتھ دھونا سنت لکھا ہے۔ علماء نے لکھا ہے کہ نیند سے بیدار نہ ہو تب بھی وضو کر نے والے کے لئے ہاتھ دھونا سنت ہے ۔
الاناء : برتن، استيقظ : بیدار ہوا، نوم : نیند
Three times before inserting them into the vessel when the one performing wudu wakes from his sleep (7). It is sunnah because it is possible that during sleep his hand went to a place of impurity and there is impurity on his hand, and the person performing wudu is unaware of it. So when he inserts his hand into the water, the water becomes impure. Therefore, before inserting his hand into the vessel, he should wash his hand three times. If there is a strong presumption (ghalib al-zann) of impurity, washing is necessary; if mere doubt, washing is sunnah. The proof of its being sunnah is this hadith: From Abu Hurairah (RA) that the Prophet (SAW) said: 'When one of you wakes from his sleep, do not dip his hand into the vessel until he washes it three times, for he does not know where his hand spent the night.' (Muslim, Tirmidhi) The author (of the matn) wrote that washing hands after waking from sleep is sunnah. Scholars have written that even if one does not wake from sleep, it is sunnah for the one performing wudu to wash his hands. Al-ina': vessel; istayqaza: woke up; nawm: sleep.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage contains the first sunnah of wudu mentioned by the author: washing the hands three times before inserting them into the water vessel after waking from sleep. The commentator (sharh) explains the rationale: during sleep, one's hand may have touched an impurity without one's knowledge. If the hand is dipped into water, the water becomes impure, thus invalidating the wudu. The ruling varies based on certainty: if there is a strong presumption (ghalib al-zann) that the hand is impure, washing is wajib; if only doubt (shakk), it is sunnah. The primary proof is the hadith of Abu Hurairah (RA) recorded by Muslim and Tirmidhi, which commands washing the hand three times upon waking. The commentator notes that the matn explicitly states this is sunnah only after waking, but many scholars extend it to all cases of wudu, making it sunnah generally. The passage ends with a brief glossary of key terms.

Key Terms
ظن غالب (ghalib al-zann): A strong presumption that something is the case, based on prevalent evidence
سنت (sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed without making it obligatory
الاناء (al-ina'): The vessel or container holding water for wudu

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Wajib
B) Sunnah
C) Haram
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Washing hands three times after waking is sunnah; it rises to wajib only with a strong presumption of impurity (ghalib al-zann).

The Ruling of Saying Bismillah at the Start of Wudu
Ruling and proof for tasmiyah in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tasmiyah in wudu, explain the interpretation of the hadith as referring to completeness (kamal), and distinguish the Hanafi position from the view of Ishaq ibn Rahawayh.

Core Idea
Saying Bismillah at the start of wudu is sunnah, not wajib; the hadith refers to completeness, not validity.

The hadith 'There is no wudu for the one who does not mention Allah's name' seems to make tasmiyah compulsory. However, the Hanafi school interprets this as indicating perfect wudu, not its essential validity. This lesson unpacks the evidence and reasoning behind the Hanafi stance, and contrasts it with an opposing view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is saying 'Bismillah' at the beginning of wudu. According to the Hanafi school, its ruling is sunnah (mustahabb), not wajib.
The text states it is the second sunnah of wudu.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'لا وضوء لمن لم يذكر اسم الله عليه' (There is no wudu for the one who does not mention the name of Allah upon it).
This is a hadith ahad (single-narrator), so its thubut is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'لا وضوء' literally negates wudu. However, Hanafis interpret 'wudu' here as 'wudu kamal' (complete wudu) because the Prophet (SAW) himself performed wudu without saying Bismillah on some occasions. Thus the negation is not of validity but of perfection.
This interpretation (haml ala al-kamal) is a known Hanafi usul tool.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Ishaq ibn Rahawayh held that deliberately omitting tasmiyah invalidates wudu (wajib), while omission due to forgetfulness or ta'wil does not. His proof is the same hadith, interpreted literally.
The Hanafi school disagrees entirely; even deliberate omission does not affect validity.
5
Conclude with mufta bihi
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that tasmiyah is sunnah; wudu performed without it is valid but incomplete. Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah explicitly states it is mustahabb.
This is the standard position of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).

(۷) دوسری سنت ] وضوء کے شروع میں بسم اللہ پڑھنا۔
حدیث میں ہے کہ جس نے بسم اللہ نہیں پڑھی اس کا وضو ہی نہیں ہے۔ ابی سفیان بن حـويـطـب عن جدتة عن ابيها قال سمعت رسول الله الله اليله يقول لا وضوء لمن لـ رء لمن لم يذكر اسم الله عليه (ب) ( ترمذی شریف ، باب فی التسمیۃ عند الوضوء ص۱۳ نمبر ۲۵ را بو داؤد شریف، باب فی التسمیۃ علی الوضوء ، ص ۱۵ نمبر ۱۰۱) حدیث میں یہ ذکر ہے کہ بغیر بسم اللہ کے وضوء ہی نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن یہ فی کمال پر محمول ہے اور حدیث کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بغیر بسم اللہ کے وضوء کامل نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدا یہ فرماتے ہیں بسم اللہ پڑھنا مستحب ہے نانه اسحاق بن راهو یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جان کر بسم اللہ چھوڑ دے تو وضو لوٹائے گا اور بھول کر یا حدیث کی تاویل کرتے ہوئے بسم اللہ چھوڑ دے تو وضو ہو جائیگا ان کی دلیل اوپر والی حدیث ہے۔
(7) The second sunnah: Reciting 'Bismillah' at the beginning of wudu. It is mentioned in a hadith that the one who does not recite 'Bismillah' has no wudu. From Abu Sufyan bin Huwaitib from his grandmother from her father: I heard the Messenger of Allah (SAW) say: 'There is no wudu for the one who does not mention the name of Allah upon it.' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud) The hadith mentions that without 'Bismillah' there is no wudu. But this is interpreted as referring to complete perfection; the meaning is that without 'Bismillah' the wudu is not complete. The author of al-Hidayah states that reciting 'Bismillah' is mustahabb. Ishaq ibn Rahawayh holds that if one intentionally leaves it, he should repeat the wudu, but if he forgets or leaves it due to interpretation (ta'wil) of the hadith, the wudu is valid. His proof is the aforementioned hadith.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage discusses the second sunnah of wudu: saying 'Bismillah' at its beginning. The commentator cites a hadith that appears to make wudu conditional upon mentioning Allah's name. However, the Hanafi school interprets this as indicating completeness (kamal), not validity. Thus saying Bismillah is sunnah, not wajib. The author of al-Hidayah considers it mustahabb (recommended). There is a differing view from Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, who considers it wajib to the extent that intentional omission requires repeating wudu, but omission due to forgetfulness or a legitimate interpretation of the hadith does not invalidate wudu. The Hanafi position aligns with the majority, treating it as sunnah.

Key Terms
تسمية (tasmiyah): The act of saying 'Bismillah' at the start of an action
مستحب (mustahabb): A recommended act, slightly less emphasized than sunnah
في كمال (fi kamal): Regarding perfection or completeness; a qualifying interpretation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, if someone deliberately omits saying 'Bismillah' at the start of wudu, what is the status of his wudu?
A) Invalid (batil)
B) Valid but incomplete (naqis)
C) Must be repeated (i'ada)
D) Nullified by sin

Key Takeaway
Saying Bismillah at the start of wudu is a sunnah that enhances reward, but it is not required for the validity of wudu.

The Siwak: Sunnah of Wudu or Salah?
Inter-madhhab dispute on siwak timing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the timing of siwak and explain the hermeneutical argument (mahdhuf) used to reconcile conflicting hadiths.

Core Idea
Siwak is sunnah of wudu, not salah, by harmonizing explicit hadiths.

This lesson resolves a classic inter-madhhab dispute: when exactly is the siwak recommended? The Hanafi school holds it is a sunnah of wudu, while the Shafi'i school considers it a sunnah of salah. The key is understanding how the Hanafis interpret the phrase 'at every prayer' as implying 'at the wudu for every prayer'—an omitted expression (mahdhuf) that aligns with the explicit hadith 'with every wudu'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State clearly: siwak is a sunnah muakkadah performed during wudu, not during the salah itself.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
The primary proof is the hadith from Abu Hurairah (RA): 'If I did not fear hardship for my ummah, I would have commanded them to use siwak with every wudu.' (Baihaqi). Also interpret the 'at every prayer' hadith accordingly.
Hadith 1: explicit wudu. Hadith 2: 'at every prayer' is interpreted as 'at the wudu of every prayer'.
3
Understand the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i takes the literal wording of the widely transmitted hadith 'at every prayer' (Muslim, Bukhari) and considers siwak a sunnah of salah itself.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that the 'at every prayer' hadith contains an omitted word (mahdhuf): 'wudu'. This is supported by the explicit Baihaqi hadith and by the logical purpose of siwak (oral hygiene), which is more connected to wudu than to prayer.
This is an expansion-based hermeneutical move.
5
Derive the practical consequence (thamarah)
Hanafi: one should use siwak while performing wudu. Shafi'i: one should use siwak before salah even if wudu was done earlier. The mufta bihi in Hanafi school is siwak during wudu.

Source Text

(۸) تیسری سنت مسواک کرنا ہے۔
حدیث میں ہے عن ابي هريرة رضى الله عنه عن النبى الله الله قال لولا ان اشق على المؤمنين و في حديث زهـيـر عـلـى امتى لامرتهم بالسواك عند كل صلوة (ج) (مسلم شریف ، باب السواک ص ۱۲۸ نمبر ۲۵۲ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی السواک ص ۱۲ نمبر ۲۲ / بخاری شریف ، باب السواک ص ۳۸ نمبر ۲۴۴) اس حدیث سے اگر چہ یہ ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ نماز کے وقت مسواک سنت ہے۔ لیکن یہاں ایک عبارت محذوف ہوگی عند وضوء كل صلوۃ یعنی ہر نماز کے وضو کے وقت مسواک کرنا سنت ہے۔
(۲) عن حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا جب تم میں سے کوئی نیند سے بیدار ہو تو اپنے ہاتھ کو برتن میں نہ ڈالے، یہاں تک کہ اس کو تین مرتبہ نہ دھو لے۔ (ب) اس کا وضوء کامل نہیں جس نے بسم اللہ نہیں پڑھی۔ (ج) آپ نے فرمایا میری امت پر مشقت کا خوف نہ ہوتا تو ہر نماز کے وقت مسواک کا حکم دیتا۔

ابي هريرة رضي الله عنه قال قال رسول الله الله الله لولا ان اشق على امتى لامرتهم بالسواك مع كل وضوء (سنن للبیھقی ، باب الدلیل علی ان السواک یہ لیس بواجب ، جلد اول ص ۵۷ نمبر ۱۴۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مسواک وضو کے وقت سنت ہے (۳) مسواک کا مقصد منہ کی گندگی صاف کرنا ہے اس لئے وہ وضو کے زیادہ مناسب ہے
اول)
امام شافعی کے نزدیک مسواک سنت نماز ہے۔ ان کی دلیل اوپر کی حدیث عند کل صلوۃ ہے (موسوعہ امام شافعی باب السواک ص ۱۰۲ ج
(8) The third sunnah: Siwak. A hadith from Abu Hurairah (RA) from the Prophet (SAW): 'If I did not fear difficulty for the believers (or for my ummah), I would have commanded them to use siwak at every prayer.' (Muslim, Tirmidhi, Bukhari) From this hadith it is established that siwak at the time of prayer is sunnah. But here an expression is omitted: 'at the wudu of every prayer', meaning it is sunnah to use siwak at the wudu of every prayer. (2) From the hashia: (a) He (SAW) said: 'When one of you wakes from sleep, do not dip his hand into the vessel until he washes it three times.' (b) 'He has no complete wudu who does not mention the name of Allah.' (c) 'If I did not fear hardship for my ummah, I would have commanded them to use siwak at every prayer.' Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part One (9) 'Al-Madmadah wa al-Istinshaq'. Page 36. Book of Purification. From Abu Hurairah (RA) that the Prophet (SAW) said: 'If I did not fear hardship for my ummah, I would have commanded them to use siwak with every wudu.' (Baihaqi) This hadith shows that siwak is sunnah at the time of wudu. The purpose of siwak is to clean the mouth, so it is more appropriate for wudu. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that siwak is sunnah for prayer (sunnat al-salat). His proof is the aforementioned hadith 'at every prayer' (Mawsu'ah al-Imam al-Shafi'i, Bab al-Siwak, p. 102).
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage covers the third sunnah of wudu: using a siwak (toothstick). The commentator cites two hadiths: one mentioning 'at every prayer' and another explicitly stating 'with every wudu'. The Hanafi position is that the siwak is sunnah during wudu, not during the prayer itself. They reconcile the 'at every prayer' hadith by interpreting it as meaning 'at the wudu for every prayer', since wudu precedes prayer. The purpose of siwak is oral hygiene, which aligns well with wudu. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, considering siwak to be a sunnah of prayer (sunnat al-salat), based on the literal wording of the hadith 'at every prayer'. The Hanafi response is that the omitted context ('wudu') is understood, and the hadith with explicit mention of wudu (from Baihaqi) supports this. Thus, the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that siwak is sunnah during wudu.

Key Terms
سواك (siwak): A tooth-cleaning stick, typically from the arak tree, used for oral hygiene
محذوف (mahdhuf): Something omitted in the wording but understood from context

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this text, when is the siwak specifically recommended?
A) During the prayer itself
B) While performing wudu
C) After waking from sleep
D) Upon entering the mosque

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that siwak is a sunnah of wudu, not salah, by interpreting the 'at every prayer' hadith as implicitly referring to wudu.

Rinsing Mouth and Sniffing Water Into Nose
Ruling on madmadah and istinshaq with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on madmadah and istinshaq in wudu, identify the proofs from the Sunnah, and explain the dispute with the Shafi'i and Maliki schools.

Core Idea
Madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah, performed separately with separate handfuls for hygiene.

This passage presents the Hanafi view on rinsing the mouth (madmadah) and sniffing water (istinshaq) during wudu. While the Maliki school considers them obligatory, and the Shafi'i school allows a combined handful, the Hanafi school holds them as sunnah, performed three times each with separate water. The proofs from hadith and the principle of hygiene are examined.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling (sunnah) and the method (three separate handfuls for each).
Reference: 'حنفیہ کے نزدیک تین مرتبہ پانی لیکر کلی کرنا سنت ہے'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that both actions can be done from the same handful three times. Also note the Maliki view that they are fard.
Shafi'i proof: 'فمضمض واستنشق من كف واحد'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Examine the hadith of Uthman (separate actions) and the hadith of Talha (explicit separation). Note the strength of these ahadith.
Abu Dawud dedicated a chapter 'يفصل بين المضمضة والاستنشاق'.
4
Follow the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school acknowledges the Shafi'i hadith but prefers the separate method due to hygiene and explicit textual evidence.
Commentator: 'الگ الگ پانی ڈالنے میں زیادہ نظافت ہے'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi uses separate water for each; Shafi'i uses one handful combined; Maliki requires repetition if omitted.
This affects the actual performance but not the validity of wudu in Hanafi.

Source Text

المضمضة : مضمضہ کرنا کلی کرنا الاستنشاق : باب استفعال سے ناک میں پانی چڑھانا، دوسرا لفظ آتا ہے استنثر : ناک سے پانی جھاڑنا
ا امام مالک کے نزدیک یہ دونوں وضو میں بھی فرض ہیں۔
حاشیہ : (الف) میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم پر داخل ہوا ، وہ وضو فرمارہے تھے اور پانی آپ کے چہرے اور ڈاڑھی پر اور سینہ مبارک پر بہہ رہا تھا۔ اور میں نے دیکھا کہ مضمضہ اور استنشاق میں فصل کر رہے ہیں۔
(9) Al-Madmadah wa al-Istinshaq. Page 36. Book of Purification. The fourth sunnah: rinsing the mouth. The fifth sunnah: putting water into the nose. A hadith: 'I saw Uthman ibn Affan (RA) asked about wudu; he called for water, brought a vessel, tipped it onto his right hand, then inserted it into water, then rinsed his mouth three times and sniffed water and expelled it three times.' (Abu Dawud, Muslim) This is the third hadith in this chapter. In this chapter, he rinsed his mouth three times with separate water, and sniffed water three times with separate water. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, it is sunnah to rinse the mouth three times with three separate handfuls. Also from Talha from his father from his grandfather: 'I entered upon the Prophet (SAW) while he was performing wudu, and water was flowing from his face, beard, and chest, and I saw him separating between madmadah and istinshaq.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on the separation between madmadah and istinshaq) Abu Dawud specifically titled a chapter that the Prophet (SAW) performed them separately. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that one should take one handful of water, use half for rinsing and half for sniffing, then again, then again, thus doing both actions with three handfuls. His proof is the hadith: 'He rinsed his mouth and sniffed water from one handful and did that three times.' (Muslim, Tirmidhi) In that hadith, rinsing and sniffing are mentioned from one handful. We (Hanafis) say that there are also hadiths with separation, and using separate water is more hygienic. Al-madmadah: rinsing the mouth. Al-istinshaq: from the form ifti'al, putting water into the nose. Another word is istinthar: expelling water from the nose. Imam Malik considers both of these actions to be obligatory (fard) in wudu. Hashiya: (a) 'I entered upon the Prophet (SAW) while he was performing wudu, water was flowing from his face, beard, and chest, and I saw him separating between madmadah and istinshaq.'
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage covers the fourth and fifth sunnahs of wudu: rinsing the mouth (madmadah) and sniffing water into the nose (istinshaq). The Hanafi position is that these are sunnah, performed three times each with separate handfuls of water. The primary proof is the action of Uthman (RA) as recorded by Abu Dawud and Muslim, showing separate rinsing and sniffing. Additionally, the hadith from Abu Dawud explicitly states that the Prophet (SAW) separated between them. The commentator then addresses the Shafi'i view: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that both actions should be done from the same handful three times, basing this on a hadith where the Prophet did them from one hand. The Hanafi response is that there are authentic hadiths for both methods, but the separate method is more hygienic (نظافت) and thus preferred. The text also notes that Imam Malik considers both to be fard (obligatory) in wudu, a stricter view. The Hanafi school firmly holds them as sunnah, not fard. The passage ends with a hadith reinforcing the separation between the actions.

Key Terms
مضمضة (madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water, swirling it around and then spitting it out
استنشاق (istinshaq): Sniffing water into the nose, then expelling it
استنثار (istinthar): Expelling water from the nose after istinshaq

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as described in this passage, how should madmadah (rinsing mouth) and istinshaq (sniffing water) be performed in wudu?
A) Both done three times with the same handful of water
B) Both done separately, each with its own three handfuls
C) Both done once with a single handful
D) Madmadah done three times, istinshaq once

Key Takeaway
Madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah acts in Hanafi wudu, performed separately with separate handfuls, supported by hadith of Uthman and Talha and the principle of hygiene.

Madmadah and Istinshaq: The Hanafi Sunnah Ruling in Wudu
Sets the Hanafi ruling with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on madmadah and istinshaq in wudu and explain why they are sunnah muakkadah, not fard.

Core Idea
Madmadah and istinshaq are confirmed sunnah, not fard, performed three times with separate water.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on two acts of wudu: rinsing the mouth (madmadah) and snuffing water into the nose (istinshaq). The source passage presents clear hadith evidence that these acts are sunnah muakkadah, not obligatory, and that they should be performed with separate water for each act. We will walk through the proof and understand why the Hanafi school maintains this view against other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their ruling
The passage identifies madmadah and istinshaq as the fourth and fifth sunnah of wudu. Determine the hukm level: sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
Sunnah muakkadah means the Prophet consistently performed it and encouraged it, but it is not fard.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
The author cites the hadith of Uthman ibn Affan demonstrating the Prophet performing madmadah three times and istinshaq three times with separate water. This is the primary proof.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud and Muslim, indicating its authenticity.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit action of the Prophet shows the method (separate water, three times). Since he consistently did it, it becomes sunnah muakkadah.
The proof does not reach the level of wujub because it is a single action (zanni al-thubut) with no commanding imperative.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage mentions that Imam al-Shafi'i allows combining madmadah and istinshaq in one handful, and Imam Malik considers both fard. This frames the Hanafi position as one of several valid views.
The Hanafi response prefers separation for hygiene and consistency with multiple narrations.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The Hanafi fatwa follows the sunnah muakkadah position with separate water, as it is more precautionary and supported by explicit practice.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, the core Hanafi texts.

(۹) چوتھی سنت کلی کرنا [ پانچویں سنت] ناک میں پانی ڈالنا۔
حدیث میں ہے رأیت عثمان بن عفان سئل عن الوضوء فدعا بماء فاتى بميضأة فاصغاها على يده اليمنى ثم ادخلها في الماء فتمضمض ثلثا و استنثر ثلثا (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب صفته وضوء النبی ص ۶ نمبر ۱۱۳/۱۰۸ر مسلم شریف باب آخر فی صفة الوضوء ص ۱۲۳ نمبر ۲۲۶) اس باب کی یہ تیسری حدیث ہے۔ اس باب میں تین مرتبہ کلی الگ پانی سے کی ہے۔ اور تین مرتبہ ناک میں پانی الگ پانی لیکر ڈالا ہے۔ اس لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک تین مرتبہ پانی لیکر کلی کرنا سنت ہے۔ (۲) عسن طلحة عن ابيه عن جده قال دخلت يعني على النبي الله وهو يتوضأ والماء يسيل من وجهه ولحيته وعلى صدره فرأيته يفصل بين المضمضة والاستنشاق (الف) (ابوداؤد، باب فی الفرق بین المضمضة والاستنشاق ص ۲۰ نمبر ۱۳۹) ابوداؤد نے باضابطہ باب باندھا ہے کہ کلی اور ناک میں پانی ڈالنا آپ نے الگ الگ فرمایا ہے۔ نانه امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک چلو پانی لے اور اس کے آدھے سے کلی کرے اور آدھے کو ناک میں ڈالے پھر دوسری مرتبہ چلو میں پانی لے اور آدھے سے کلی کرے اور آدھے کو ناک میں ڈالے ، پھر تیسری مرتبہ چلو میں پانی لے اور آدھے سے کلی کرے اور آدھے کو ناک میں ڈالے۔ اس طرح تین ہی چلو سے دونوں کام کرے۔ ان کا استدلال ان احادیث سے ہے جس میں ہے۔ به فمضمض واستنشق من كف واحد فعل ذلک ثلاثا ( مسلم شریف ، باب آخر فی صفۃ الوضوء ص ۱۲۳ نمبر ۲۳۵ / ترندی شریف ، باب المضمضة والاستنشاق من کف واحد، ص ۱۴ نمبر (۲۸) اس حدیث میں ایک ہی پانی سے کلی اور ناک
میں پانی ڈالنے کا ذکر ہے۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ حدیث کی اوپر کی بھی ہے۔ اور الگ الگ پانی ڈالنے میں زیادہ نظافت ہے۔ المضمضة : مضمضہ کرنا کلی کرنا الاستنشاق : باب استفعال سے ناک میں پانی چڑھانا، دوسرا لفظ آتا ہے استنثر : ناک سے پانی

ا امام مالک کے نزدیک یہ دونوں وضو میں بھی فرض ہیں۔
حاشیہ : (الف) میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم پر داخل ہوا ، وہ وضو فرمارہے تھے اور پانی آپ کے چہرے اور ڈاڑھی پر اور سینہ مبارک پر بہہ رہا تھا۔ اور میں نے دیکھا کہ مضمضہ اور
استنشاق میں فصل کر رہے ہیں۔
(9) The fourth sunnah is rinsing the mouth, and the fifth sunnah is snuffing water into the nose.
In a hadith: 'I saw Uthman ibn Affan – he was asked about wudu – he called for water, and a small vessel was brought. He tilted it onto his right hand, then put it into the water, rinsed his mouth three times, and expelled water from his nose three times.' (Abu Dawud, Bab Sifat Wudu' al-Nabi, p. 6, no. 113/108; Muslim, Bab Akhir fi Sifat al-Wudu', p. 123, no. 226) This is the third hadith in this chapter. In this chapter, he rinsed his mouth three times with separate water, and snuffed water into his nose three times with separate water. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, it is sunnah to rinse three times with water. (2) From Talhah from his father from his grandfather, he said: 'I entered upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, while he was performing wudu, and water was flowing from his face, his beard, and his chest, and I saw him separating between rinsing the mouth and snuffing water into the nose.' (a) (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Farq bayn al-Madmadah wa al-Istinshaq, p. 20, no. 139) Abu Dawud dedicated a chapter that the Prophet, peace be upon him, did rinsing and snuffing separately. But Imam al-Shafi'i says: take one handful of water, use half for rinsing and half for snuffing, then a second handful, then a third, thus doing both acts with only three handfuls. His evidence is hadith: 'He rinsed his mouth and snuffed water from one handful, doing that three times.' (Muslim, Bab Akhir fi Sifat al-Wudu', p. 123, no. 235; Tirmidhi, Bab al-Madmadah wa al-Istinshaq min Kaffin Wahid, p. 14, no. 28) This hadith mentions rinsing and snuffing from one water. We say that there is also the above hadith, and using separate water is more hygienic. al-Madmadah: rinsing the mouth. al-Istinshaq: from the form istaf'ala, means drawing water into the nose. Another word is istinthar: expelling water from the nose.
And Imam Malik considers both obligatory in wudu.
Footnote (a): 'I entered upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, while he was performing wudu, and water was flowing from his face, beard, and chest, and I saw him separating between rinsing and snuffing.'
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof statement establishing two sunan of wudu: madmadah (rinsing the mouth) and istinshaq (snuffing water into the nose). The author presents a hadith from Uthman ibn Affan showing the Prophet performed each three times with separate water, and then a hadith from Talhah showing separation between the acts. This forms the Hanafi proof that these acts are sunnah, not fard. The author then contrasts with Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues from another hadith that one handful suffices for both acts, and with Imam Malik, who considers them fard. The Hanafi response emphasizes that separate water is more hygienic and is supported by explicit practice. The commentary also clarifies the Arabic terminology: madmadah for rinsing, istinshaq for drawing water into the nose, and istinthar for expelling it.

Key Terms
المضمضة (al-madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water during wudu
الاستنشاق (al-istinshaq): Drawing water into the nose during wudu
الاستنثار (al-istinthar): Expelling water from the nose after istinshaq

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the hukm level of madmadah and istinshaq in wudu?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah muakkadah
D) Mustahabb

Key Takeaway
Madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah muakkadah in Hanafi wudu, performed three times with separate water; omitting them does not invalidate wudu.

Inter-Madhhab Dispute on Madmadah and Istinshaq
Analyzes the inter-madhhab dispute with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the inter-madhhab dispute on madmadah and istinshaq, state each school's evidence, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Hanafis separate water for rinsing and snuffing; Shafi'is combine; Malikis consider them fard.

This lesson examines the scholarly disagreement regarding the method and status of madmadah and istinshaq in wudu. The Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Maliki schools each draw from different hadith evidence, leading to distinct rulings. Understanding this dispute strengthens one's ability to evaluate proofs and appreciate legitimate ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school holds madmadah and istinshaq as sunnah muakkadah, performed three times with separate water. Proofs: hadith of Uthman (three separate rinses and snuffs) and hadith of Talhah (explicit separation).
The Hanafi position emphasizes the explicit separation action.
2
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds both acts as sunnah but allows combining them in one handful, using a hadith where the Prophet rinsed and snuffed from one handful three times.
The Shafi'i proof is based on a different narration.
3
State the Maliki position
Imam Malik considers madmadah and istinshaq as fard in wudu, meaning wudu is invalid without them.
The Maliki view is the strongest obligation among the three.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to Shafi'i
The Hanafi response acknowledges both hadith but prefers the separation because it is more hygienic and supported by an explicit chapter heading in Abu Dawud dedicated to separation.
The Hanafi tarjih is based on precaution (ihtiyat) and consistency.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi wudu uses 6 handfuls (3 for madmadah, 3 for istinshaq); Shafi'i uses 3 handfuls for both combined. For Maliki, omitting either act invalidates wudu; for Hanafi, it does not.
This affects daily practice and water usage.

Source Text

(9) The fourth sunnah is rinsing the mouth, and the fifth sunnah is snuffing water into the nose.

He tilted it onto his right hand, then put it into the water, rinsed his mouth three times, and expelled water from his nose three times.' (Abu Dawud, Bab Sifat Wudu' al-Nabi, p. 6, no. 113/108; Muslim, Bab Akhir fi Sifat al-Wudu', p. 123, no. 226) This is the third hadith in this chapter. In this chapter, he rinsed his mouth three times with separate water, and snuffed water into his nose three times with separate water. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, it is sunnah to rinse three times with water. (2) From Talhah from his father from his grandfather, he said: 'I entered upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, while he was performing wudu, and water was flowing from his face, his beard, and his chest, and I saw him separating between rinsing the mouth and snuffing water into the nose.' (a) (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Farq bayn al-Madmadah wa al-Istinshaq, p. 20, no. 139) Abu Dawud dedicated a chapter that the Prophet, peace be upon him, did rinsing and snuffing separately. But Imam al-Shafi'i says: take one handful of water, use half for rinsing and half for snuffing, then a second handful, then a third, thus doing both acts with only three handfuls. His evidence is hadith: 'He rinsed his mouth and snuffed water from one handful, doing that three times.' (Muslim, Bab Akhir fi Sifat al-Wudu', p. 123, no. 235; Tirmidhi, Bab al-Madmadah wa al-Istinshaq min Kaffin Wahid, p. 14, no. 28) This hadith mentions rinsing and snuffing from one water. We say that there is also the above hadith, and using separate water is more hygienic. al-Madmadah: rinsing the mouth. al-Istinshaq: from the form istaf'ala, means drawing water into the nose. Another word is istinthar: expelling water from the nose.
And Imam Malik considers both obligatory in wudu.
Footnote (a): 'I entered upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, while he was performing wudu, and water was flowing from his face, beard, and chest, and I saw him separating between rinsing and snuffing.'

Wiping the Ears: Sunnah or Sunnah with New Water?
Establishes wiping ears as sunnah in wudu with dispute on whether to use new water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on wiping the ears in wudu and explain why new water is not required, citing the primary evidence.

Core Idea
The ears are from the head—wipe them with the same water; no fresh water needed.

In wudu, the sunnah acts perfect the obligatory elements. One such sunnah is wiping the ears. But how? With the same water as the head or with fresh water? This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling and the evidence behind it, contrasting with the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? Wiping the ears in wudu. What is the hukm? Sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? Hadith that the Prophet wiped his head and ears, and said 'the ears are from the head.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this dalil prove the ruling? The phrase 'the ears are from the head' linguistically includes ears in the head wipe, so no separate water is required.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? Imam al-Shafi'i argues using new water is sunnah, citing a hadith about separate water.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon? Hanafis follow the more direct evidence; new water is not required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۰) ومسح الاذنين
(۱۰) چھٹی سنت ) دونوں کانوں کا مسح کرنا ہے۔
حدیث میں ہے ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم مسح برأسه واذنيه ظاهرهما و باطنهما ( ترندی شریف، باب مسح الاذنین ظاهرها بالمنهما ص ۱۶ نمبر ۳۶ / ابوداؤد، باب صفة وضوء النبی ص ۶ نمبر (۱۲) انه مسح براسه وقال الاذنان من الرأس (الف) (ترمذی، باب
ما جاء ان الاذنین من الراس نمبر ۳۷) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ کان کے اوپر اور نیچے کا حصہ سر کے ساتھ مسح کرنا سنت ہے۔ فائده امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ کان کے لئے الگ پانی لینا مسنون ہے۔ اور شعمی فرماتے ہیں کہ آگے کا حصہ چہرے کے ساتھ دھویا جائے اور کان کے پیچھے کا حصہ سر کے ساتھ دھویا جائے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے سمع عبد الله بن زيد يذكر انه راى رسول الله يتوضأ فاخذ لاذنيه ماء خلاف الماء الذي اخذ لرأسه (سنن بیھقی ، باب مسح الاذنین بماء جدید ج اول ص ۱۰۷، نمبر ۳۰۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کان کے لئے الگ پانی لیا۔
(10) And wiping the ears
(10) The sixth sunnah: wiping both ears.
In a hadith: 'The Prophet, peace be upon him, wiped his head and his ears, their outer and inner parts.' (Tirmidhi, Bab Mash al-Udhunayn Zahirihima wa Batinihima, p. 16, no. 36; Abu Dawud, Bab Sifat Wudu' al-Nabi, p. 6, no. 12) 'He wiped his head and said: The ears are from the head.' (a) (Tirmidhi, Bab Ma Ja'a anna al-Udhunayn min al-Ra's, no. 37) This hadith proves that wiping the upper and lower part of the ear with the head is sunnah. Benefit: Imam al-Shafi'i says that taking fresh water for the ears is sunnah. And Shu'bah says: 'The front part should be washed with the face, and the back part with the head.' Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is the hadith: 'I heard Abdullah ibn Zayd mention that he saw the Messenger of Allah performing wudu, and he took for his ears water different from the water he took for his head.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Mash al-Udhunayn bi Ma'in Jadid, vol. 1, p. 107, no. 308) This hadith states that he took separate water for the ears.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof statement establishing the sixth sunnah of wudu: wiping the ears (mash al-udhunain). The author presents hadith showing the Prophet wiped his head and ears together, and the statement 'the ears are from the head' indicates they are wiped with the same water as the head. This is the Hanafi position: ears are included in the head wipe. The author then notes that Imam al-Shafi'i considers using new water for the ears as sunnah, citing a hadith. Another opinion (attributed to Shu'bah) suggests splitting the ear washing: front with face, back with head. The commentary highlights this as a minor ikhtilaf, but the Hanafi position is to wipe the ears with the same water as the head, not with fresh water.

Key Terms
مسح الاذنين (mash al-udhunain): Wiping the two ears during wudu

D) The front is washed with face water and back with head water.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi wudu, wiping the ears is a sunnah performed with the same water used for the head, as the ears are considered part of the head.

Takhlil al-Lahyah: Passing Water Through the Beard in Wudu
A ruling-with-proof passage establishing the sunnah of takhlil al-lahyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on takhlil al-lahyah and distinguish between rulings for thick and thin beards.

Core Idea
Passing water through a thick beard is sunnah; for thin beards, water must reach the skin.

In this lesson, we examine the seventh sunnah of wudu – passing water through the beard (takhlil al-lahyah). The author cites two hadith to establish the Prophet's practice and command, then clarifies that the ruling depends on beard density. This distinction reflects the Hanafi school's precision in applying sunnah acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the text is ruling on (takhlil al-lahyah) and its hukm level (sunnah for thick beard).
The act is passing wet fingers through the beard from underneath.
2
Examine the dalil
Read the two hadith: from Uthman showing the Prophet's practice, and from Anas with the Prophet's statement of divine command.
These are ahad hadith, giving zanni thubut and dalala, supporting sunnah.
3
Apply the density distinction
Note the additional ruling: if the beard is thin (skin visible), water must reach the skin; if thick, washing over is enough and takhlil is sunnah.
This distinction is key to applying the ruling correctly.
4
Understand the implication
Understand that omitting takhlil for a thick beard does not invalidate wudu, but one loses reward. For a thin beard, failing to wet the skin invalidates that part of wudu.

انس بن مالک ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان اذا توضأ اخذ كفا من ماء فادخله تحت حنكه خلل به لحيته وقال هكذا

(3) From Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, when he performed wudu, took a handful of water, put it under his chin, passed it through his beard, and said: 'Thus my Lord commanded me.' Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof statement on the seventh sunnah of wudu: takhlil al-lahyah (passing wet fingers through the beard from underneath). The author cites two hadith: one from Uthman showing the Prophet's practice, and another from Anas where the Prophet states he was commanded by his Lord to do so. The note clarifies a key detail: for a thin beard (where skin is visible), water must reach the skin (that is fard); for a thick beard (dense), washing over the beard suffices, and passing water through it is sunnah, not obligatory. This is a typical Hanafi differentiation based on the extent of the beard.

Key Terms
تخليل اللحية (takhlil al-lahyah): Passing water through the beard by inserting wet fingers from underneath

Key Takeaway
Passing water through a thick beard is a recommended sunnah, but ensuring water reaches the skin under a thin beard is necessary.

The Sunnah of Takhlil al-Asabi' in Wudu
Establishes takhlil al-asabi' as sunnah with proof and wisdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on takhlil al-asabi' (passing water between fingers) in wudu, cite the proof from the Sunnah, and explain why it is crucial for valid wudu.

Core Idea
Passing water between fingers is sunnah, but any dry spot, even a hair's width, invalidates wudu.

In wudu, thoroughness is key. The eighth sunnah of wudu is takhlil al-asabi', an act that ensures water reaches every part of the hands and feet. In this lesson, we examine the proof from the Prophet's command and the wisdom behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that takhlil al-asabi' (passing water between fingers) is listed as the eighth sunnah of wudu. The passage explicitly calls it a sunnah.
It is not fard, but a recommended practice.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites a hadith from Ibn Abbas reporting the Prophet's command: 'When you perform wudu, pass water between the fingers of your hands and your feet.' This hadith is recorded by Tirmidhi and Nasa'i.
The sources are given for verification.
3
Analyze the proof and derive the ruling
In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) from the Prophet indicates obligation unless there is evidence to lower it. Here, the ruling is sunnah due to other proofs (e.g., the practice of the Prophet) and the fact that washing the whole hand is already fard. The command here emphasizes extra care.
The passage does not discuss the usul reasoning, but it is implicit.
4
Understand the wisdom (hikmah)
The wisdom is to ensure water reaches every part of the limb. Even a hair's breadth of dryness invalidates wudu, so this sunnah helps guarantee full coverage.
This connects takhlil to the validity of wudu.
5
Apply in practice
When performing wudu, after washing the hands and feet, intentionally pass water between the fingers using the fingers of the other hand or by rubbing. This fulfills the sunnah and safeguards against invalidating dryness.
Not doing it does not break wudu, but missing a sunnah is a loss of reward.

(12) And the fingers
(12) The eighth sunnah: passing water between the fingers.

This underscores the importance of thoroughness in wudu. The ruling is sunnah based on the hadith.

The Ruling on Washing Thrice in Wudu
Ruling with proof on the sunnah of repeating wudu washes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that washing each limb once is fard and three times is sunnah, and explain the hadith proof for the sunnah.

Core Idea
Washing once is fard; washing thrice is sunnah for certainty and following the Prophet's practice.

In this passage, the author clarifies the ninth sunnah of wudu: repeating the washing of each limb three times. Many students mistakenly think thrice is obligatory; the text explicitly distinguishes between fard (once) and sunnah (thrice). The ruling is further supported by a hadith showing the Prophet's own practice through the action of Uthman ibn Affan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is washing the wudu limbs (face, hands, feet). The text states: washing once is fard (obligatory), washing three times is sunnah (recommended).
This distinction is crucial: the fard is fulfilled with one wash; additional washes are meritorious but not required.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith where Uthman ibn Affan demonstrates the Prophet's wudu, washing each limb three times, and then quotes the Prophet saying whoever performs wudu like this and prays two rak'ahs will be forgiven.
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim and Bukhari; it is a primary proof for the sunnah nature of thrice washing.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's consistent practice of washing three times, as reported by Uthman, indicates that it is a sunnah (recommended) act. The fact that the Prophet did not require it in every instance (the basic fard is once) shows it is not fard.
Hanafi usul: the Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates sunnah unless there is evidence it was obligatory.
4
Note the wisdom behind thrice
The text adds that washing three times ensures no spot remains dry, even the size of a hair, providing certainty of complete purification.
This wisdom aligns with the Hanafi emphasis on certainty (yaqeen) in acts of worship.

(13) And repeating the washing thrice
(13) The ninth sunnah: repeating the washing three times.
(1) Washing each limb once is fard, and washing three times is sunnah. Washing three times ensures that no place, even equal to a hair, remains dry. (2) In a hadith: 'I saw Uthman ibn Affan call for a vessel, then pour water on his hands three times and washed them, then put his right hand into the vessel and rinsed his mouth and snuffed water, then washed his face three times, and his forearms up to the elbows three times, then wiped his head, then washed his feet three times up to the ankles, then said: The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever performs wudu like this wudu of mine, then prays two rak'ahs without having bad thoughts...'
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof statement on the ninth sunnah: takrar al-ghusl (repeating the washing of each limb three times). The author distinguishes: washing once is fard (obligatory) for the limbs that are fard (face, hands, feet); washing twice or thrice is sunnah. The wisdom is thoroughness—three times ensures no dryness remains. The author then presents the hadith of Uthman showing the Prophet's practice of washing each limb three times. This hadith is foundational for the Hanafi ruling that thrice is sunnah. The text cuts off mid-hadith but the point is clear.

Key Terms
تكرير الغسل (takrar al-ghusl): Repeating the washing of wudu limbs (usually thrice)

The Ruling on Intention (Niyyah) in Wudu
Ruling with proof on intention in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intention in wudu and explain the evidence that distinguishes it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Intention in wudu is sunnah, not fard, because water purifies inherently and reward is separate from validity.

This passage explains the Hanafi view that intention is recommended in wudu, not obligatory. The author clarifies the terminology of mustahab vs sunnah and provides textual evidence from the Quran, hadith, and the practice of the Companions. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying wudu in daily practice and for appreciating how Hanafi usul interprets general commands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Intention (niyyah) during wudu. The Hanafi school states it is sunnah (or mustahab).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites three proofs: the hadith 'innama al-a'mal bi-niyyat', the Quranic verse on pure water, and the hadith on sea water being purifying.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does each proof support the ruling? The hadith is about reward, not validity; water is inherently purifying; Umar's wudu without valid intention shows validity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds intention as fard in wudu, based on the same hadith interpreted as a general requirement.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi view is mufta bihi because the evidence for water's inherent purity is stronger, and the hadith's primary import is reward.

(۱۴) وضو کرنے والے کے لئے سنت ہے کہ پاکی کی نیت کرے۔ سنت ہونے کی وجہ یہ حدیث ہے۔ عمر بن خطاب رضي الله عنه على المنبر يقول سمعت رسول الله الله يقول انما الاعمال بالنيات وانمالکل امرء ما نوی (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب کیف کان بدء الوحی الی رسول اللہ اللہ ص ۲ نمبر ۱ ) اعمال کے ثواب کا دارو مدار یا اعمال کے صحیح ہونے کا دارومدار نیت پر ہے۔ بغیر نیت کے وضو کا ثواب نہیں ہوگا۔ اس لئے وضو میں وضو کی نیت کرنا
سنت ہے۔ وضو میں نیت کرنا فرض اس لئے نہیں ہے کہ پانی کو خود بخود پاک کرنے والا قرار دیا ہے چاہے نیت کرے یا نہ کرے۔ وی (۱) آیت ہے انزلنا من السماء ماء طهورا ( آیت ۴۸ سورۃ الفرقان (۲۵) (۲) حدیث میں ہے قال رسول الله هو الطهور ماءه الحل ميتته (ج ) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی ماء البحرانه طلبو ص ۲۱ نمبر ۶۹ ) جب پانی بغیر نیت کی قید کے خود بخود پاک کرنے والا ہے تو نیت کرنا ضروری نہیں رہا۔ البتہ حدیث بالا کی وجہ سے سنت رہے گا (۳) حضرت عمر نے قرآن کریم چھونے کے لئے کفر کی حالت میں وضو کیا ہے۔ اور کفر کی حالت میں نیت کا اعتبار نہیں اس لئے ان کا وضو کرنا بغیر نیت کے درست رہا۔ معلوم ہوا کہ وضو کے لئے نیت کی شرط نہیں ہے۔
