حاشیہ : (الف) عثمان بن عفان کو دیکھا کہ برتن منگوایا پھر تین مرتبہ اپنی ہتھیلیوں پر پانی ڈالا اور اس کو دھویا ۔ پھر دائیں ہاتھ کو برتن میں داخل کیا اور مضمضہ کیا اور استنشاق کیا۔ پھر اپنے چہرے کو تین مرتبہ دھو یا پھر سر پرمسح کیا پھر دونوں پاؤں کو تین مرتبہ ٹخنوں تک دھویا۔ پھر کہا کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا جو میرے اس وضو کی طرح وضو کرے پھر دورکعت نماز پڑھے اور دل میں ادھر ادھر کا کوئی خیال نہ آئے تو اس کے پچھلے گناہ معاف ہو جائیں گے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا اعمال کا دارومدار نیت پر ہے۔ ہر آدمی کے لئے وہ ہے جو اس نے نیت کی (ج) آپ نے فرمایا سمندر کا پانی پاک ہے اور اس کا مردہ ( مچھلی ) حلال ہے۔
Section on recommended acts of wudu. Necessary note: Mustahab is that which doing it gives reward, and not doing it has no punishment. The author wrote that making intention, wiping the whole head, performing wudu in order, and doing wudu consecutively are mustahab. However, in other books they are called sunnah (as in al-Hidayah) and hadiths also show these four are sunnah. The early scholars used to call sunnah also mustahab, so the author called them mustahab. However, starting from the right side and wiping the neck are mustahab. (14) It is sunnah for the one performing wudu to intend purification. The reason it is sunnah is this hadith: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab on the pulpit said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: Deeds are judged by intentions, and each person gets what he intended.' (Bukhari, Book of how revelation began, 1; Muslim, Book of intention, 536). The reward of deeds or the validity of deeds depends on intention. Without intention, there will be no reward for wudu. Therefore, making intention in wudu is sunnah. Intention in wudu is not fard because water is declared inherently purifying, whether one intends or not. And (1) the verse: 'We send down from the sky pure water' (Surah Al-Furqan, 48). (2) In a hadith: The Prophet said: 'Its water is purifying, its dead (sea creatures) are halal.' (Tirmidhi, Book of sea water, 69). Since water is inherently purifying without the condition of intention, intention is not necessary. However, due to the above hadith, it remains sunnah. (3) Sayyiduna Umar made wudu to touch the Quran while in a state of disbelief, and intention is not considered in disbelief, so his wudu without intention was valid. This shows intention is not a condition for wudu. Prayer, fasting, zakat, hajj, etc. are devotional acts where the primary goal is reward, so these acts are not valid without intention; there intention is fard. And Imam al-Shafi'i, based on the hadith 'innama al-a'mal bi-niyyat', holds intention in wudu as fard (Mawsu'ah Imam Shafi'i, vol. 1, chapter on intention in wudu). Footnotes: (a) He saw 'Uthman ibn 'Affan call for a vessel, then pour water on his palms three times and wash them. Then he put his right hand in the vessel and gargled and sniffed water. Then he washed his face three times, then wiped his head, then washed both feet three times to the ankles. Then he said: The Prophet said: Whoever performs wudu like my wudu, then prays two rak'ahs without any worldly thoughts, his previous sins will be forgiven. (b) The Prophet said: Deeds are judged by intentions, and each person gets what he intended. (c) The Prophet said: Sea water is purifying and its dead (fish) are halal.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the status of intention (niyyah) in wudu according to the Hanafi school. The author begins by defining mustahab: an act that brings reward but no punishment for omission. He notes that despite calling the listed items mustahab, other texts classify them as sunnah, including the author's own source. The early Hanafi scholars often used mustahab interchangeably with sunnah. The main ruling is that intention in wudu is sunnah, not fard. The evidence provided is: (1) The well-known hadith 'innama al-a'mal bi-niyyat' is about reward, not validity. (2) Water is declared inherently purifying in the Quran (25:48) and hadith (Tirmidhi), so intention is not needed for purification. (3) The example of Sayyiduna Umar making wudu without a valid intention while a disbeliever shows validity without intention. The passage then contrasts with other acts of worship like prayer, where intention is fard because the purpose is reward. Finally, the author reports the Shafi'i position that intention in wudu is fard, based on the same hadith. The Hanafi response distinguishes between validity and reward: wudu without intention is valid but unrewarded. This is a standard intra-Hanafi clarification and inter-madhhab dispute. The teacher should emphasize that the Hanafi school considers intention recommended (sunnah) in wudu, not obligatory, because the act of purification itself is not a devotional act in the same sense as prayer.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intentional resolve in the heart to perform an act.
مستحب (mustahab): Recommended act; reward for doing, no punishment for leaving.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on making intention (niyyah) in wudu?
A) Fard
B) Sunnah
C) Wajib
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Intention in wudu is sunnah; the act remains valid without it, but reward depends on intention.

The Ruling on Covering the Whole Head in Masah
Ruling on covering entire head in masah with proof and dispute on number of times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of wipes for masah of the head and explain why three wipes with new water is not considered masah.

Core Idea
One wipe covering the whole head is the sunnah; three wipes with new water becomes washing.

The Hanafi school emphasizes that the masah (wiping) of the head in wudu is performed once, covering the entire head. This ruling is derived from the explicit action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and distinguishes between the acts of wiping and washing. In this lesson, we examine the evidence and the dispute with the Shafi'i school regarding the number of wipes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is masah of the head in wudu. The ruling is that covering the whole head (isti'ab) once is sunnah mu'akkadah.
The fard is wiping any part of the head; isti'ab is sunnah.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Cite the hadith of Abdullah ibn Zaid (Bukhari) where the Prophet wiped his head once, bringing his hand forward and backward.
This is an explicit action (fi'l) of the Prophet.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows one wipe covering the whole head. The word 'masaha' in the action indicates a single wipe, not multiple.
The hadith does not mention new water each time.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that three wipes with new water each time is sunnah, citing hadiths like Muslim and Abu Dawud.
The Shafi'i school interprets 'three times' as three separate wipes.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi response reconciles the hadiths: the three wipes in those narrations refer to moving the hand back and forth with the same water to ensure full coverage – not using new water. Using new water changes the act to ghasl (washing), which is not the intended masah.
Thus the Hanafi position is preferred: one wipe, but the hand may be passed multiple times with the same water.

كتاب الطهارة
(۱۵) ويستوعب رأسه بالمسح (١٦) ويرتب الوضوء فيبتدأ بما بدأ الله تعالى بذكره
الخت البيتة : دل سے ارادہ کرنے کا نام نیت ہے اور زبان سے بول لے تو بہتر ہے۔
(۱۵) پورے سر کا مسح کرنا۔
(۱) حدیث میں ہے عن عبد الله بن زيد عن وضوء النبي ال... ثم ادخل يده في الاناء فمسح برأسه فاقبل بيده وادبــر بهـا (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب مسح الرأس مرۃ ص ۳۲ نمبر ۱۹۲) (۲) ابوداؤد ، باب صفت وضوء النبی ص ۶ نمبر ۱۲ فی تصریح فمسح برأسه مرة واحدة ) حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آپ نے ایک مرتبہ سر پر مسح فرمایا (۳) اگر نئے نئے پانی سے تین مرتبہ مسیح کریں تو وہ دھوتا ہو جائے گا مسح باقی نہیں رہے گا۔ دھونے کے اعضاء میں تین مرتبہ دھوئیں تو کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے۔ لیکن مسح تین مرتبہ نئے نئے پانی سے کریں تو موضوع ہی بدل جائے گا۔ اس لئے ایک ہی مرتبہ مسح کرنا سنت ہے۔
جن احادیث میں تین مرتبہ دھونے کا تذکرہ ہے وہ ایک ہی پانی سے پورے سر کوگھیر نے کے لئے تین مرتبہ کیا گیا ہے۔ اور یہ تو ہم بھی کہتے ہیں کہ ایک پانی سے ہاتھ کو تین مرتبہ سر پر پھیرا جائے تا کہ اچھی طرح پورے سر پر سح ہو جائے۔
امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ تین مرتبہ مسح کرے اور تینوں مرتبہ نیا پانی لینا سنت ہے۔ ان کا استدلال اس حدیث سے ہے و مسح رأسه ثلاثا ( ابوداؤد، باب صفة وضوء النبی ص ۶ نمبر ۷ (۱۰) فمسح برأسه فاقبل بهما وادبر بدء بمقدم رأسه ثم ذهب بهما الى قفاة ثم ردهما حتى رجع الى المكان الذى بدء منه وغسل رجليه (ب) (مسلم شریف، باب آخر فی صفۃ الوضور ص ۱۲۳ نمبر ۲۳۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تین مرتبہ مسح کرے۔ ہم جواب دیتے ہیں کہ یہ سب احادیث میں ایک ہی پانی سے استیعاب کے لئے کئی
مرتبہ سح کیا ہے جس کے قائل ہم بھی ہیں۔ يستوعب : گھیرے، احاطہ کرے
نو مسح کے لئے نیا پانی لینا سنت ہے۔
ومسح برأسه بماء غير فضل يده ( مسلم شریف ، باب آخر فی صفۃ الوضور ص ۱۲۳ نمبر ۲۳۶)
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے برتن میں ہاتھ ڈالا اور سر پر مسح کیا اس طرح کہ اپنے ہاتھ کو پیچھے سے آگے کیا پھر آگے سے پیچھے کیا (ب) آپ نے سر پر سح فرمایا اور ہاتھ کو پیچھے سے آگے کی طرف لائے اور پیچھے کی طرف لے گئے۔ اور سر کے اگلے حصے سے شروع کیا۔ پھر دونوں ہاتھوں کو گدی تک لے گئے پھر ان کو واپس لوٹا یا یہاں تک کہ اس مقام تک واپس لائے جہاں سے شروع کیا تھا اور پاؤں کو دھویا۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part One, 39, Book of Purification (15) And he should cover his whole head in wiping (masah). (16) And he should arrange the order of wudu, beginning with what Allah began mentioning. The note: Intention is resolve in the heart, and it is better to utter it with the tongue. (15) Wiping the whole head. (1) In a hadith from Abdullah ibn Zaid about the Prophet's wudu: ... Then he put his hand in the vessel and wiped his head, bringing his hand forward and backward. (Bukhari, Book of wiping the head once, Hadith 192) (2) Abu Dawud, Book of description of the Prophet's wudu, Hadith 12, states clearly: He wiped his head once. From the hadith it is known that he wiped his head once. (3) If one wipes three times with new water, it becomes washing (ghasl) and not wiping. For washing the limbs, washing three times is fine, but if one wipes three times with new water, the nature of the act changes. Therefore, wiping once is sunnah. The hadiths that mention three times are actually about using the same water to cover the whole head three times (for thoroughness). We also say that the hand should be passed over the head three times with the same water to cover the whole head well. Imam al-Shafi'i says one should wipe three times and it is sunnah to take new water each time. His evidence is the hadith: 'He wiped his head three times' (Abu Dawud, Hadith 7/10; Muslim, Hadith 235). We respond that all these hadiths are about using the same water for coverage, which we also accept. 'Yastaw'ib' means to encompass, to cover. Note: Taking new water for wiping is sunnah. And he wiped his head with water not from the leftover in his hand (Muslim, Hadith 236). Footnote: (a) He put his hand in the vessel and wiped his head, bringing his hand from back to front and front to back. (b) He wiped his head, bringing his hands from back to front and back again, beginning from the front of the head, then taking them to the nape, then returning them to where he started, and washed his feet.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on wiping the head (masah) in wudu. The author cites the matn: 'And he should cover his whole head in wiping.' The commentary explains that it is sunnah to wipe the entire head once, not three times with new water. The primary evidence is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Zaid that the Prophet wiped his head once (forward and backward). The author then addresses the Shafi'i position that three wipes with new water is sunnah, based on a hadith that mentions three times. The Hanafi response clarifies that those hadiths refer to moving the hand back and forth with the same water for thorough coverage, not using new water each time. Using new water for masah changes the act to washing (ghasl), which is not the intended act. The author also notes a separate hadith that using new water for masah is actually a sunnah (for those who wish to do so), but the obligatory aspect is covering the head once. The footnote describes the prophetic practice: bringing the hands from the front of the head to the back and back again. The teacher should emphasize the distinction between masah (wiping) and ghasl (washing), and that the Hanafi school holds one wipe covering the whole head as sunnah, while the Shafi'i school holds three wipes with new water.

Key Terms
مسح (masah): Wiping with a wet hand on a body part; distinct from ghasl (washing).
استيعاب (isti'ab): Encompassing or covering the entire head in wiping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, how many times should one wipe the head in wudu?
A) Once
B) Three times with new water each time
C) Three times with the same water
D) Twice

Key Takeaway
One wipe covering the whole head is the sunnah for masah; using new water changes it to washing.

Wiping the Head Once: The Hanafi View on Masah
Ruling with Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on head wiping number

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that wiping the head once is sunnah, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Wiping the head once is sunnah; three times with fresh water changes masah to ghusl.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute on the number of wipings in masah of the head. The Hanafi school holds that a single wipe with one application of water is sunnah, while the Shafi'i school considers three wipings with fresh water as sunnah. We will analyze the evidence from hadith and the Hanafi response that reconciles the reports.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Begin by precisely stating what the Hanafi school holds regarding the number of wipings and the use of water: one wipe with one application is sunnah; multiple passes with the same water for coverage are allowed.
Refer to the matn phrase 'yasta'ību ra'sahu bil-masah' (he covers his head with wiping).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Identify Imam al-Shafi'i as the opponent and his view: it is sunnah to wipe three times, each time taking fresh water.
The Shafi'i position relies on hadiths that explicitly mention 'masaha bira'sihi thalathan' (he wiped his head three times).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: the hadith of forward and backward motion and the report 'masaha bira'sihi thalathan' from Abu Dawood.
Some also cite the hadith from Muslim which describes the Prophet moving his hands forward and backward, which is interpreted as three wipings.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: those hadiths describe multiple passes with the same water for complete coverage (istī'āb), not three separate fresh applications. The explicit report 'masaha bira'sihi marratan wahidatan' (once) is preferred.
The Hanafi response also argues that using fresh water three times would change the act to ghusl (washing), which is a different legal category.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: Hanafi: once is sunnah (three passes with same water allowed); Shafi'i: three times with fresh water is sunnah. Both agree the obligatory part (wiping the head) is fulfilled by one wipe.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the position of once, based on the principle of avoiding excessive water use.

(۱) حدیث میں ہے عن عبد الله بن زيد عن وضوء النبي ال... ثم ادخل يده في الاناء فمسح برأسه فاقبل بيده وادبــر بهـا (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب مسح الرأس مرۃ ص ۳۲ نمبر ۱۹۲) (۲) ابوداؤد ، باب صفت وضوء النبی ص ۶ نمبر ۱۲ فی تصریح فمسح برأسه مرة واحدة ) حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آپ نے ایک مرتبہ سر پر مسح فرمایا (۳) اگر نئے نئے پانی سے تین مرتبہ مسیح کریں تو وہ دھوتا ہو جائے گا مسح باقی نہیں رہے گا۔ دھونے کے اعضاء میں تین مرتبہ دھوئیں تو کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے۔ لیکن مسح تین مرتبہ نئے نئے پانی سے کریں تو موضوع ہی بدل جائے گا۔ اس لئے ایک ہی مرتبہ مسح کرنا سنت ہے۔

From the heart, the name of intention is niyyah, and it is better to speak it. (15) Wiping the entire head. (1) In a hadith from Abdullah bin Zayd about the wudu of the Prophet (s)... then he put his hand in the vessel and wiped his head, moving his hand forward and backward. (Bukhari, Bab Masah al-Ra's Marrah, p. 32 no. 192) (2) Abu Dawood, Bab Sifat Wudu al-Nabi, p. 6 no. 12 states clearly: 'He wiped his head once.' From the hadith it is understood that he wiped his head once. (3) If one wipes three times with fresh water, it becomes washing; masah would not remain. There is no harm in washing the limbs three times. But if masah is done three times with fresh water, the action changes. Therefore, wiping once is sunnah. The hadiths that mention three times refer to moving the hand over the head three times with the same water to cover the entire head. We also say that the hand should be passed over the head three times with the same water so that the whole head is well wiped. Imam al-Shafi'i says that one should wipe three times, and each time taking fresh water is sunnah. His evidence is the hadith: 'He wiped his head three times' (Abu Dawood, p. 6 no. 7; Muslim, p. 123 no. 235) from which it is understood that one wipes three times. We answer that in all these hadiths, multiple wipings with the same water were done to cover the whole head, which we also affirm. Istī'āb means to encompass, to cover. Note: Taking fresh water for masah is sunnah. 'And he wiped his head with water not remaining from his hand' (Muslim, p. 123 no. 236).
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the number of times to wipe the head in wudu. The Hanafi position, based on the hadith of Abdullah bin Zayd and others, is that wiping once is sunnah. The author explains that if one uses fresh water each time, the act becomes washing (ghusl) rather than wiping (masah). The Shafi'i position, citing hadiths like the one from Muslim showing three wipings, considers three wipings with fresh water as sunnah. The Hanafi response reconciles those hadiths by noting that the multiple wipings in the reports were done with the same water to ensure complete coverage of the head, not separate fresh applications. Thus, the Hanafi view remains that a single wipe suffices, and it is sunnah to do it once. The footnote adds that taking fresh water for wiping is sunnah, citing another hadith.

Key Terms
مسح (masah): Wiping, i.e., passing a wet hand over a limb without water flowing, as opposed to ghusl (washing).
استيعاب (istī'āb): Complete coverage; ensuring the entire head is included in the wiping.
سنت (sunnah): Emphasized recommended practice; omission is permissible but leaves one lacking reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is fard to wipe three times with the same water.
D) It is optional to wipe once or three times, both equally sunnah.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, wiping the head once with one application of water is sunnah; multiple passes with the same water for coverage are allowed, but using fresh water each time changes the act to ghusl.

Order (Tartib) in Wudu
Matn statement on order of wudu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the order (tartīb) of wudu and explain that it is sunnah, not wajib.

Core Idea
The order of wudu is sunnah in the Hanafi school, not wajib, despite the Quranic sequence.

This matn statement is a memorization anchor pointing to the ideal sequence of wudu as mentioned in the Quran. However, the legal ruling in the Hanafi school is that this order is sunnah, not obligatory. Understanding this distinction helps avoid the common misconception that reversing the order invalidates wudu.

Guided Path
1
Read the matn line carefully.
The matn says: 'And he should perform wudu in order, beginning with what Allah Almighty mentioned first.' This is a concise instruction to follow the Quranic sequence.
2
Identify the Quranic sequence.
Allah mentions the limbs in Surah al-Ma'idah (5:6): face, hands, head (wiping), feet. The matn references this order.
3
Understand the Hanafi interpretation.
The Hanafi school, based on hadith evidence (e.g., the practice of Ali ibn Abi Talib), holds that the imperative 'yurattib' indicates sunnah, not wujub. Thus, order is recommended but not mandatory.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position.
Imam al-Shafi'i considers order wajib because the Quranic sequence and the Prophet's practice show continuity. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).

(16) And he should perform wudu in order, beginning with what Allah Almighty mentioned first. Al-khut al-baytah: from the heart the name of intention is niyyah, and it is better to speak it.

Commentary
This passage presents the matn (core text) statement regarding order (tartīb) in wudu. The matn instructs that wudu should follow the sequence in which Allah mentioned the limbs in the Quran: face, then hands, then wiping the head, then feet. The Hanafi school rules that this order is sunnah, not wajib, based on the hadith of Ali (رضي الله عنه) and the understanding that the Quranic imperative does not enforce sequence. The missing sharh would typically elaborate on the evidence and the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i who holds order to be wajib. The Urdu line after the matn seems to be a separate note on niyyah (intention) and may be a fragment from another part of the text.

Key Terms
يرتب (yurattibu): He performs in order, observing sequence.
الوضوء (al-wudu'): Ritual washing before prayer.

Continuity (Muwalat) in Wudu
Ruling on performing wudu consecutively

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on muwalat in wudu and explain why it is mustahabb using the dalil from the athar of Ibn 'Umar.

Core Idea
Muwalat in wudu is mustahabb, not wajib — a break does not invalidate wudu.

You may have heard that wudu must be performed in one continuous sequence without any delay. However, the Hanafi school takes a more lenient view. In this lesson, we examine the evidence that shows continuity is recommended but not obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses muwalat (consecutive washing of wudu limbs). State the Hanafi ruling: mustahabb (recommended).
The text uses mustahabb, synonymous with sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
2
Locate the primary proof
The author cites the practice of the Prophet (s) as observed in hadiths, and the specific athar of Ibn 'Umar.
The athar is from Muwatta Imam Malik.
3
Analyze the athar's legal implication
Ibn 'Umar washed face and head, then later wiped his khuff when entering mosque. This shows a permissible break; hence muwalat is not obligatory.
The break occurred for a valid reason (janazah), but the principle is established.
4
Understand the scope
If a valid excuse causes a delay, the recommended practice is still considered fulfilled in terms of sunnah. Without excuse, the sunnah is missed but wudu remains valid.
The Hanafi school prioritizes ease and does not deem such breaks invalidating.

(۱) تمام احادیث میں ذکر ہے کہ آپ نے پے در پے اعضاء دھوئے ہیں۔ ایسا نہیں ہوا کہ ایک عضو دھو کر بہت دیر کے بعد دوسرا عضو ھو یا اس لئے پے در پے دھونا بھی مستحب ہے۔ البتہ عذر کی وجہ سے دیر ہو جائے تو سنت کی ادائیگی میں فرق نہیں آئے گا (۲) اثر میں ہے ان عبد الـلـه بـن عـمـر بال بالسوق ثم توضأ وغسل وجهه ومسح برأسه ثم دعى لجنازة ليصلى عليها حين دخل المسجد فمسح على خفيه ثم صلى عليها (موطا امام مالک، باب ما جاء فی امسح علی الخفین ص ۲۴) اس اثر میں مسح علی الخفین بعد میں کیا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ تمام اعضاء کا پیدر پے دھونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔
(17) And continuity (tawālī) (18) and starting with the right. Performing consecutively. i.e., after washing one limb, immediately wash the next; do not delay so much that the first limb dries. The phrase al-tawālī is not in some copies. (1) In all hadiths it is mentioned that the Prophet (s) washed limbs consecutively; he never washed a limb and then waited long before the next. Therefore, washing consecutively is mustahabb. If there is an excuse and delay occurs, the sunnah is not affected. (2) An athar: 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar was in the market, then performed wudu, washed his face, wiped his head, then was called for a janazah to pray upon entering the mosque, so he wiped over his khuff and then prayed over it.' (Muwatta Imam Malik, Bab ma ja'a fi al-masah 'ala al-khuffayn, p. 24) This shows that washing all limbs consecutively is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on muwālāt (consecutive performance) in wudu. The author states that it is mustahabb (recommended) to wash limbs one after the other without lengthy pauses. The proof includes the practice of the Prophet (s) observed in hadiths and the athar from Ibn 'Umar who delayed wiping his khuff until after entering the mosque, indicating that a break does not invalidate wudu or require repetition. The note mentions that the phrase 'al-tawālī' is absent in some manuscripts, suggesting it may be an addition. The analysis confirms that muwālāt is not wajib; it is a recommended practice that is pardoned in case of necessity.

Key Terms
التوالى (al-tawālī): Consecutive performance; performing wudu acts without delaying until the earlier limb dries.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; omission is not sinful but is disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on performing wudu acts consecutively (muwalat)?
A) It is wajib; delaying invalidates wudu.
B) It is mustahabb; if a break occurs, wudu remains valid.
C) It is fard; any delay requires starting over.
D) It is makruh to wash consecutively.

Key Takeaway
Muwalat in wudu is mustahabb, not obligatory; a break does not invalidate the act.

Starting with the Right in Wudu – Mustahabb with Proof
Ruling on beginning wudu with the right side

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on beginning wudu with the right side and explain the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Starting wudu with the right side is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory—the Prophet loved it, but did not command it absolutely.

This passage addresses a common practice in wudu: beginning with the right side. The author clarifies that while some may consider it sunnah, the Hanafi school regards it as mustahabb (recommended). The evidence comes from two hadiths showing the Prophet's practice. Understanding this distinction (mustahabb vs. sunnah) is important for correct fiqh and avoiding exaggeration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? It is beginning wudu with the right side. The ruling is mustahabb (recommended).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? Two hadiths: one from Aisha (RA) about the Prophet loving tayammun in all his affairs, and the instruction to Umm Atiyyah regarding washing the deceased.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove mustahabb? The word 'yahibuhu' (he loved) indicates a preferred action, not an obligation. The Prophet's practice is a model, but not a command.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars consider it sunnah (a more emphasized recommended action). What is the difference? In practice, both are non-obligatory, but sunnah carries a higher virtue. The author adopts mustahabb.
5
Determine the practical implication
For the person performing wudu: starting with the right is meritorious, but if one forgets or starts with the left, wudu is still valid and no compensation is needed.

(۱۸) وبالميامن
دھونے کو دائیں طرف سے شروع کرنا ( مستحب ہے)
وجہ حدیث میں ہے عن عائشة رضی ا الله عنها كان النبى الا الله يعجبه التيمن في تنعله وترجله وطهوره في شانه كله ، وقال النبي الا الله الام عطية في غسل ابنته ابدأن بميامنها ومواضع الوضوء منها (ب) بخاری شریف، باب التيمن في الوضوء والغسل ص ۲۹ نمبر ۱۶۸/۱۶۷) ان احادیث کی بنا پر دائیں جانب سے وضو کرنا مستحب ہے۔ اور بعض حضرات نے اس کو سنت کہا ہے۔ التیمن : دائیں جانب سے شروع کرنا۔
(18) And with the right (by al-yamin). Starting washing from the right side (is mustahabb). The proof is the hadith from 'A'isha (radiyallahu 'anha): 'The Prophet (s) loved to begin with the right in putting on shoes, combing hair, purification, and in all his affairs.' And the Prophet (s) said to Umm 'Atiyyah regarding washing his daughter: 'Begin with her right side and the places of wudu on her.' (Bukhari, Bab al-Tayammun fi al-Wudu' wa al-Ghusl, p. 29 no. 168/167) Based on these hadiths, starting wudu from the right side is mustahabb. Some scholars have called it sunnah. Al-tayammun: starting with the right side.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage concerns the desirability of beginning wudu with the right side (tayammun). The author states that it is mustahabb (recommended), while some scholars consider it sunnah. The proof is from two hadiths: one from 'A'isha that the Prophet (s) loved to start with the right in various acts, and another from Umm 'Atiyyah regarding washing the deceased, where he instructed to begin with the right side. Since wudu is a form of purification, the same principle applies. The term 'tayammun' is defined as beginning with the right side.

Key Terms
الميامن (al-mayamin): The right (plural); starting with the right side.
التيمن (al-tayammun): Beginning with the right side; seeking blessing from the right.

D) It is fard.

Key Takeaway
Beginning wudu with the right side is mustahabb, supported by the Prophet's practice of tayammun; it is not obligatory.

The Ruling on Order (Tartib) in Wudu: Sunnah, Not Wajib
Explaining that order in wudu is sunnah and responding to Shafi'i's view of obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on order in wudu, cite the key evidence, and explain why it is sunnah not wajib, contrasting with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Order in wudu is sunnah, not wajib — omitting it does not invalidate the wudu.

In this lesson, we examine a classic ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on the necessity of washing the limbs in sequence during wudu. The Hanafi school holds that order is sunnah, while the Shafi'i school considers it wajib. Understanding this difference depends on how we interpret the Quranic verse and the Prophet's practice. We will explore the proofs on both sides and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling on tartib: it is sunnah (recommended), not wajib. Note that this is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i considers tartib wajib, based on the Quranic order and the Prophet's constancy.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
Review the evidence: the 'fa' in 'faghsilu' indicates sequence but not obligation, and the hadith of Ali (ra) shows order is not essential.
The hadith: 'ما ابالی اذا اتممت وضوئی بای اعضائی بدأت'
4
Examine the Shafi'i dalil
Understand the Shafi'i argument: the Quranic sequence and the Prophet's continuous practice imply obligation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: Hanafis consider wudu valid if order is omitted; Shafi'is require order for validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة (۱۷) والتوالى (۱۸) وبالميامن تقریبا تمام احادیث میں اسی ترتیب سے اعضاء دھونا مذکور ہے جس ترتیب سے قرآن میں ذکر ہے۔ اس لئے حضور کی مواظبت کرنے سے ترتیب سنت ہے (۳) از اتمتم الی الصلوۃ فالنفسلو او جو کم الآیۃ میں فاغسلوا کی ف تعقیب کے لئے ہے۔ اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر نماز کے لئے کھڑے ہو تو پہلے چہرہ دھو ؤ جب کھڑے ہونے اور چہرہ دھونے میں ترتیب ہوئی تو باقی اعضا میں بھی ترتیب ہونی چاہئے اس لئے وضو میں ترتیب سنت ہے۔ لیکن یہ ترتیب واجب نہیں ہے جیسا کہ امام شافعی نے فرمایا کیونکہ (۱) اوپر کے دلائل سنت پر دلالت کرتے ہیں وجوب پر نہیں (۲) حضرت علیؓ نے فرمایا تھا ما ابالی اذا اتممت وضوئی بای اعضائی بدأت (الف) ( دار قطنی ، باب ماروی فی جواز تقدیم غسل الید الیسری علی الیمنی ج اول ص ۹۲ حدیث نمبر ۲۸۹ رسمن للبیھقی ، باب الرخصة في البدائية باليسار ج اول ص ۱۴۰ نمبر ۴۰۶) نا امام شافعی پچھلے دلائل کی وجہ سے ترتیب واجب قرار دیتے ہیں۔ جواب گزر گیا۔
Almost all hadiths mention washing the limbs in the same order as mentioned in the Quran. Therefore, due to the Prophet's constancy, order is sunnah. (3) In the verse 'When you stand up for prayer, wash your faces...' the 'fa' in 'faghsilu' indicates sequence. This means that if you stand up for prayer, first wash your face. Since there is sequence between standing and washing the face, there should also be sequence in the remaining limbs. Therefore, order in wudu is sunnah. But this order is not obligatory, as Imam al-Shafi'i stated, because (1) the above evidences indicate sunnah, not obligation; (2) Hadrat Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'I do not care, when I have completed my wudu, with which limb I begin.' (Reference: Darqutni, Bab ma ruwi fi jawaz taqdim ghasl al-yad al-yusra 'ala al-yumna, vol. 1, p. 92, hadith 289, and al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-rukhsah fi al-bidayah bi al-yasar, vol. 1, p. 140, no. 406) So Imam Shafi'i declares order obligatory due to previous evidences. The response has passed.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on the order (tartib) of washing limbs in wudu. The author begins by noting that nearly all hadiths describe the limbs being washed in the same sequence as in the Quran (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6). This constancy (muwazabah) of the Prophet establishes the order as sunnah. Evidence from the Quran: the imperative 'faghsilu' uses the particle 'fa' which implies sequence (ta'qib) — meaning washing follows standing for prayer. From this, the commentators infer a sequence among the limbs themselves. However, the author clarifies that this order is sunnah, not wajib (obligatory). This is a point of dispute: Imam al-Shafi'i considers it wajib. The text provides two reasons for the Hanafi position: First, the evidences (the hadiths and the Quranic inference) indicate sunnah level, not obligation — because the prophetic practice shows it, but not with a command that indicates obligation. Second, a statement from Ali ibn Abi Talib (ra) is quoted: 'I do not care, when I have completed my wudu, with which limb I begin.' This shows that order is not necessary for the validity of wudu. The author then notes that despite these evidences, Imam al-Shafi'i held it to be wajib. The response (jawaab) is considered already given — that the evidences only indicate sunnah. Thus, the Hanafi position is that order is a sunnah, and omitting it does not invalidate wudu, but it is better to observe it.

Key Terms
ترتیب (tartib): Order of washing limbs in wudu as mentioned in Quran (face, hands, head, feet).
سنت (sunnah): A recommended act proven by the Prophet's practice, neither fard nor wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on observing the order (tartib) of washing limbs in wudu?
A) It is fard (obligatory).
B) It is wajib (obligatory).
C) It is sunnah (recommended).
D) It is mustahab (preferable).

Key Takeaway
Order of washing limbs in wudu is a recommended practice (sunnah) in the Hanafi school, not an obligation, and omitting it does not invalidate the wudu.

Ruling on Continuity (Muwalat) in Wudu: Mustahab
Explaining that washing limbs consecutively without delay is mustahab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on muwalat and explain the evidence from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
Continuity in wudu is mustahab, not wajib—delaying between limbs does not invalidate wudu.

Many students assume that washing limbs consecutively without delay is obligatory. This lesson clarifies that the Hanafi school considers muwalat only mustahab. You will learn the proofs from the Prophet's practice and a companion's action, and understand why wudu remains valid even with a delay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (muwalat in wudu) and what level of hukm it carries (mustahab).
Muwalat means washing the next limb before the previous one dries.
2
Analyze the primary dalil (Prophet's practice)
The author cites that the Prophet consistently performed muwalat. Consider why this constancy indicates mustahab rather than wajib.
Continuous practice without command suggests preference, not obligation.
3
Analyze the secondary dalil (athar of Ibn Umar)
Ibn Umar wiped over his khuffs after completing part of wudu, breaking continuity. This shows delay is permissible.
The athar directly demonstrates that muwalat is not required.
4
Synthesize the Hanafi position
Combine the evidence: muwalat is mustahab, but wudu is valid even with a delay. Note that an excused delay does not affect the sunnah.
One should try to maintain continuity, but it is not a condition of validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۷) پے در پے کرنا۔ جائے یعنی ایک عضو کو دھونے کے بعد فورا دوسرا عضو دھوئے ایسا نہیں کہ دوسرا عضو د ھونے میں بہت دیر کر دے یہاں تک کہ پہلا عضو خشک ہو التوالی کا جملہ بعض نسخوں میں نہیں ہے۔ (۱) تمام احادیث میں ذکر ہے کہ آپ نے پے در پے اعضاء دھوئے ہیں۔ ایسا نہیں ہوا کہ ایک عضو دھو کر بہت دیر کے بعد دوسرا عضو ھو یا اس لئے پے در پے دھونا بھی مستحب ہے۔ البتہ عذر کی وجہ سے دیر ہو جائے تو سنت کی ادائیگی میں فرق نہیں آئے گا (۲) اثر میں ہے ان عبد الـلـه بـن عـمـر بال بالسوق ثم توضأ وغسل وجهه ومسح برأسه ثم دعى لجنازة ليصلى عليها حين دخل المسجد فمسح على خفيه ثم صلى عليها (موطا امام مالک، باب ما جاء فی امسح علی الخفین ص ۲۴) اس اثر میں مسح علی الخفین بعد میں کیا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ تمام اعضاء کا پیدر پے دھونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔
To do consecutively. That is, after washing one limb, immediately wash the second, not delay the second so much that the first becomes dry. The phrase 'al-muwalat' is not in some manuscripts. (1) In all hadiths it is mentioned that the Prophet washed limbs consecutively. It never happened that he washed one limb and then delayed much before washing the next. Therefore, washing consecutively is also mustahab. However, if a delay occurs due to an excuse, it does not affect the performance of the sunnah. (2) It is reported that Abdullah ibn Umar once sold in the market, then performed wudu, washing his face and wiping his head, then was called for a janazah prayer when he entered the mosque, so he wiped over his khuffs and then prayed over it. In this effect, wiping over the khuffs was done later, which shows that washing all limbs consecutively is not necessary.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on muwalat (continuity) in wudu. Muwalat means to wash the limbs one after the other without a significant pause. The author begins by noting that the term 'al-muwalat' is absent in some manuscripts, indicating it may not be a consensus term. The proof from hadith: the Prophet consistently washed limbs without unnecessary delay. This constancy makes muwalat mustahab (preferable), not obligatory. The text then presents an effect from Abdullah ibn Umar: he was in the market, performed wudu (washing face and wiping head), then was called for a funeral prayer. He then wiped over his khuffs (which is normally done after washing feet) and prayed. This shows that the continuity of all limbs is not required because he wiped over his khuffs later, breaking the sequence of washing. This supports the ruling that muwalat is not wajib. Thus, the Hanafi position is that muwalat is mustahab (or part of the sunnah acts) but omitting it without excuse is makruh tanzih, and wudu remains valid. If there is a valid excuse (like forgetting or necessary interruption), the sunnah is still fulfilled.

Key Terms
توالی (muwalat): Washing limbs consecutively without a break that would cause the previous limb to dry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is fard.
B) It is wajib.
C) It is mustahab.
D) It is strictly prohibited.

Key Takeaway
Muwalat in wudu is mustahab; wudu remains valid even with a delay between limbs.

Ruling on Starting with the Right in Wudu: Mustahab
Explaining that beginning wudu with the right side is mustahab, supported by hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on starting wudu with the right side and explain the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Starting wudu with the right side is mustahab, not obligatory – the Prophet's practice indicates preference.

This passage addresses a common question: must wudu begin with the right side? The author clarifies that it is recommended (mustahab), not required. The evidence comes from prophetic hadith showing the Prophet's love for starting with the right in all affairs, including purification. Some scholars call it sunnah, but the author maintains it is mustahab due to the nature of the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is starting wudu with the right side. The ruling in the Hanafi school is mustahab (recommended).
Some Hanafi scholars call it sunnah, but the author here presents it as mustahab.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is from two hadith: one from Aisha (ra) and one from Umm Atiyyah, both recorded in Bukhari.
These hadith show the Prophet's practice and instruction.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's 'liking' (ya'jabuhu) indicates recommendation, not obligation. The command 'ابدا' (start) in the Umm Atiyyah hadith is interpreted as showing preference.
In Hanafi usul, commands can indicate obligation or recommendation based on context.
4
Note the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars consider it sunnah, but the author (and the majority) hold it as mustahab.
The difference is subtle: constancy (muwazabah) would make it sunnah, but the evidence is seen as supporting mustahab.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that starting with the right is mustahab. Omitting it does not affect the validity of wudu.
This is consistent with the footnote citing Ali (ra): 'I do not care if I complete my wudu from which limb I begin.'

Source Text

(۱۸) دھونے کو دائیں طرف سے شروع کرنا ( مستحب ہے) وجہ حدیث میں ہے عن عائشة رضی ا الله عنها كان النبى الا الله يعجبه التيمن في تنعله وترجله وطهوره في شانه كله ، وقال النبي الا الله الام عطية في غسل ابنته ابدأن بميامنها ومواضع الوضوء منها (ب) بخاری شریف، باب التيمن في الوضوء والغسل ص ۲۹ نمبر ۱۶۸/۱۶۷) ان احادیث کی بنا پر دائیں جانب سے وضو کرنا مستحب ہے۔ اور بعض حضرات نے اس کو سنت کہا ہے۔ التیمن : دائیں جانب سے شروع کرنا۔ حاشیہ : (الف) مجھے کوئی پرواہ نہیں کہ اگر میں اپنا وضو پورا کرلوں تو کسی عضو سے وضو شروع کروں ۔ (ب) آپ کو دائیں جانب سے شروع کرنا اچھا لگتا تھا جوتا پہننے میں کنگی کرنے میں اور وضو کرنے میں اور ہر چیز میں۔ آپ نے ام عطیہ سے فرمایا اپنی بیٹی کے غسل کے سلسلہ میں کہ اس کی دائیں جانب سے غسل شروع کرنا اور اس کے وضو کے مقامات کو بھی دائیں جانب سے شروع کرنا
Starting washing from the right side is mustahab. Evidence: Hadith from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) liked to start with the right when putting on shoes, combing hair, performing purification, and in all his affairs. And the Prophet said to Umm Atiyyah regarding washing his daughter: 'Start with her right side and the places of wudu on her.' (Bukhari, chapter on starting with the right in wudu and ghusl, p. 29, no. 168/167) Based on these hadiths, performing wudu from the right side is mustahab. And some scholars have called it sunnah. Al-Tayammun: starting from the right side. Footnote: (a) I do not care if I complete my wudu from which limb I begin. (b) The Prophet liked starting with the right in putting on shoes, combing hair, performing wudu, and in everything. He said to Umm Atiyyah regarding washing his daughter: start with her right side and the places of wudu on her.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on starting wudu with the right side (tayammun). The author states it is mustahab, but some scholars consider it sunnah. The evidence is a hadith from Aisha (ra) that the Prophet liked to begin with the right in all matters, including purification. Another hadith to Umm Atiyyah instructs to start washing his daughter from the right side. These indicate preference. The author notes that the difference between mustahab and sunnah is subtle: constancy (muwazabah) makes it sunnah, but the weaker evidence makes it mustahab according to the author. The footnote quotes Ali (ra) showing it is not essential. Thus, the Hanafi position: it is mustahab to start with the right, and if done, it is better, but wudu is valid if started with the left.

Key Terms
تیمن (tayammun): Starting with the right side in washing actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on starting wudu with the right side?
A) Wajib.
B) Sunnah.
C) Mustahab.
D) Mubah.

Key Takeaway
Starting wudu with the right is recommended (mustahab), not obligatory; the Prophet's practice shows preference, but omitting it does not invalidate wudu.

Ruling on Wiping the Neck in Wudu: Mustahab
Explaining that wiping the neck in wudu is mustahab, supported by hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping the neck during wudu and identify the evidence (dalil) that establishes it as mustahab.

Core Idea
Wiping the neck in wudu is mustahab, not sunnah, based on a lesser-strength hadith.

In this lesson, we examine a specific act within wudu – wiping the neck (masah al-raqaba). The author presents two hadith reports and clarifies that this act is mustahab (recommended), not part of the fourteen sunnan. Understanding the distinction between sunnah and mustahab is essential for properly prioritising acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being discussed and what legal classification (hukm) the text assigns to it. Here, the act is wiping the neck during wudu, and the ruling is explicitly stated as mustahab.
Mustahab is a level below sunnah; its reward is promised but omission is not blameworthy.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited by the author. Two ahad hadith are provided: one from Ibn Umar promising protection from the yoke, and another from a companion witnessing the Prophet's practice.
Both hadith are ahad (solitary), making their transmission (thubut) zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyse how the evidence indicates the ruling. The promise of reward in the first hadith implies desirability (istihbab), not obligation. The second hadith shows the Prophet's action, which is also indicative of recommendation.
In Hanafi usul, a promise of reward without threat of punishment points to istihbab.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Check if any other school or position differs. The text does not mention any ikhtilaf; the ruling is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) within the Hanafi school and beyond.
Thus, no further tarjih is needed.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Since there is no conflict, the stated position is the mufta bihi. The author also lists the fourteen sunnan separately, emphasizing that neck wiping is an additional recommended act.
The Hanafi position is clear: it is mustahab.

Wiping the neck is mustahab. (1) From Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever performs wudu and wipes his neck with his hands will be protected from the yoke on the Day of Judgment.' (Reference: Al-Isaba, Bab Sunan al-Wudu, vol. 1, p. 34 / Sharh Ihya al-Ulum for Allama al-Zabidi, vol. 2, p. 365, Bab Kayfiyyat al-Wudu, I'la al-Sunan, vol. 1, p. 120) (2) From Lays (?) from Talha ibn Musarrif from his father from his grandfather that he saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) wipe his head until he reached the nape and what follows from the front of the neck. Commentary
This passage covers the ruling on wiping the neck (masah al-raqaba) during wudu. The author presents two hadiths: one from Ibn Umar promising protection from the yoke on Judgment Day, and another from a companion who saw the Prophet wiping the head including the nape. This makes it a mustahab act. The author then lists fourteen sunnan of wudu as mentioned by the author of the matn. Among them are washing hands three times to the wrists, saying Bismillah at the start, using miswak, rinsing mouth, sniffling water, wiping ears, combing beard, combing fingers, washing each limb three times, making intention for purification, wiping entire head, performing in order, starting with the right, and doing consecutively. Wiping the neck is listed separately as mustahab. This shows that the fourteen sunnan encompass all these actions, and neck wiping is an extra mustahab. The Hanafi position is that wiping the neck is mustahab, not sunnah, as it has weaker evidence.

Key Takeaway
Wiping the neck in wudu is a recommended (mustahab) act, supported by hadith but not obligatory.

Nullifiers of Wudu: Everything Exiting from the Two Passages
Ruling with Quranic and Hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that anything exiting from the front or back passage nullifies wudu and explain the proofs from Quran (5:6) and Hadith (Safwan ibn 'Assal).

Core Idea
Anything that exits from the front or back passage — even pure air — nullifies wudu.

This lesson introduces the first nullifier of wudu mentioned in the matn: anything that exits from the two passages (al-sabilayn). The text provides Quranic and Hadith proofs, establishing that any exit from the front or back, including wind, breaks wudu. The commentary clarifies the scope and addresses a common misunderstanding that only impure substances nullify wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The matn states: 'That which nullifies wudu is everything that comes out of the two passages.' Identify that 'the two passages' refer to the front (urethra) and back (anus).
The ruling is that any exit from these passages is a nullifier (naqid).
2
Examine the Quranic proof
The text cites Quran 5:6 'or one of you comes from the privy'. Analyze how this verse implies wudu is required after using the privy, which includes any exit from the two passages.
The phrase 'from the privy' (min al-gha'it) indicates the place where one relieves oneself.
3
Examine the Hadith proof
The text cites the hadith of Safwan ibn 'Assal where the Prophet exempts removing khuffs for 'gha'it, baul, and nawm'. Note that gha'it and baul are exits from the two passages, and the hadith does not restrict to impure substances.
The hadith shows that these acts break the state of purity requiring khuff removal, thus they are nullifiers.
4
Understand the qa'ida mentioned
The commentary adds a principle: when any impurity slides from its place and reaches the external body, wudu breaks. This is a broader principle, but the text focuses on the two passages.
This principle extends to other situations like bleeding from a wound, but the lesson's ruling is specific to the two passages.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school includes all exits (including wind). The Shafi'i school considers only najas (impure) substances as nullifiers. Identify the practical difference: for Hanafis, passing wind breaks wudu; for Shafi'is, it does not.
This difference arises from different interpretations of the proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نواقض کا بیان ضروری نوت المعانی الناقصة : وضو توڑنے والی چیزیں، جن نجاستوں کے نکلنے یا داخل ہونے سے وضو ٹوٹ جاتا ہے اس کا بیان ہے۔ (۲۰) وضو کو توڑنے والی ہر وہ چیز ہے جو پیشاب یا پاخانہ کے رستے سے نکلے۔ (۱) آیت میں ہے او جاء احد منكم من الغائط او لمستم النساء فلم تجدوا ماء فتيمموا صعيدا طيبا (ب)(آیت سورة المائدة (۵) پاخانہ کرنے کی وجہ سے پیشاب اور پاخانہ کے راستے سے پیشاب اور پاخانہ اور جو کچھ نکلے گا اس سے وضوٹوٹ جائے گا۔ آیت سے اس کا پتہ چلا (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن صفوان بن عسال قال رسول الله الله يأمرنا اذا كنا سفرا ان لا ننزع خفافنا ثلاثة ايام ولياليهن الا من جنابة ولكن من غائط و بول ونوم (ج) ترندی شریف ، باب امسح على الخفين للمسافر والمقيم ص ۲۷ نمبر ۹۶ رنسائی شریف، باب التوقیت فی المسح علی الخفین ہیں ۱۷ نمبر ۱۲۷) پاخانہ، پیشاب اور جنابت پاخانہ اور پیشاب کے راستے سے نکلتے ہیں اس لئے جو چیزیں بھی ان دونوں راستوں سے نکلے وہ ناقص وضو ہیں (۳) یہ دونوں مقام مقام نجاست نہیں ہیں ۔ نجاست کہیں اوپر سے کھسک کر آتی ہے۔ اور قاعدہ ہے کوئی ناپا کی اپنی جگہ سے کھسک کر جسم کے ظاہری حصے پر آجائے تو اس سے وضوٹوٹ جاتا ہے۔
Section on Nullifiers. Necessary Note: Matters that nullify: things that break wudu, from the exit or entry of impurities that cause wudu to break. (20) Every thing that breaks wudu is whatever comes out through the urinary or anal passage. (1) The verse: 'Or one of you comes from the privy, or you have touched women, and you find no water, then perform tayammum with clean earth' (Surah al-Ma'idah). Coming from the privy means that urine, stool, and whatever exits from these passages breaks wudu. This is understood from the verse. (2) Hadith: From Safwan ibn 'Assal: The Messenger of Allah commanded us that when we are on a journey, we not remove our khuffs for three days and nights except for janabah, but [we remove them] for relieving oneself, urination, and sleep. (Tirmidhi, Bab al-Mash 'ala al-Khuffayn, p. 27, no. 96; Nasa'i, Bab al-Tawqit fi al-Mash 'ala al-Khuffayn, p. 17, no. 127) Stool, urine, and janabah come out from the two passages, therefore whatever comes out of these two passages is a nullifier of wudu. (3) These two places are not places of impurity. Impurity slides down from above. And the principle is: when any impurity moves from its place and reaches the external part of the body, wudu breaks.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage introduces the section on nullifiers of wudu (nawaqid al-wudu). The matn states: 'That which nullifies wudu is everything that comes out of the two passages (al-sabilayn).' The commentary explains: the two passages are the front (urethra) and back (anus). Any substance that exits from them — urine, stool, wind, blood, pus, etc. — is a nullifier. The proof: Quran verse 5:6 mentions 'coming from the privy' (gha'it) which implies wudu is required after such acts. The hadith from Safwan ibn 'Assal shows that relieving oneself (gha'it), urine (baul), and sleep (nawm) break wudu (although sleep does not require removal of khuffs). The text clarifies that these passages themselves are not impure; the impurity comes from the body. The principle (qa'ida) stated: when any impurity moves from its original place and touches the external body, wudu is broken. This includes conditions like blood or pus exiting from other than the two passages? The text seems to focus on the two passages, but the principle may be broader. However, for this lesson, the ruling is specific: only exiting from the two passages is mentioned as the nullifier. The Hanafi view is that anything that exits from the front or back — including wind (fart) — breaks wudu. This is a key difference from some other schools like Shafi'i who consider only najas (impure) substances breaking wudu, not pure wind. But here the text states 'كل ما خرج' (everything that exits). So the Hanafi position is that even air exiting from the anus breaks wudu.

Key Terms
نواقض (nawaqid): Things that invalidate wudu.
سبیلین (sabilayn): The two passages: the front (urinary) and the back (anal).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in the text, which of the following breaks wudu?
A) Only urine and stool.
B) Only impure substances.
C) Everything that exits from the front or back passage, including wind.
D) Only substances that require removal of khuffs.

Key Takeaway
The first nullifier of wudu is anything that exits from the front or back passage, based on Quran 5:6 and the hadith of Safwan ibn 'Assal.

Blood, Pus, and Ichor: When Do They Nullify Wudu?
States conditions and proofs for blood nullifying wudu, and refutes opposing views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for blood nullifying wudu, apply it to examples, and evaluate the opposing Shafi'i/Maliki proof.

Core Idea
Flowing blood nullifies wudu only if it reaches a washable area – mere appearance or internal presence does not break it.

This passage from a Hanafi mutun commentary explains a crucial detail of wudu nullification: blood, pus, and ichor must flow to a place normally washed in wudu or ghusl. We'll examine the ruling, its evidence, and why the Shafi'i and Maliki schools disagree.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is ruled upon? The exit of blood, pus, or ichor from the body. The hukm: wudu becomes batil (void) if the substance flows to a 'mawdi' yalhaquhu hukm al-tathir'.
This condition is unique to Hanafis.
2
Locate the condition
The key term is 'mawdi' yalhaquhu hukm al-tathir': a place where washing is fard in wudu or ghusl. The text gives examples: outer ear, outer nose, etc.
Impurity inside a body cavity does not nullify wudu.
3
Find the dalil
Three proofs are cited: (1) the nosebleed hadith ordering wudu and building prayer, (2) the istihadah hadith of Fatimah bint Abi Hubaysh, (3) the explicit hadith 'al-wudu' min kulli dam sa'il'. Also the Quranic verse 6:145 declaring flowing blood najis.
These establish flowing blood as a nullifier.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik hold that blood does not break wudu at all, regardless of flow. They cite the action of Ubadah ibn al-Samit who prayed while bleeding from arrows.
This is a major cross-madhhab difference.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The text responds: the Companion's action is his own ijtihad; the Prophet's explicit hadith takes precedence. Also, he may have been ma'dhur (excused) due to continuous bleeding, or the blood only appeared without flowing.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text

(۲۱) والدم والقيح والصديد وت یہ چیزیں پیشاب کے رستے سے نکلتی ہیں (۱) پیشاب (۲) ندی (۳) ودی (۴) منی (۵) حیض (۶) نفاس (۷) استحاضہ ۔ اور یہ چیزیں پاخانہ کے راستے سے نکلتی ہیں (۱) پاخانہ (۲) ہوا (۳) پاخانہ کا کیڑا۔ ان کے نکلنے سے وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ (۲۱) خون، پیپ اور کیچ لہو جب بدن سے نکلے اور ایسی جگہ تک پہنچ جائے جس کو پاکی کا حکم لاحق ہوتا ہے ( تو وضوٹوٹ جائے گا ) موضع يلحقه حكم التطهير : یہ فقہ کا ایک محاورہ ہے۔ اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ خون، پیپ وغیرہ جب تک بدن کے اندر ہوں تو اس سے وضو نہیں ٹو تھا جب تک کہ بہہ کر بدن سے باہر نہ نکل جائے اور ایسی جگہ نہ آجائے جہاں آسانی سے ہاتھ سے دھویا جا سکے۔ مثلا کان کے اندر پیپ ہو تو وضو نہیں ٹوٹی گا۔ لیکن اگر کان کے سوراخ میں باہر کی طرف پیپ بہہ کر آ جائے جہاں انگلی سے آسانی سے پو نچھا اور دھویا جا سکتا ہے تو اب وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ ناک منہ، کان ، پیشاب، شرمگاہ اور پاخانہ کے اندر ناپاکی ہو تو وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا لیکن باہر کی طرف آ جائے جہاں آسانی کے ساتھ انگلی سے ناپا کی کو پونچھا اور دھویا جا سکتا ہے تو اب وضوٹوٹ جائیگا۔ کیونکہ نا پا کی ایسی جگہ نکل کر آگئی جہاں غنسل میں یا وضو میں دھونا فرض ہوتا ہے۔ انہیں مقامات کو موضع يلحقه حكم التطهير " کہتے ہیں۔

یں چوٹ لگی اور خون صرف ظاہر ہوا اپنی جگہ سے بہا اور کھسکا نہیں تو وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ اس لئے کہ صرف خون کا ظہور ہوا ہے۔ خون ابھی بہا نہیں ہے۔ بہتا ہوا خون ناپاک ہے اور وضو توڑتا ہے۔ قرآن میں ہے و دما مسفوحا او لحم خنزیر فانه رجس (الف)( آیت ۱۴۵ ،سورۃ الانعام ۶) اس لئے اگر زخم پر خون ظاہر ہوا ہو لیکن اپنی جگہ سے کھسکا نہ ہو تو وضو نہیں ٹوٹی گا۔ ہاں اگر خون اتنا بہ رہا تھا کہ اپنی جگہ سے کھسک سکتا تھا لیکن بار بار پونچھ دیا گیا جس کی وجہ سے خون نہ بہہ سکا تو وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ کیونکہ بہنے اور کھسکنے کے قابل خون تھا وت اگر مسلسل خون بہہ رہا ہو کہ وضو کر کے نماز پڑھنے کا موقع نہ ملتا ہو اور اس حالت پر ایک دن اور ایک رات گزر گئے ہوں تو اب وہ معذور کے حکم میں ہے۔ اس لئے اب اس کا خون بہنے سے نماز کے وقت میں وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ معذور ہو گیا۔ خون سے وضو ٹوٹنے کی اجہ (1) حدیث میں ہے نکسیر پھوٹے تو وضو کرو اور نماز پر بنا کرو۔ عن عائشة قالت قال رسول الله الله من اصابه قيء او رعاف او قلس او مذى فـلـيـنـصرف فليتوضأ ثم ليبين على صلواته وهو في ذالك لا يتكلم (ب) ( ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب ما جاء فی البناء علی الصلوۃ ص ۱۷۱ نمبر ۱۲۲۱ ردار قطنی ، باب فی الوضوء من الخارج من البدن ، ج ، اول، ص ۱۶۰، نمبر ۵۵۵) رعاف یعنی نکسیر پھوٹنا اور خون کا نکلنا ہے۔ اس سے وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ اس لئے دوبارہ وضو کر کے اس پر نماز کی بنا کرے بشرطیکہ درمیان میں بات نہ کی ہو ۔ (۲) حدیث ہے جاءت فاطمة ابنة ابي حبيش الى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت یا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم انی امراة استحاض فلا اطهر أفادع الصلوة ؟ فقال رسول الله الله لا انما ذلك عرق وليس بحيض فاذا اقبلت حيضتك فدعي الصلوة واذا ادبرت فاغسلى عنك الدم ثم صلى وقال ابى ثم توضأى لكل صلوة (ج) ( بخاری حاشیہ : (الف) بہتا ہوا خون اور سور کا گوشت تو یقین نا پاک ہے۔ (ب) آپ نے فرمایا جس کو قے ہوئی ہو یا نکسیر پھوٹی ہو پاتے ہوئی یا ندی نکلی ہو اس کو واپس جانا چاہئے اور وضو کرنا چاہئے پھر اپنی نماز پر بنا کرنا چاہئے۔ یہ اس وقت ہے کہ درمیان میں بات نہ کی ہو۔ (ج) فاطمہ بنت جیش نے حضور کے باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )س
اذا خرج من البدن فتجاوز الى موضع يلحقه حكم الطهارة شریف ، باب غسل الدم ص ۳۶ نمبر (۲۲۸) نوٹ عرق سے مرادرگ سے نکلنے والے اور خون کی طرح اس کا حکم ہے ۔ حیض کے خون کا حکم نہیں ہے (۳) قال رسول الله الله الوضوء من كل دم سائل (الف) (دار قطنی، باب فی الوضوء من الخارج من البدن ص ۶۳ نمبر (۵۷) پیپ اور کیچ لہو بھی خون کی قسمیں ہیں اور خون ہی سے بنتے ہیں۔ اس لئے ان کے نکلنے سے بھی وضوٹوٹ جائیگا۔
وہ
فائدہ امام شافعی اور امام مالک رحمۃ اللہ علیھما کے نزدیک خون، پیپ بدن سے نکلے تو وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ (1) غزوہ ذات رقاع میں عبادہ بن بشر کو تیر مارا اور وہ نماز پڑھتے رہے اور خون بہتا رہا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ خون بہنے سے وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا ورنہ وہ خون نکلتے ہی نماز توڑ دیتے۔ روایت میں ہے کہ حتی رماه بثلاثة اسهم ثم ركع وسجد ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب الوضوء من الدم ص ۲۹ نمبر ۱۹۸) اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ صحابی کا اپنا نفعل ہے حضور کو وضو ٹوٹنے کی اطلاع نہیں تھی (۲) امام شافعی کے یہاں خون بدن پر لگنے سے وضو ٹوٹ جاتا ہے تو جب بہا ہوگا تو خون بدن پر لگا ہی ہوگا جس سے ان کے یہاں بھی اس فعل سے وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ ان کا دوسرا استدلال یہ ہے کہ صحابہ کو جہاد میں زخم ہوتا تھا اور وہ نماز پڑھتے رہتے تھے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ خون ناقص نہیں ہے۔ پوری تفصیل بخاری باب من لم ير الوضاء الامن المخرجين من القبل والد برص ۲۹ نمبر ۱۷۶ تا ۱۸۰ میں دیکھیں۔ ہم جواب دیتے ہیں یا تو مسلسل خون بہنے سے و معذور کے حکم میں تھے یا خون صرف زخم پر ظاہر ہوتا تھا بہتا نہیں تھا اور خون ظاہر ہونے سے وضو ہمارے یہاں بھی نہیں ٹو نما جیسا کہ اوپر گزر گیا التح : پیپ، الصدید : کچ لہو، ایسا پیپ جس میں خون کی آمیزش ہو، تجاوز : بہہ پڑے، کھسک جائے۔
And blood, pus, and ichor. And these things exit from the urethra: (1) urine, (2) madhi (pre-ejaculate), (3) wadi (post-urine discharge), (4) mani (semen), (5) menstruation, (6) postpartum bleeding, (7) istihadah. And these things exit from the anus: (1) stool, (2) wind, (3) intestinal worms. Their exit breaks wudu. (21) Blood, pus, and ichor: when they exit the body and reach a place to which the ruling of purification applies, then wudu breaks. 'Mawdi' yalhaquhu hukm al-tathir': this is a legal idiom. Its meaning is that as long as blood, pus, etc. are inside the body, wudu does not break until they flow out of the body and come to a place that can be easily washed by hand. For example, if pus is inside the ear, wudu does not break. But if in the ear hole the pus flows outward to where it can be easily wiped and washed with a finger, then wudu breaks. If impurity is inside the nose, mouth, ear, urethra, vagina, or anus, wudu does not break, but if it comes outward to where it can be easily wiped and washed with a finger, then wudu breaks, because the impurity has come out to a place where washing is fard in ghusl or wudu. Those places are called 'mawdi' yalhaquhu hukm al-tathir'.
If one is injured and blood appears but does not flow or move from its place, then wudu does not break, because only the appearance of blood has occurred; it has not flowed. Flowing blood is najis and breaks wudu. Allah says: 'or flowing blood or the flesh of swine, for indeed it is filth' (Surah al-An'am 6:145). So if blood appears on a wound but has not moved from its place, wudu does not break. Yes, if blood was flowing so much that it could move from its place, but it was repeatedly wiped away so that it did not flow, then wudu breaks because the blood was capable of flowing and moving. And if blood flows continuously such that there is no opportunity to perform wudu and pray, and this condition lasts for a day and a night, then such a person is ruled as excused. Therefore, from that point, his wudu does not break by the flowing blood during the prayer time because he has become excused. The proof for wudu breaking from blood: (1) Hadith: 'If a nosebleed occurs, then perform wudu and build upon your prayer.' [from Aisha ra, the Prophet said: Whoever is afflicted with vomiting, nosebleed, regurgitation, or madhi should go back, perform wudu, then build upon his prayer as long as he does not speak in between.] (Ibn Majah, Bab al-Bina' ala al-Salah, p.171 no.1221; Dar Qutni, Bab al-Wudu min al-Kharij, v.1 p.160 no.555) Nosebleed (ru'af) means blood exiting the nose. This breaks wudu, so one should repeat wudu and build upon the prayer provided he has not spoken in between. (2) Hadith: 'Fatimah bint Abi Hubaysh came to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who has istihadah and I do not become pure; shall I leave the prayer? He said: No, that is only a vein and is not menstruation. When your menstruation comes, leave the prayer; when it ends, wash off the blood from yourself and pray. My father said: Then perform wudu for every prayer.' (Bukhari, Bab Ghasi al-Dam, p.36 no.228) Note: 'Irq' means from a vein, and its ruling is like that of blood, not like menstrual blood. (3) The Prophet said: 'Wudu is from every flowing blood.' (Dar Qutni, Bab al-Wudu min al-Kharij, p.63 no.57) Pus and ichor are also types of blood and are formed from blood, so their exit also breaks wudu.
Benefit: According to Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik, if blood or pus exits the body, wudu does not break. (1) In the Ghazwah of Dhat al-Riqa', Ubadah ibn al-Samit was hit by an arrow and he continued praying while blood flowed. This indicates that flowing blood does not break wudu, otherwise he would have broken his prayer when the blood exited. The tradition says: '...until he was hit with three arrows, then he bowed and prostrated.' (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Wudu min al-Dam, p.29 no.198) The answer is that this is the Companion's own action; the Prophet was not informed of the nullification. (2) According to Imam al-Shafi'i, if blood touches the body, wudu breaks; so when blood flows, it would touch the body, and thus in his school, this action would break wudu. Their second argument is that Companions would be wounded in jihad and would continue praying, indicating that blood is not a nullifier. See full details in Bukhari, Bab man lam yara al-wudu' illa min al-makhrajayn, p.29 nos.176-180. We respond: either they were ruled as excused due to continuous bleeding, or the blood only appeared on the wound and did not flow; even in our school, appearance of blood without flow does not break wudu, as passed above. The explanation: al-qayh: pus, al-sadeed: ichor, pus mixed with blood, tujawuz: to flow over, to move.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn regarding nullifiers of wudu, specifically addressing blood, pus, and ichor. The author first states the general list of nullifiers from the urethra and anus, then focuses on item (21): blood, pus, and ichor. The key condition is that they must exit the body and reach a place to which the ruling of purification applies (mawdi' yalhaquhu hukm al-tathir). This is a Hanafi technical term meaning a place that is washed during wudu or ghusl, i.e., an external body surface that can be easily cleaned. For example, pus inside the ear does not break wudu, but once it flows out to the ear canal where it can be wiped, wudu breaks. The author then explains that mere appearance of blood on a wound does not break wudu unless it flows from its place. He cites the Quranic verse (6:145) to establish that flowing blood is najis, and then provides hadith evidence: (1) the hadith on nosebleed commanding wudu and building upon prayer, (2) the hadith of Fatimah bint Abi Hubaysh commanding wudu for each prayer in istihadah, and (3) the explicit hadith 'Wudu is from every flowing blood'. The commentary also notes that if a person has continuous bleeding such that no time remains for wudu and prayer, and this continues for a day and night, he is considered excused (ma'dhur) and his wudu does not break from each occurrence. Finally, the passage presents a benefit (fa'idah) discussing the Shafi'i and Maliki positions that blood does not nullify wudu. They cite the action of Ubadah ibn al-Samit who prayed while bleeding from arrows. The Hanafi response is that this was his own ijtihad and that the Prophet's explicit hadith takes precedence. They also argue that in Shafi'i's own school, if blood touches the body it breaks wudu, so the action would actually break wudu by that logic. The second argument of the Companions being wounded in jihad is answered by either the excuse of continuous bleeding or that the blood only appeared without flowing, which even Hanafis do not consider a nullifier. The passage concludes with a glossary explaining the terms.

Key Terms
موضع يلحقه حكم التطهير (mawdi' yalhaquhu hukm al-tathir): A place to which the ruling of purification applies, i.e., an external body surface that is washed in wudu or ghusl, such as the outside of the ear, nose, etc.
معذور (ma'dhur): An excused person who has continuous bleeding or other impurity that lasts for a complete day and night, such that he cannot maintain wudu; his wudu does not break with each occurrence.
رعاف (ru'af): Nosebleed; blood exiting the nose.
استحاضة (istihadah): Non-menstrual uterine bleeding; continuous bleeding from a vein.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does blood nullify wudu?
A) When it exits the body at all
B) When it flows to a place where washing is fard (mawdi' yalhaquhu hukm al-tathir)
C) When it is more than a dirham in size
D) When it appears on the skin

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, blood, pus, and ichor only break wudu when they flow to a place that is washed during wudu or ghusl.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Vomit Nullifies Wudu When It Fills the Mouth
Provides the Hanafi ruling on vomit as a nullifier of wudu with conditions and proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for vomit to nullify wudu in the Hanafi school and explain the hadith evidence and reconciliation of contradictory narrations.

Core Idea
Vomit nullifies wudu only if it fills the mouth — the exit of impurity from the lower stomach.

In this lesson, we examine the twenty-second nullifier of wudu: vomit (qay'). The Hanafi ruling is conditional: only vomit that fills the mouth (mala' al-fam) breaks wudu. The reasoning is based on the origin of the vomit — lower stomach (impure) vs. upper stomach (pure) — and on reconciling hadiths that seem contradictory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Vomit nullifies wudu when it fills the mouth; less than a mouthful does not.
2
Understand the reasoning
The mouthful comes from lower stomach where food is impure; the exit of impurity nullifies wudu. Less than mouthful comes from upper stomach where food is still pure.
3
Examine the dalil
The hadith of Abu Darda' shows the Prophet performed wudu after vomiting, confirmed by Thawban.
4
Reconcile contradictory hadiths
Another hadith shows the Prophet did not perform wudu after vomiting; reconciliation is based on the quantity of vomit.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position is that a mouthful nullifies; this is the relied-upon ruling.

Source Text

(۲۲) والقيء اذا كان ملأ الفم ( تو وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا ) (۱) جوتے منہ بھر کے ہو وہ پیٹ کے نچلے حصے سے آتی ہے جہاں غذا نجاست بن چکی ہوتی ہے۔ اور نجاست کا نکلنا ناقض وضو ہے اس لئے منہ بھر کے قے سے وضوٹوٹ جائے گا۔ اور جوتے منہ بھر کر نہ ہو وہ پیٹ کے اوپر کے حصے سے آتی ہے جہاں غذا ابھی نجاست نہیں بنی ہوتی ہے اس لئے وہ پاک ہے۔ اس لئے منہ بھر کرتے نہ ہو تو اس سے وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ (۲) بعض حدیث میں ہے کہ وضوٹوٹے گا اور بعض حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ آپ کو قے ہوئی اور آپ نے وضو نہیں فرمایا تو یہ احادیث اس پر محمول کی جائیں گی کہ جس میں وضو کیا وہ منہ بھر کر تے تھی اور جس میں وضو نہیں کیا وہ منہ بھر کر نہیں تھی (۳) حدیث یہ ہے عن ابی درداء رضی الله عنه ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قاء وجه فتوضأ فلقيت ثوبان في مسجد دمشق فذكرت ذالك له فقال صدق انا صببت له وضوءه (ب) (ترمذی شریف، باب الوضوء من القىء والرعاف ص ۲۵ نمبر ۸۷) (۴) مسئلہ نمبر ۲۱ میں ابن ماجہ کی حدیث گزری جس میں تھا کہ قے سے وضو ٹوٹتا ہے۔اس حدیث
And vomit when it fills the mouth. (1) That which fills the mouth comes from the lower part of the stomach where the food has become impure. And the exit of impurity nullifies wudu, so vomit that fills the mouth breaks wudu. And that which does not fill the mouth comes from the upper part of the stomach where the food has not yet become impure, so it is pure. Therefore, if it does not fill the mouth, wudu does not break. (2) There is a hadith that it breaks wudu, and another hadith indicates that the Prophet vomited and did not perform wudu. So these hadiths are interpreted such that the one in which he performed wudu was when the vomit filled the mouth, and the one in which he did not was when it did not fill the mouth. (3) The hadith is from Abu Darda': 'The Prophet vomited and performed wudu. I met Thawban in the mosque of Damascus and mentioned this to him, and he said: He told the truth; I poured out water for his wudu.' (Tirmidhi, Bab al-Wudu min al-Qay' wa al-Ru'af, p.25 no.87) (4) In issue no.21, the hadith of Ibn Majah passed that vomit breaks wudu. This hadith...
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of nullifiers of wudu, now addressing item (22): vomit (qay'). The ruling given is that vomit nullifies wudu only if it fills the mouth (mala' al-fam). The reasoning is anatomical: vomit that fills the mouth comes from the lower stomach where digestion has progressed and the food has become impure; therefore, its exit is the exit of impurity, which nullifies wudu. Vomit that does not fill the mouth comes from the upper stomach where food is still in a pure state, so it is considered pure and does not nullify wudu. The author then reconciles apparently contradictory hadiths: one indicates that the Prophet performed wudu after vomiting, and another indicates he did not. The reconciliation is based on the quantity: when he performed wudu, the vomit filled the mouth; when he did not, it was less than a mouthful. The primary hadith cited is that of Abu Darda', where the Prophet vomited and then performed wudu, and Thawban confirmed that he provided water for his wudu. This hadith is used as evidence that vomit nullifies wudu when it is a mouthful. The passage ends referencing the hadith from Ibn Majah mentioned earlier in item (21), which also states that vomit breaks wudu, but the text cuts off before completing the point.

Key Terms
ملأ الفم (mala' al-fam): A mouthful; the quantity of vomit that fills the mouth. It is the threshold for nullification of wudu in the Hanafi school.
قئ (qay'): Vomit; the ejection of stomach contents through the mouth. In Hanafi terminology, it is a nullifier of wudu only when it fills the mouth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does vomit nullify wudu according to the Hanafi school?
A) Whenever some vomit exits
B) When it fills the mouth
C) When it comes from the upper stomach
D) When it is mixed with food

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, vomit nullifies wudu only when it fills the mouth; less than a mouthful does not.

Flowing Blood and Pus Break Wudu: Hanafi vs Shafi'i/Maliki
Inter-madhhab dispute on nullification of wudu by blood/pus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on flowing blood and pus breaking wudu, cite the primary proof, and evaluate the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i/Maliki objections.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, flowing blood and pus break wudu; the Shafi'i/Maliki position disagrees but is refuted by explicit hadith.

This passage addresses a classical inter-madhhab dispute: does the exit of blood or pus from the body invalidate wudu? The Hanafi school holds that it does, relying on the hadith 'Wudu is from every flowing blood.' The Shafi'i and Maliki schools disagree, citing the practice of Companions. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh proofs and identify the operative ruling in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: the exit of flowing blood, pus, and ichor from the body invalidates wudu. Note that menstrual blood has a separate ruling.
The nullifier is the act of exiting, not the substance itself.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik hold that blood and pus do not break wudu, regardless of whether they flow.
This is a mukhtalaf fih issue across madhhabs.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
They cite the incident of Ubada ibn al-Samit who prayed while bleeding, and the general practice of Companions in jihad who continued praying while wounded.
These are actions of individuals, not explicit textual proofs.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes: Ubada's action was his own ijtihad (not reported to the Prophet), and the Companions in jihad were either continuously bleeding (ma'dhur) or only had blood appear without flowing, which does not break wudu even in the Hanafi school.
The response also points out that according to Shafi'i's own principle, blood touching the body breaks wudu, so the incident would actually support wudu being broken.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in the Hanafi school, if blood flows and one intentionally continues prayer, the prayer is invalid. In the Shafi'i/Maliki school, the prayer remains valid.
This affects whether one must repeat the prayer after renewing wudu.

فائدہ امام شافعی اور امام مالک رحمۃ اللہ علیھما کے نزدیک خون، پیپ بدن سے نکلے تو وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ (1) غزوہ ذات رقاع میں عبادہ بن بشر کو تیر مارا اور وہ نماز پڑھتے رہے اور خون بہتا رہا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ خون بہنے سے وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا ورنہ وہ خون نکلتے ہی نماز توڑ دیتے۔ روایت میں ہے کہ حتی رماه بثلاثة اسهم ثم ركع وسجد ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب الوضوء من الدم ص ۲۹ نمبر ۱۹۸) اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ صحابی کا اپنا نفعل ہے حضور کو وضو ٹوٹنے کی اطلاع نہیں تھی (۲) امام شافعی کے یہاں خون بدن پر لگنے سے وضو ٹوٹ جاتا ہے تو جب بہا ہوگا تو خون بدن پر لگا ہی ہوگا جس سے ان کے یہاں بھی اس فعل سے وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ ان کا دوسرا استدلال یہ ہے کہ صحابہ کو جہاد میں زخم ہوتا تھا اور وہ نماز پڑھتے رہتے تھے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ خون ناقص نہیں ہے۔ پوری تفصیل بخاری باب من لم ير الوضاء الامن المخرجين من القبل والد برص ۲۹ نمبر ۱۷۶ تا ۱۸۰ میں دیکھیں۔ ہم جواب دیتے ہیں یا تو مسلسل خون بہنے سے و معذور کے حکم میں تھے یا خون صرف زخم پر ظاہر ہوتا تھا بہتا نہیں تھا اور خون ظاہر ہونے سے وضو ہمارے یہاں بھی نہیں ٹوٹتا جیسا کہ اوپر گزر گیا

التح : پیپ، الصدید : کچ لہو، ایسا پیپ جس میں خون کی آمیزش ہو، تجاوز : بہہ پڑے، کھسک جائے۔
