If something exits the body and reaches a place subject to the ruling of purity (22). Section on washing blood. Page 36, number (228). Note: Sweat is what exits from the vein and its ruling is like blood. The ruling of menstrual blood is not (the same). (3) The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Wudu is (required) from every flowing blood.' (a) (Dar Qutni, chapter on wudu from that which exits the body, p. 63, no. 57). Pus and ichorous blood are also types of blood and are formed from blood. Therefore, their exiting also breaks wudu.

Benefit: According to Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik (may Allah have mercy on them), if blood or pus exits the body, wudu does not break. (1) In the Ghazwah of Dhat al-Riqa', Ubada ibn al-Samit was struck by an arrow and he continued praying while blood flowed. This indicates that flowing blood does not break wudu, otherwise he would have broken the prayer when the blood exited. The narration states: 'until he was hit with three arrows, then he bowed and prostrated' (Abu Dawud, chapter on wudu from blood, p. 29, no. 198). The answer to this is that this was the Companion's own action; he did not inform the Prophet (ﷺ) that wudu was broken. (2) According to Imam al-Shafi'i, when blood touches the body, wudu breaks. So when blood flows, it certainly touches the body, so in his school too, this action would break wudu. Their second argument is that the Companions would be wounded in jihad and would continue praying. This shows that blood is not a nullifier. See full details in Bukhari, chapter: 'Who did not see wudu except from the two exits...' p. 29, nos. 176-180. We respond: either due to continuous bleeding they were in the ruling of excused persons, or the blood only appeared on the wound without flowing, and according to us blood appearing (without flowing) does not break wudu as previously mentioned.

Al-Madd: pus; as-sadeed: ichor, pus mixed with blood; tajaawaza: to flow, to move.

Footnote: (continued from previous page) She said: O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who has istihadah (chronic bleeding) and do not become pure. Should I leave prayer? He said: No. This is only blood from a vein and is not menstruation. So when your period comes, leave prayer, and when it ends, wash the blood and pray. My father said: Perform wudu for every prayer. (a) Wudu is from every flowing blood. (b) He vomited and then performed wudu. Then I met Thawban in the mosque of Damascus and mentioned this, and he said: He spoke the truth; I poured the water for his wudu.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute over whether the exit of blood, pus, and similar fluids breaks wudu. The Hanafi position is that any flowing blood (dam sa'il) and its derivatives like pus (madd) and ichor (sadeed) break wudu. The proof is the hadith 'Wudu is from every flowing blood' (al-wudu' min kulli dam sa'il). Menstrual blood is excluded because it has a separate ruling (istihadah is discussed in the footnote). The Shafi'i and Maliki schools argue that wudu is not broken by blood or pus exiting the body. They cite the incident of Ubada ibn al-Samit who prayed while bleeding from arrows. The Hanafi response distinguishes that the Companion's action was his own ijtihad; the Prophet was not informed. Also, according to Shafi'i's own principle, blood touching the body would break wudu, so the incident would actually support wudu breaking. Another argument from the opponents about the general practice of Companions in jihad is answered by either the condition of continuous bleeding (ma'dhur) or that blood was only visible on the wound without flowing. The footnote clarifies istihadah (chronic non-menstrual bleeding) as distinct from menstrual blood, citing the hadith of Fatima bint Abi Hubaysh and the instruction to perform wudu for each prayer. This supports the Hanafi position that flowing blood breaks wudu, while also specifying exceptions.

Key Terms
دم سائل (dam sā'il): Flowing blood that exits the body, as opposed to blood that merely appears on the skin without flowing.
الصدید (as-ṣadīd): Ichor: thin, watery pus mixed with blood that oozes from wounds.
مستحاضہ (mustaḥāḍah): A woman suffering from istihadah (chronic, non-menstrual uterine bleeding).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It breaks wudu because it is a form of flowing blood.
B) It does not break wudu because it is not blood.
C) It breaks wudu only if it reaches a place subject to purity.
D) It breaks wudu only if it is mixed with blood.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that flowing blood and pus break wudu, supported by the hadith 'al-wudu' min kulli dam sa'il,' and the Shafi'i/Maliki objection is rebutted by distinguishing flowing from non-flowing blood.

Vomiting and Wudu: The Mouthful Distinction and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on vomiting and wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on vomiting and wudu, identify the condition of a mouthful, and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i/Maliki objection.

Core Idea
Vomiting a mouthful breaks wudu; less does not — distinction based on stomach source determines purity.

Does vomiting break wudu? The answer differs among schools. In this passage, the Hanafi position is clarified with a precise condition: only a mouthful from the lower stomach nullifies wudu. The author also addresses the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik, reconciling apparent contradictions in the hadith. Let's examine the reasoning and evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: vomiting a mouthful breaks wudu; less than a mouthful does not. Note the distinction based on stomach source (lower vs upper).
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik hold that vomiting does not break wudu at all. Their main proof is an athar from al-Hasan: 'There is no wudu from vomiting.'
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the athar and the reports that the Prophet (ﷺ) vomited without performing wudu. Understand why the other school considers all vomiting as not nullifying.
The opponent relies on apparent absence of wudu after vomiting.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school reconciles the conflicting narrations by interpreting the mouthful condition. The hadith of Abu Darda (Prophet vomited and performed wudu) is taken as evidence for mouthful vomit. The narrations without wudu are understood as less than a mouthful or delayed wudu.
Also, the source of vomit (lower stomach impurity) supports the distinction.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: In the Hanafi school, if a person vomits a mouthful, wudu is broken. In the Shafi'i and Maliki schools, wudu remains intact regardless of the amount. Also, phlegm does not break wudu in Hanafi.
This difference affects daily worship preparedness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۲) اور قے جب کہ منہ بھر کے ہو ( تو وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا ) (۱) جب قے منہ بھر کے ہو وہ پیٹ کے نچلے حصے سے آتی ہے جہاں غذا نجاست بن چکی ہوتی ہے۔ اور نجاست کا نکلنا ناقض وضو ہے اس لئے منہ بھر کے قے سے وضوٹوٹ جائے گا۔ اور قے منہ بھر کر نہ ہو وہ پیٹ کے اوپر کے حصے سے آتی ہے جہاں غذا ابھی نجاست نہیں بنی ہوتی ہے اس لئے وہ پاک ہے۔ اس لئے منہ بھر کر نہ ہو تو اس سے وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ (۲) بعض حدیث میں ہے کہ وضوٹوٹے گا اور بعض حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ آپ کو قے ہوئی اور آپ نے وضو نہیں فرمایا تو یہ احادیث اس پر محمول کی جائیں گی کہ جس میں وضو کیا وہ منہ بھر کر تھی اور جس میں وضو نہیں کیا وہ منہ بھر کر نہیں تھی (۳) حدیث یہ ہے عن ابی درداء رضی الله عنه ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قاء فتوضأ فلقيت ثوبان في مسجد دمشق فذكرت ذالك له فقال صدق انا صببت له وضوءه (ب) (ترمذی شریف، باب الوضوء من القىء والرعاف ص ۲۵ نمبر ۸۷) (۴) مسئلہ نمبر ۲۱ میں ابن ماجہ کی حدیث گزری جس میں تھا کہ قے سے وضو ٹوٹتا ہے۔

سے معلوم ہوا کہ قی سے وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا۔

نام امام شافعی اور امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ قے سے وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ کیونکہ آپ نے قے کی اور وضو نہیں کیا۔ ان کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ عن الحسن قال ليس في المفلس وضوء (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الوضوء من التنى والفلس ، ج اول ص ۱۳۸، نمبر ۵۲۳ ) ہم جواب دیتے ہیں کہ ہوسکتا ہے کہ وہ منہ بھر کرتے نہ ہو۔ یا منھ بھر کر ہو گا فوری طور پر وضو نہیں کیا بعد میں وضو کیا ہو گا اگر چہ وضو ٹوٹ گیا تھا۔ نو بلغم وغیرہ کی قے ہو تو اس سے وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا کیونکہ بلغم پر نجاست نہیں ہوتی اور نہ وہ پیٹ کے نچلے حصے سے آتا ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عمار بن ياسر ... قال يدعمار ! ما نخامتك ودموع عينيك والماء الذي في ركوتك الاسواء (دارقطني باب نجاسة البول والامر بالنزہ منہ الخ ، ج اول ص ۱۳۴ نمبر ۴۵۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بلغم پانی کے ملنے کی طرح پاک ہے۔
(22) And vomiting when it fills the mouth (then wudu breaks). (1) When vomit fills the mouth, it comes from the lower part of the stomach where food has become impure. The exit of impurity is a nullifier of wudu, so vomiting a mouthful breaks wudu. And if vomit does not fill the mouth, it comes from the upper part of the stomach where food has not yet become impure, so it is pure. Therefore, if it does not fill the mouth, wudu does not break. (2) Some hadiths indicate that wudu breaks, and some hadiths show that the Prophet (ﷺ) vomited and did not perform wudu. These hadiths are reconciled by the interpretation that the hadith where wudu was performed was for a mouthful vomit, and where wudu was not performed was for less than a mouthful. (3) The hadith from Abu Darda (may Allah be pleased with him): 'The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) vomited and performed wudu.' I met Thawban in the mosque of Damascus and mentioned this to him. He said, 'He spoke the truth; I poured the water for his wudu.' (Tirmidhi, Bab al-Wudu' min al-Qay' wa al-Ru'af, p. 25, no. 87). (4) In issue no. 21, the hadith of Ibn Majah passed which stated that vomiting breaks wudu.

From this it is known that vomiting breaks wudu.

Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik say that vomiting does not break wudu, because the Prophet (ﷺ) vomited and did not perform wudu. Their evidence is the athar from al-Hasan: 'There is no wudu due to vomiting' (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Wudu' min al-Tanay wa al-Fals, vol. 1 p. 138 no. 523). We respond: It is possible that the vomit was not a mouthful, or if it was a mouthful, he may have performed wudu later even if wudu was broken. Also, if phlegm or similar matter is vomited, wudu does not break because phlegm is not impure and it does not come from the lower stomach. (2) There is a hadith from 'Ammar ibn Yasir... saying: 'O 'Ammar! Your phlegm, the tears of your eyes, and the water in your vessel are all equivalent.' (Dar Qutni, chapter on the impurity of urine etc., vol. 1 p. 134 no. 452). This hadith indicates that phlegm is pure like water.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute over whether vomiting breaks wudu. The Hanafi position distinguishes between vomit that fills the mouth (mul' al-fam) and less than that. A mouthful of vomit comes from the lower stomach where food has become impure (najis), so its exit is a nullifier. Less than a mouthful comes from the upper stomach, where food is still pure, so wudu does not break. The proof is the hadith of Abu Darda and Thawban that the Prophet (ﷺ) vomited and performed wudu, and the hadith of Ibn Majah (referenced) that vomiting breaks wudu. The opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik relies on an athar from al-Hasan that there is no wudu from vomiting, and on reports that the Prophet (ﷺ) vomited without performing wudu. The Hanafi response reconciles the conflicting reports by differentiating between mouthful and less. The passage also clarifies that phlegm (balgham) does not break wudu because it is not impure and comes from the upper respiratory tract. The hadith of 'Ammar ibn Yasir is cited to show that phlegm is pure. This ruling highlights the Hanafi method of reconciling apparently contradictory hadith based on the distinction of condition (mouthful vs. less).

Key Terms
قے (qay'): Vomiting; the expulsion of stomach contents through the mouth.
بلغم (balgham): Phlegm; a viscous secretion from the respiratory tract, not from the stomach.
ملأ الفم (mul' al-fam): A mouthful; an amount of vomit that fills the mouth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, when does vomiting break wudu?
A) Only when the vomit fills the mouth and comes from the lower stomach.
B) Whenever there is any amount of vomit, regardless of source.
C) Only if the vomit is mixed with blood.
D) Vomiting never breaks wudu.

Key Takeaway
Vomiting breaks wudu only when it fills the mouth, indicating it comes from the lower stomach where food has become impure.

Deep Sleep vs. Light Sleep: The Hanafi Criterion for Wudu
Explains when sleep and unconsciousness break wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish deep sleep (wudu-breaking) from light sleep (non-breaking) and apply the Hanafi criterion of istirkhā' al-mafāṣil.

Core Idea
Deep sleep that relaxes joints breaks wudu; dozing where awareness remains does not.

This passage establishes a practical distinction for the Muslim: not all sleep invalidates wudu. The Hanafi school uses the physical sign of joint relaxation to determine when wudu must be renewed, supported by hadith evidence and the principle of loss of intellect (ghalaba 'alā al-'aql).

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
The root cause is the complete removal of intellect (ghalaba 'alā al-'aql), making it impossible to know if wind was released.
This is the legal basis for deeming wudu broken.
2
Recognize the physical indicator
The physical sign of deep sleep is relaxation of joints (istirkhā' al-mafāṣil), which occurs when lying on the side or leaning such that removal of support would cause a fall.
If joints are not relaxed, the sleep is light.
3
Distinguish sleep positions
Positions that cause joint relaxation: lying on side, leaning against a support. Light sleep positions: sitting, standing, bowing, prostrating where awareness remains.
The key is whether the person would fall if support is removed.
4
Understand the dalil
Hadith of 'Ali (wudu required after sleep) is specified by the hadith of sleeping on side (wudu only when joints relax). This is a case of takhsīs (specification).
The second hadith qualifies the first.
5
Apply to practical scenarios
If someone sleeps in a chair leaning back and would fall if the chair were taken, wudu breaks. If they doze sitting upright, wudu remains.
Always check for complete loss of awareness and joint relaxation.

(۲۳) والنوم مضطجعا او متكأ او مستندا الى شيء لو ازيل لسقط عنه والغلبة على العقل ( ان چیزوں سے وضو ٹوٹ جاتا ہے) (۱) اصل یہ ہے کہ گہری نیند سے یا پاگل پنے سے عقل زائل ہو جاتی ہے اور یہ پتہ نہیں چلتا ہے کہ اس حالت میں ہوا نکلی یا نہیں نکلی ۔ اس لئے عقل زائل ہوتے ہی ہوا نکلنے اور وضوٹوٹنے کا حکم لگا دیا جاتا ہے۔ اس کو استرخاء مفاصل کہتے ہیں کہ تمام رگیں ڈھیلی ہو گئیں۔ لیکن اگر نیند گہری نہ ہو اور کچھ ہوش باقی ہو جیسے سجدے کی حالت میں، قیام کی حالت میں یا بیٹھے بیٹھے سو گیا تو چونکہ ابھی کچھ عقل و شعور باقی ہے اس لئے ہوا نکلنے اور وضو ٹوٹنے کا حکم نہیں لگائیں گے۔ کروٹ کے بل یا تکیہ لگا کر یا ٹیک لگا کر سونے سے عقل زائل ہو جاتی ہے اور نیند گہری ہوتی ہے۔ البتہ گرتا اس لئے نہیں ہے کہ تکیہ اور سہارا اس کو گرنے سے روکے ہوئے ہیں۔ اس لئے وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا (۲) حدیث میں دونوں قسم کے ثبوت ہیں عن علی ابن طالب رضی الله عنه قال قال رسول الله الا الله وكاء الله العينان فمن نام فليتوضا (الف) (ابو داؤد، باب في الوضوء من النوم ص ۳۰ نمبر ۲۰۳ (۳) قال رسول الله الا الله ان الوضوء لا يجب الا على من نام مضطجعا فانه اذا اضطجع استرخت مفاصله (ب) (ترمذی شریف ، باب الوضوء من النوم ص ۲۴ نمبر ۸ ) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ گہری نیند سونے سے وضو ٹوٹے گا۔ ہلکی نیند ہو تو وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن انس قال كان اصحاب رسول الله ينتظرون العشاء الآخرة حتى تخفق رئوسهم ثم يصلون ولا يتوضأون (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الوضوء من النوم ص ۳۰ نمبر ۲۰۰ / ترمذی شریف، باب الوضوء من النوم ، نمبر ۷۸) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیٹھے بیٹھے یا رکوع یا سجدے میں سو جائے جس میں گہری نیند نہیں ہوتی تو وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا

حاشیہ : (الف) ہوا کو روکنے والی چیز آنکھیں ہیں (یعنی بیدار آنکھیں ) پس جو سو گیا اس کو وضو کرنا چاہئے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا وضو نہیں واجب ہے مگر جو کروٹ پر سوئے ۔ اس لئے کہ جب کروٹ پر سوتا ہے تو اس کے جوڑ ڈھیلے ہو جاتے ہیں (تو ہوا نکلنے لگتی ہے ) (ج) صحابہ کرام عشاء کا انتظار کرتے رہتے یہاں تک کہ نیند سے جھونکے کھانے لگتے پھر نماز پڑھتے اور وضو نہیں کرتے۔
(23) And sleeping lying on one's side, or leaning, or resting against something such that if it were removed he would fall, and loss of consciousness (these things break wudu). (1) The principle is that from deep sleep or madness the intellect is removed, and it is not known whether wind (gas) was released or not in that state. Therefore, when the intellect is removed, the ruling of wind release and breaking of wudu is applied. This is called istirkha' al-mafasil (relaxation of joints) meaning all muscles loosen. But if the sleep is not deep and some awareness remains, such as sleeping in prostration, standing, or sitting, then because some intellect and consciousness remain, we do not rule that wind was released and wudu is broken. Sleeping on one's side, leaning on a pillow, or against something causes the intellect to be removed and sleep becomes deep. However, one does not fall because the pillow or support prevents it. Therefore, wudu breaks. (2) There are proofs of both types in hadith: From 'Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him): The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'Indeed, the eyes are the tie of the anus. So whoever sleeps, let him perform wudu.' (a) (Abu Dawud, chapter on wudu from sleep, p. 30 no. 203). (3) He said: 'Indeed, wudu is only obligatory upon one who sleeps lying on his side, because when he lies on his side his joints relax.' (b) (Tirmidhi, chapter on wudu from sleep, p. 24 no. 8). From these hadiths it is known that deep sleep breaks wudu. Light sleep does not break wudu. The evidence is the hadith from Anas: 'The Companions of the Messenger of Allah would wait for the Isha prayer until their heads would nod (from drowsiness), then they would pray and not perform wudu.' (c) (Abu Dawud, chapter on wudu from sleep, p. 30 no. 200 / Tirmidhi, chapter on wudu from sleep, no. 78). From this it is known that if one sleeps while sitting, bowing, or prostrating in a manner that does not involve deep sleep, wudu does not break.

Footnote: (a) The thing that blocks wind is the eyes (i.e., open eyes). So whoever sleeps should perform wudu. (b) He said: Wudu is not obligatory except for one who sleeps on his side, because when he sleeps on his side, his joints relax (so wind can escape). (c) The noble Companions would wait for Isha until they would nod from sleep, then they would pray without performing wudu.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding what types of sleep break wudu. The Hanafi position is that deep sleep that completely removes intellect (ghalaba 'ala al-'aql) breaks wudu because one cannot be certain whether wind (gas) was released. The physical sign of deep sleep is the relaxation of joints (istirkha' al-mafasil), which occurs when one sleeps lying on the side, leaning so that removal of support would cause a fall, or in a state of unconsciousness or madness. The principle is that when the controlling faculty (the 'eye' that holds gas) is released, the possibility of nullification is presumed. However, light sleep where some awareness remains, such as dozing while sitting, standing, bowing, or prostrating, does not break wudu because the joints are not fully relaxed and one can still sense if wind was released. Three hadiths are cited: (1) The hadith of 'Ali that 'the eyes are the tie of the anus' — meaning that awareness (open eyes) prevents involuntary gas release. Therefore, sleep (loss of awareness) necessitates wudu. (2) The hadith explicitly stating that wudu is obligatory only upon one who sleeps on his side (mudtaji'an). (3) The hadith of Anas that the Companions would doze while waiting for Isha and then pray without wudu. These hadiths together distinguish deep sleep (with complete loss of awareness and relaxation of joints) from light sleep (where some awareness remains). The footnote explains the meanings: the 'tie' is the eyes; when open they control the passage. The hadith about sleeping on the side indicates that relaxation of joints is the key. The behavior of the Companions shows that light sleep (like dozing) does not break wudu.

Key Terms
استرخاء مفاصل (istirkhā' al-mafāṣil): Relaxation of joints; the physical looseness of muscles and joints that occurs during deep sleep, indicating that one cannot control the release of wind.
غلبة على العقل (ghalaba 'alā al-ʻaql): Overpowering of the intellect; a state where the mind is completely overcome (by sleep, madness, or unconsciousness).
نوم مضطجع (nawm mudṭajiʻ): Sleep while lying on one's side, usually with the body horizontal. This position leads to relaxation of joints.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following sleep states breaks wudu?
A) Sleeping while sitting upright with awareness of surroundings.
B) Sleeping while lying on one's side with complete loss of awareness.
C) Dozing while waiting for prayer in a sitting position.
D) Sleeping in prostration if one does not lose awareness.

Key Takeaway
Deep sleep that removes intellect and relaxes joints breaks wudu; light sleep with remaining awareness does not.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Obligations and Sunnahs of Ghusl with Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling with proof for fard acts of ghusl, including a dispute with Shafi'i, followed by sunnah list.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three obligations of ghusl according to the Hanafi school, explain the evidence for madmadah and istinshaq being fard, and compare the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Rinsing the mouth and nose are obligatory in ghusl because every external part must be washed — even a single hair left dry invalidates it.

This passage from al-Sharh al-Sameri explains the obligations (fard) and Sunnahs of ghusl. While all schools agree that washing the entire body is obligatory, the Hanafi school uniquely holds that madmadah and istinshaq are also fard. The author provides Quranic and hadith evidence and addresses the Shafi'i objection. Understanding this ruling is essential for valid ghusl in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three fard acts of ghusl
From the passage, list the three actions that are obligatory: rinsing the mouth, inhaling water into the nose, and washing the entire body.
These are often referred to as the arkan (pillars) of ghusl.
2
Examine the Quranic and hadith evidence
The passage cites Quran 5:6 ('purify yourselves') and two hadiths: one from Ali (Abu Dawud) warning of punishment for leaving any spot dry, and another from Abu Hurairah (Dar Qutni) explicitly stating that the Prophet made madmadah and istinshaq an obligation.
The hadith from Dar Qutni is key: it uses the word 'fard' (fariḍah).
3
Understand the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school holds that the mouth and nose are part of the external body; therefore water must reach them. The Quranic command to 'purify' implies complete washing, and the hadith threats confirm that even a hair-sized dry spot invalidates ghusl.
This is the mufta bihi (operative) position.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that in ghusl, the Prophet performed wudu (where madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah), and a separate Dar Qutni hadith calls them sunnah. The Hanafi response is that the explicit hadith making them fard takes precedence, and wudu analogy does not override it.
The practical consequence: omission invalidates ghusl in Hanafi but not in Shafi'i.
5
Review the sunnah acts of ghusl
The passage lists eight sunnah acts in a specific order, based on the practice of the Prophet as reported by Aisha. These include washing hands, washing private parts, removing impurities, performing wudu, pouring water over head, pouring three times, moving aside, and washing feet last.
The order is sunnah; if changed, ghusl is still valid but with less reward.

Source Text

وفرض الغسل المضمضة والاستنشاق وغسل سائر البدن (۲۶) وسنة الغسل ان
غسل کے فرائض کا بیان یک
(۲۵) غسل کے فرض (۱) کلی کرنا (۲) ناک میں پانی ڈالنا (۳) پورے بدن کو دھونا ہے۔
(1) اصل میں پورے بدن پر پانی پہنچانا ہے کہ ایک بال برابر بھی خشک نہ رہ جائے۔ اور منہ اور ناک کے حصے بھی بدن کے باہر کے حصے شمار کئے جاتے ہیں۔ اس لئے کلی کر کے اور ناک میں پانی ڈال کر وہاں تک پانی پہنچا نا ضروری ہے (۲) آیت میں ہے وان كنتم جنبا فاطهروا ( آیت ۶ سورۃ المائدة (۵) آیت میں ہے کہ جنابت کی حالت میں خوب خوب پاکی حاصل کرو اور یہ اس وقت ہو سکتا ہے کہ کلی کر کے اور ناک میں پانی ڈال کر ہر جگہ پانی پہنچایا جائے۔ اس لئے کلی کرنا اور ناک میں پانی ڈالنا غسل میں فرض ہیں (۳) حدیث میں ہے عن على قال ان رسول الله الا الله قال من ترک موضع شعره من جنابة لم يغسلها فعل بها كذا كذا من النار (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الغسل من الجنابة ص ۳۸ نمبر ۲۴۹) معلوم ہوا کہ ایک بال برابر بھی غسل میں خشک رہ جائے تو غسل نہیں ہو گا اسی لئے کلی کرنا اور ناک میں پانی ڈالنا ضروری ہے۔ (۴) عن ابي هريرة ان النبي الا الله جعل المضمضة والاستنشاق للجنب ثلاثا فريضة (ب) ( سنن دار قطنی ، باب ماروی فی مضمضة والاستنشاق في غسل الجنابة ج اول ص ۱۲۱ نمبر ۴۰۳) فائدہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک کلی کرنا اور ناک میں پانی ڈالنا سنت ہیں۔ کیونکہ احادیث سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ آپ فنسل میں وضو کرتے تھے اور وضو میں مضمضہ اور استنشاق سنت ہیں۔ اس لئے غسل میں سنت ہونگے۔ دار قطنی میں دوسری حدیث ہے سن رسول الله الله الاستنشاق في الجنابة ثلاثا ( ج اول ص ۱۲۱ نمبر ( ۴۰ ) اس سے وہ سنت ثابت کرتے ہیں۔ امام مالک کے نزدیک کلی کرنا اور ناک میں پانی ڈالنا نسل میں بھی فرض ہے۔
غسل کی سنتوں کا بیان ہے
(۲۶) غسل کی سنتیں یہ ہیں (۱) غسل کرنے والا پہلے اپنے دونوں ہاتھوں کو دھوئے (۲) اور اپنی شرم گاہ کو دھوئے (۳) اور نجاست کو زائل کرے اگر اس کے بدن پر ہو (۴) پھر نماز کے وضو کی طرح وضو کرے مگر پاؤں ابھی نہ دھوئے (۵) پھر اپنے سر پر پانی بہائے (۶) اور پورے بدن پر تین مرتبہ پانی بہائے (۷) پھر اس جگہ سے الگ ہو جائے (۸) پھر دونوں پاؤں کو دھوئے۔
یہ آٹھ کام اسی ترتیب سے سنت ہیں۔ پاؤں پہلے اس لئے نہ دھوئے کہ غسل کا پانی پاؤں کے پاس جمع ہو گا اور پاؤں کو نا پاک کر دے گا۔ اس لئے اس کو اخیر میں دھوئے۔ البتہ پانی پاؤں کے پاس جمع نہ ہوتا ہو تو پہلے بھی پاؤں دھو سکتا ہے۔ حدیث میں اسی ترتیب سے ان سنتوں کا ذکر ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت كان رسول الله الله اذا اغتسل من الجنابة يبدأ فيغسل يديه ثم يفرغ بيمينه على شماله فيغسل فرجه ثم يتوضأ وضوءه للصلوة ثم يأخذ الماء فيدخل اصابعه في اصول الشعر حتى ا اذا رأي ان قد حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا جس نے جنابت سے ایک کے برابر بھی چھوڑ دیا اور نہیں دھو یا تو اس کے ساتھ آگ سے ایسا ایسا کیا جائے گا۔ یعنی عذاب دیا جائیگا (ب) حضور نے مضمضہ اور استنشاق کو جنبی کے لئے تین مرتبہ فرض قرار دیا (ج) حضور نے جنابت میں تین مرتبہ استنشاق کو سنت قرار دیا۔
And the obligation of ghusl: rinsing the mouth, inhaling water into the nose, and washing the rest of the body. (26) And the sunnah of ghusl: ... Explanation of the obligations of ghusl: (25) The obligations of ghusl: (1) rinsing the mouth, (2) putting water into the nose, (3) washing the entire body. (1) In principle, it is to make water reach the entire body so that not even a hair remains dry. The mouth and nose are considered parts of the external body. Therefore, it is necessary to rinse the mouth and put water into the nose to reach those areas. (2) The verse says: 'And if you are in a state of janabah, then purify yourselves' (Quran 5:6). The verse means to achieve complete purity, which can only be done by rinsing the mouth and nose and reaching water everywhere. Therefore, rinsing the mouth and nose are obligatory in ghusl. (3) The hadith: From Ali, he said: 'The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: Whoever leaves a spot the size of a hair from janabah without washing it, such and such will be done to him from the Fire.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Ghusl min al-Janabah, p. 38, no. 249). This indicates that if even a hair remains dry, the ghusl is not valid; hence rinsing the mouth and nose are necessary. (4) From Abu Hurairah: 'The Prophet ﷺ made rinsing the mouth and inhaling water into the nose for the person in janabah an obligation three times.' (Dar Qutni, Bab Ma Ruwiya fi al-Madmadah wa al-Istinshaq fi Ghusl al-Janabah, vol. 1, p. 121, no. 403). Benefit: According to Imam al-Shafi'i, rinsing the mouth and nose are sunnah because hadith indicate that the Prophet used to perform wudu in ghusl, and in wudu, madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah, so they would be sunnah in ghusl as well. There is another hadith in Dar Qutni: 'The Messenger of Allah made istinshaq in janabah three times as a sunnah.' (vol. 1, p. 121, no. 404). From this they prove it is sunnah. According to Imam Malik, rinsing the mouth and nose are obligatory in ghusl as well. Explanation of the sunnahs of ghusl: (26) The sunnahs of ghusl are: (1) The one performing ghusl first washes both hands, (2) washes his private parts, (3) removes any impurity from his body, (4) then performs wudu like the wudu for prayer but without washing the feet yet, (5) then pours water over his head, (6) pours water over the entire body three times, (7) then moves away from that place, (8) then washes both feet. These eight actions are sunnah in this order. The feet are not washed earlier because the water of ghusl will collect around the feet and make them impure; therefore they are washed last. However, if water does not collect around the feet, one may wash them earlier. The hadith mentions these sunnahs in this order. From Aisha, she said: 'When the Messenger of Allah ﷺ performed ghusl from janabah, he would begin by washing his hands, then pour water with his right hand over his left and wash his private parts, then perform wudu like the wudu for prayer, then take water and insert his fingers into the roots of his hair until he thought that...' Footnote (a): He said: 'Whoever leaves a spot the size of a hair from janabah without washing it, such and such will be done to him from the Fire,' i.e., he will be punished. (b) The Prophet made madmadah and istinshaq for a person in janabah an obligation three times. (c) The Prophet made istinshaq in janabah three times as a sunnah.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage explains the obligations (fard) and sunnahs of ghusl (ritual bath) in Hanafi fiqh. The passage type is a ruling with proof, including a dispute between schools. The author begins by stating that the obligations of ghusl are three: rinsing the mouth (madmadah), inhaling water into the nose (istinshaq), and washing the entire body. The reason is that the mouth and nose are considered external parts of the body; water must reach every part, including those hidden areas, otherwise a single dry hair invalidates the ghusl. Proofs are provided: the Quranic command 'فاطهروا' (purify yourselves) is interpreted to require complete washing, which necessitates reaching the mouth and nose. A hadith from Ali (Abu Dawud) warns of punishment for leaving any spot dry, and another hadith from Abu Hurairah (Dar Qutni) explicitly states that the Prophet made madmadah and istinshaq an obligation (fard) for the one in janabah. The author then notes a dispute: Imam al-Shafi'i considers them sunnah based on the fact that the Prophet performed wudu during ghusl, and in wudu these actions are sunnah. The Hanafi response is that the Dar Qutni hadith classifying them as fard takes precedence. Imam Malik holds that they are fard. The passage then lists the sunnahs of ghusl: eight actions in order, starting with washing hands, then private parts, removing impurity, performing wudu without feet, pouring water over head, pouring water over body three times, moving aside, and finally washing feet. The order is based on the practice of the Prophet as reported by Aisha, and the delay in washing feet is to avoid standing in the used water that may have become impure.

Key Terms
مضمضہ (madmadah): The act of rinsing the mouth in ghusl, considered obligatory in Hanafi fiqh.
استنشاق (istinshaq): The act of inhaling water into the nose in ghusl, considered obligatory in Hanafi fiqh.
غسل (ghusl): Ritual bath to remove major impurity (janabah, menstruation, postpartum bleeding), consisting of washing the entire body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what is the ruling on rinsing the mouth (madmadah) and inhaling water into the nose (istinshaq) in ghusl?
A) They are sunnah (recommended) but not required.
B) They are fard (obligatory) and leaving them intentionally invalidates the ghusl.
C) They are makruh (disliked).
D) They are only required if the person remembers them in wudu.

Key Takeaway
Madmadah and istinshaq are fard in ghusl according to the Hanafi school; the Shafi'i school considers them sunnah, but the Hanafi position is relied upon for fatwa.

Fard Acts of Ghusl with Inter-Madhhab Dispute
States the obligatory acts of ghusl with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers madmadah and istinshaq fard in ghusl, and contrast this with the Shafi'i view, evaluating the evidence.

Core Idea
Rinsing the mouth and sniffing water into the nose are fard in ghusl for Hanafis — omitting them invalidates the purification.

In this lesson, we examine the three obligatory acts of ghusl according to the Hanafi school. The inclusion of rinsing the mouth (madmadah) and sniffing water into the nose (istinshaq) as fard is a distinctive position, rooted in Quranic and hadith evidence. This lesson will walk you through the proofs and the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam Shafi'i, who considers these acts sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fard acts of ghusl
List the three acts the Hanafi school considers obligatory: rinsing the mouth, sniffing water into the nose, and washing the entire body.
These are considered fard; if any is omitted, the ghusl is invalid.
2
Examine the Quranic proof
Analyze the verse 'wa in kuntum junuban fathharu' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6) and how it implies full purification including the mouth and nose.
The imperative 'fathharu' is understood by Hanafis as requiring complete coverage of external body parts.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
Review the hadith from Abu Hurairah that the Prophet made madmadah and istinshaq fard for the junub, and the hadith of Ali warning of punishment for leaving a hair's breadth dry.
These hadith directly support the obligation.
4
Contrast the Shafi'i position
Understand the Shafi'i evidence: the Prophet performed wudu within ghusl, and in wudu these acts are sunnah; also a hadith in Dar Qutni calls them sunnah.
Shafi'is conclude that they are sunnah in ghusl by analogy to wudu.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical difference: if madmadah and istinshaq are omitted, Hanafis require repeating the ghusl, while Shafi'is consider it valid.
This affects the validity of subsequent worship relying on ghusl.

Source Text

(25) The obligatory acts of ghusl are: rinsing the mouth, sniffing water into the nose, and washing the entire body. (25) Explanation of the obligations of ghusl: (1) To rinse the mouth, (2) To put water into the nose, (3) To wash the entire body. (1) The essence is to reach water to the entire body so that not even a hair's breadth remains dry. The mouth and nose parts are also counted as external parts of the body. Therefore, it is necessary to reach water there by rinsing the mouth and putting water into the nose. (2) In the verse: 'And if you are in a state of janabah, then purify yourselves' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6). The verse means to achieve thorough purification in the state of janabah, and this can only happen by rinsing the mouth and putting water into the nose to reach water everywhere. Thus, rinsing the mouth and putting water into the nose are obligatory in ghusl. (3) In the hadith: 'Ali narrated that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Whoever leaves a spot the size of a hair from janabah without washing it, such and such will be done to him from the Fire.' (Abu Dawud) This shows that if even a hair's breadth remains dry in ghusl, the ghusl is invalid. Hence, rinsing and sniffing are necessary. (4) Abu Hurairah narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) made rinsing and sniffing for the junub three times an obligation. (Dar Qutni) Benefit: According to Imam Shafi'i, rinsing and sniffing are sunnah because the hadiths indicate that the Prophet performed wudu in ghusl, and in wudu these acts are sunnah. Therefore, they are sunnah in ghusl. In Dar Qutni, another hadith states: 'The Prophet made sniffing in janabah three times a sunnah.' With this they prove it is sunnah. According to Imam Malik, rinsing and sniffing are obligatory in ghusl as well.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute on the obligatory acts of ghusl. The Hanafi school holds that rinsing the mouth (madmadah) and sniffing water into the nose (istinshaq) are fard (obligatory) in ghusl, along with washing the entire body. The proof is from the Quranic command to 'purify yourselves' which implies thorough washing including these parts, and from hadiths that explicitly state these acts as obligations. The passage then notes that Imam Shafi'i considers them sunnah based on the practice of the Prophet who performed wudu within ghusl, and wudu's acts are sunnah there as well. Imam Malik, however, agrees with the Hanafis that they are fard. The Hanafi position is supported by the specific hadith from Dar Qutni calling them fard. The Urdu commentary further explains the reasoning, emphasizing that leaving any area dry invalidates ghusl, and that these areas are considered external body parts.

Key Terms
مَضْمَضَة (madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water three times
إسْتِنْشَاق (istinshaq): Sniffing water into the nose and then expelling it

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) They are sunnah
B) They are fard
C) They are mustahabb
D) They are makruh

Key Takeaway
Madmadah and istinshaq are fard (obligatory) in ghusl for Hanafis; omitting them invalidates the ghusl.

The Eight Sunnah Acts of Ghusl: Order and Proof
Lists the eight sunnah acts of ghusl in sequence with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eight sunnah acts of ghusl in their prescribed order and state the evidence from the hadith of Aisha.

Core Idea
Eight sunnah acts perfect the ghusl; feet are washed last to avoid impurity from used water.

In Hanafi fiqh, ghusl has obligatory (fard) acts and recommended (sunnah) acts. This passage lists the eight sunnah acts in the order taught by the Prophet (ﷺ). Understanding these sunan helps you complete your purification with the full reward. The order is based on the practice of Aisha (ra).

Guided Path
1
Enumerate the eight sunnah acts from the text.
Read the passage carefully and list the eight acts in the order they appear: (1) wash hands, (2) wash private parts, (3) remove impurity from body, (4) perform wudu except feet, (5) pour water over head, (6) pour water over entire body three times, (7) move away from that place, (8) wash feet.
The order is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Note the exception for the feet.
Understand why feet are delayed: the used water may collect and make the feet impure. If water does not collect, feet can be washed earlier.
This shows practical reasoning behind the rule.
3
Identify the evidence.
The hadith of Aisha (ra) is cited as the proof. The Prophet (ﷺ) consistently followed this order.
Hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Apply the ruling in practice.
When performing ghusl, follow this order to gain the full reward. If the order is changed accidentally, the ghusl is still valid.
Sunnah muakkadah means omission is not sinful but loses reward.

(26) The sunnah of ghusl is that the one washing starts by washing his hands and private parts, and removes impurity if on his body, then performs wudu like for prayer except for the feet, then pours water over his head and all his body three times, then moves away from that place and washes his feet. (26) Explanation of the sunnahs of ghusl: (26) The sunnahs of ghusl are: (1) The washer first washes his both hands, (2) and washes his private parts, (3) and removes impurity if on his body, (4) then performs wudu like for prayer but does not yet wash his feet, (5) then pours water over his head, (6) and pours water over the entire body three times, (7) then moves away from that place, (8) then washes both feet. Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement enumerating the sunnah acts of ghusl. The text first gives the Arabic matn listing the eight sunnah acts in sequence, followed by an Urdu commentary that explains each step and the reasoning behind the order. The key point is that the feet are deliberately left for last to avoid contamination with the used water that collects on the floor. If the water does not pool, the feet may be washed earlier. The hadith of Aisha is cited as evidence for this sequence. The commentary also mentions that these are sunnah, not fard, meaning the ghusl is valid if omitted but it is better to follow them. The Urdu adds that the order is sunnah, not obligatory.

Women Exempt from Undoing Braids in Ghusl if Water Reaches Roots
States the Hanafi ruling with its condition and scriptural proof for women's braids in ghusl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's braids in ghusl, identify the condition for the concession, and explain the proof from the hadith of Umm Salamah.

Core Idea
A woman need not undo her braids if water reaches the roots – a Prophetic concession for hardship.

The general rule in ghusl requires water to reach every hair root. But for women, the Prophet ﷺ granted a special concession: if water can penetrate the braids and reach the roots, she does not have to undo them. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its condition, and the textual evidence from the hadith of Umm Salamah, alongside the important hadith of Aisha that clarifies the necessity of wetting the roots.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (undoing braids) and the hukm level (it is not required – a rukhsa/concession). Note that the default obligation to wet the roots remains.
The ruling is specific to women; men with braids must undo them to wet the roots.
2
Locate the condition for the concession
Find the condition that triggers the concession: water must reach the roots of the hair. Without this condition, the default obligation applies.
The text emphasizes 'إذا بلغ الماء' (if water reaches).
3
Analyze the primary dalil (hadith of Umm Salamah)
Read the hadith where Umm Salamah asks about undoing her tight braid for janabah ghusl. The Prophet replied she need not undo it; three handfuls suffice. Understand the wajh al-dalalah: the explicit negation of the need to undo implies that the obligation is fulfilled by wetting the roots, which can be achieved without unbraiding.
This hadith is from Muslim (no. 330), classified as ahad, zanni al-thubut.
4
Reconcile with the hadith of Aisha
The source also cites the hadith of Aisha which describes vigorous rubbing to make water reach the roots. This shows that reaching the roots is necessary; the concession is only about the method (not undoing) if the roots can be wetted otherwise.
The Hanafi position combines both hadith: roots must be wetted, but unbraiding is not the only way.
5
Note the ikhtilaf and its thamarah
Some scholars (unspecified) argue that reaching the roots is not necessary at all, based solely on the hadith of Umm Salamah. The practical consequence: under their view, a woman's ghusl would be valid even if water does not penetrate to the roots, as long as she pours over her head. The Hanafi view requires wetting the roots.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.

(۲۷) وليس على المرأة ان تنقض ضفائرها في الغسل اذا بلغ الماء رأحفن على رأسه ثلاث حفنات ثم افاض على سائر جسده ثم غسل رجليه (الف) مسلم شریف، باب صفة غسل الجنابة ص ۱۴۷ نمبر ۳۱۶ ی / بخاری شریف، بخاری باب الغسل مرة واحدة ، ص ۳۹، نمبر ۲۵۷) اس حدیث سے ترتیب کے ساتھ سنتیں ثابت ہوئی استبرا نوں نجاست پہلے اس لئے زائل کرے تاکہ پورے بدن پر پھیل کر بدن کو اور ناپاک نہ کرے۔ اس لئے غسل کے شروع میں نجاست کو صاف کرنا ضروری ہے اگر بدن پر نجاست ہو۔ ت فرج : شرمگاه، یفیض : بدن پر پانی بہائے يتنحى : نحی سے مشتق ہے، ایک کنارے ہو جائے ،ہٹ جائے۔ (۲۷) عورت پر نہیں ہے کہ غسل میں اپنے جوڑے کو کھولے اگر پانی بال کی جڑ میں پہنچ جائے۔ (1) قاعدہ کے اعتبار سے جنابت، حیض اور نفاس کے غسل میں بالوں کی جڑ تک پانی پہنچانا ضروری ہونا چاہئے ۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ مرد کو جوڑا ہو تو اس کو کھولنا اور بالوں میں پہنچانا ضروری ہے۔ لیکن عورت کو حضور نے بار بار کی پریشانی کی وجہ سے خصوصی رعایت دی ہے کہ اگر سر کے تمام بالوں کی جڑ تک پانی پہنچ جائے تو جوڑے کو کھولنا ضروری نہیں (۲) حدیث میں ہے عورتوں کو جوڑا کھولنا ضروری نہیں ہے اگر بالوں کی جڑ تک پانی پہنچ جاتا ہو۔ عن ام سلمة قالت قلت یا رسول الله الله انى امرأة اشد ضفر رأسى افأنقضه لغسل الجنابة ؟قال لا ، انما یکفیک ان تحثی علی رأسك ثلاث حثيات ثم تفيضين عليك الماء فتطهرين (ب) ( مسلم شریف، باب حکم ضفائر المغتسلة ص ۱۴۹ نمبر ۳۳۰ / ابو داؤد شریف، باب المرأة هل تنقض شعرها عند الغسل نمبر (۲۵) اس حدیث کے چار حدیثوں کے بعد عائشہ کی حدیث ہے جس میں یہ لفظ ہے ثم تصب على رأسها فتدلكه دلكا شديدا حتى تبلغ شؤن رأسها (ج) (مسلم شریف، باب استعمال المغتسلة من الحیض فرصة من مسلک فی موضع الدم ص ۱۵۰ نمبر ۳۳۲) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ پانی بالوں کی جڑوں کے اندر پہنچانا ضروری ہے تب غسل ہوگا۔ اگر جوڑ انہیں کھول اور پانی جڑ تک نہیں پہنچا تو عورتوں کا غسل نہیں ہو گا۔ نا من بعض ائمہ کے نزدیک بال کی جڑ تک پانی پہنچانا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ ان کا استدلال حدیث ۳۳۰ سے ہے۔
(27) And it is not upon the woman to undo her braids in ghusl if water reaches... the head with three handfuls then pours over all his body then washes his feet. (a) Muslim, Kitab al-Ghusl, etc. This hadith establishes the sunnah in order. Removal of impurity: impurity should be removed first so that it does not spread over the body and make it more impure. Farj: private parts. yufid: pours water over body. yatanahha: moves away. (27) It is not upon the woman to undo her braids in ghusl if water reaches the root of the hair. (1) According to the general rule, in ghusl for janabah, hayd, and nifas, it is necessary to make water reach the roots of the hair. That is why if a man has a braid, he must undo it to reach the roots. But a woman is given a special concession by the Prophet due to repeated hardship: if water reaches the roots of all the hair of the head, she does not have to undo the braid. (2) In the hadith: Umm Salamah said: I said, O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who braids my hair tightly; should I undo it for ghusl of janabah? He said: No, it is sufficient for you to pour three handfuls of water over your head, then pour water over yourself and you become pure. (Muslim) After this hadith comes the hadith of Aisha with the wording: 'then she pours water over her head and rubs it vigorously until the water reaches the roots of her hair.' (Muslim) This proves that it is necessary to make water reach the roots of the hair for ghusl to be valid. If [a woman] does not undo her braid and water does not reach the roots, her ghusl is not valid. According to some scholars, it is not necessary to make water reach the roots; they use the hadith 330 as evidence.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning women's braids in ghusl. The Hanafi position: a woman does not have to undo her braids if water reaches the roots of her hair. This is a specific concession from the Prophet due to the hardship of repeatedly braiding and unbraiding hair. The general principle is that water must reach the hair roots, and for men with braids, undoing is necessary. The text cites the hadith of Umm Salamah as the primary proof. However, there is also a hadith of Aisha that indicates vigorous rubbing to ensure water reaches the roots. The commentary reconciles: if water reaches the roots without undoing the braid, that is sufficient; if not, the braid must be undone. Some scholars (unspecified) argue that reaching the roots is not necessary, using the same hadith; but the Hanafi position is the one that combines both narrations, requiring the roots to be wetted but not necessarily by undoing the braid if water can penetrate.

Key Terms
ضَفَائِر (ḍafā'ir): Braids or plaits of hair

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Water must reach the roots of her hair
C) She must pour exactly three handfuls
D) She must be in a state of janabah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on women's braids in ghusl is a balanced concession: water must reach the roots, but unbraiding is not the only means.

The Manner of Ghusl and Ruling on Unplaiting Hair
Ruling with proof: sunnah method and women's concession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sunnah order of ghusl and state the Hanafi ruling on whether women must undo their plaits, citing the relevant proof.

Core Idea
Women need not undo their braids in ghusl if water reaches the roots — a concession from the Prophet.

This passage explains the recommended method of performing ghusl and a key Hanafi dispensation for women. Understanding the interplay between the general principle that water must reach hair roots and the specific concession that unplaiting is not required is essential for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its sunnah order
Read the first part of the passage describing the sequence of ghusl: washing hands and private parts, removing impurity, performing wudu except feet, pouring water over head and body thrice, then washing feet.
This order is sunnah muakkadah, not fard.
2
Locate the ruling on women's hair
Focus on the statement: 'It is not upon a woman to undo her plaits if water reaches the roots.' This is the Hanafi position.
3
Trace the dalil from Umm Salamah
The hadith of Umm Salamah (Muslim 330) is cited: the Prophet (PBUH) explicitly said no to undoing plaits and instructed three handfuls over the head.
The negation (لا) indicates a concession.
4
Reconcile with Aisha's hadith
Aisha's hadith (Muslim 332) mentions vigorous rubbing until water reaches the partings. This is reconciled by requiring water to reach the roots, not necessarily undoing the plait.
The author stresses that if water does not reach roots, ghusl is invalid.
5
Determine the practical application
Conclude: women may keep plaits if water reaches roots; otherwise, they must undo them. The sunnah order is recommended but not obligatory for validity.
This is the mufta bihi position.

The one performing ghusl begins by washing his hands and private parts, and removes any impurity if present on his body. Then he performs wudu like for prayer except his feet. Then he pours water over his head and the rest of his body three times. Then he moves away from that place and washes his feet. (27) And it is not upon a woman to undo her plaits in ghusl if water reaches the roots. He poured three handfuls over his head, then poured over the rest of his body, then washed his feet. (A) [Hadith references]. From this hadith, the sunan with order are proven. Impurity removal first so that it does not spread over the body and make it impure. So at the beginning of ghusl, removing impurity is necessary if there is impurity on the body. (T: farj = private part, yufeed = pour water over body, yatanahha = go aside). (27) It is not upon a woman to undo her plaits in ghusl if water reaches the root of the hair. (1) By principle, in ghusl of janabah, hayd, and nifas, it is necessary that water reach the roots of the hair. That is why if a man has a plait, he must undo it and ensure water reaches the hair. But the Prophet (PBUH) gave special concession to women due to repeated difficulty: if water reaches the roots of all head hair, undoing the plait is not necessary. (2) In hadith: Women need not undo plait if water reaches roots. From Umm Salamah: I said O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who braids my hair tightly; shall I undo it for ghusl of janabah? He said no, it suffices you to pour three handfuls over your head, then pour water over yourself, and you become pure. (B) [Hadith references]. After four hadiths, there is the hadith of Aisha with the words: then she pours water over her head and rubs it vigorously until it reaches the partings of her head. (C) From this hadith it is proven that it is necessary to make water reach inside the roots of the hair; then ghusl is valid. If the plait is not undone and water does not reach the roots, the woman's ghusl is not valid. According to some imams, making water reach the roots is not necessary; they argue from hadith no. 330. Footnote: (A) The Prophet (PBUH) performed ghusl of janabah by first washing both hands, then pouring water from right hand to left and washing private part, then performing wudu like for prayer, then taking water and inserting fingers into hair roots until he saw they were wet, then pouring three handfuls over head, then pouring water over entire body, then washing both feet. (B) Umm Salamah: I said O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who braids my hair; shall I undo it for ghusl of janabah? He said no, it suffices you to pour three handfuls over your head, then pour water over yourself and become pure. (C) Then pour water over your head and rub vigorously until it reaches the plaits of the head.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, describing the sunnah method of ghusl (ritual bath) and the specific concession for women regarding unplaiting their hair. The author first states the recommended order: the person performing ghusl begins by washing the hands and private parts, removes any impurity from the body, performs wudu as for prayer except for the feet (which are washed later), then pours water over the head and the rest of the body three times, finally moving to a different spot to wash the feet. This order is based on sound hadiths, and the act of impurity removal at the start is to prevent spreading impurity. Then the author addresses a key Hanafi ruling: a woman is not required to undo her plaits (braids) during ghusl if water reaches the roots of her hair. The general principle (qā'idah) is that water must reach the hair roots for ghusl to be valid—this applies to men as well—but the Prophet (PBUH) gave women a special concession due to the difficulty of unbraiding and rebraiding. The evidence is the hadith of Umm Salamah in Sahih Muslim, where the Prophet said that pouring three handfuls of water over the head suffices. However, the author also cites another hadith from Aisha that indicates vigorous rubbing until water reaches the roots is necessary, which seems to contradict the first. The author reconciles by stating that the first hadith provides a concession only if water actually reaches the roots; if it does not, then the plait must be undone. A minority of imams hold that reaching the roots is not necessary, but the Hanafi position is that it is obligatory (fard) for ghusl, with the concession remaining. The footnote further clarifies the exact sunnah method of the Prophet.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): The ritual bath that purifies from major impurity (janabah, hayd, nifas).
ضفائر (dafā'īr): Plaits or braids of hair, specifically the tightly woven hair of women.
حثيات (hathayāt): Handfuls of water, typically three in number as per hadith.

Causes of Obligatory Ghusl: Maniy and Meeting of Circumcised Parts
States the two causes of obligatory ghusl and discusses conditions for maniy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two causes of obligatory ghusl and explain the Hanafi condition that maniy must exit with dafq (gushing) and shahwa (desire) for ghusl to be wajib.

Core Idea
Ghusl is wajib only if maniy gushes with desire; without both, it’s just madhi—wash and wudu, not ghusl.

This passage establishes the two grounds for obligatory ghusl: the emission of maniy under specific conditions, and full sexual intercourse (even without emission). The Hanafi school uniquely requires maniy to exit with gushing and desire, distinguishing it from other fluids like madhi. The text also presents the Shafi'i counter-argument and notes an internal Hanafi difference about the timing of desire. By studying this, you will understand not only the rulings but also the evidentiary basis and the practical consequence of the condition of dafq and shahwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two causes
Read the opening statement. The first cause is the emission of maniy (from man or woman) with two qualifiers: gushing and desire. The second cause is the meeting of the circumcised parts (intercourse) without emission.
The meeting of circumcised parts is a metaphor for full penetration; this cause is agreed upon by all schools.
2
Analyze the condition for maniy
The author explains that for maniy to necessitate ghusl, it must exit with dafq (forceful emission) and shahwa (desire). If it exits without desire, as in chronic illness (jariyan), only wudu is broken. Note the distinction between maniy and madhi/wadi.
Madhi (prostatic fluid) and wadi (after-urine discharge) do not require ghusl, only wudu.
3
Examine the proofs cited
The author cites the hadith of Ali (RA) where the Prophet distinguishes between madhi (wash private part and wudu) and maniy that gushes (perform ghusl). Also, Musnad Ahmad: 'If you gush it, perform ghusl; if not, do not.' Identify these as dalil naqli and note their thubut (authenticity) and dalala (indication).
The Hanafis consider these hadiths as specifying (mukhasis) the general command in 'Innama al-ma'u min al-ma''.
4
Understand the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i argues from the general hadith that any maniy requires ghusl. The Hanafi response is that this hadith is either abrogated or restricted by the more specific hadith of Ali. The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is clear: a person who emits maniy without desire (e.g., due to illness) needs only wudu in the Hanafi school, but ghusl in the Shafi'i school.
The Hanafi position is supported by the principle that a specific (khass) text overrides a general (amm) text when both are authentic.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifah and Muhammad consider the moment of separation from its place; if no desire at that instant, ghusl is not required. Abu Yusuf adds the condition that desire must be absent both at separation and at the moment of exit. The mufta bihi (operative position) follows Abu Hanifah and Muhammad.
This ikhtilaf arises from how strictly 'desire' is interpreted in relation to the emission process.

And the meanings that necessitate ghusl: (1) the emission of maniy in a gushing manner with desire from the man and the woman, (29) and (2) the meeting of the two circumcised parts without emission of maniy. [Urdu: undo, plaits is the plural of plait.] [Urdu: The causes for ghusl becoming wajib: (28) The matters that make ghusl wajib: (1) Mani exiting with gushing and desire from man and woman. (1) If mani exits with gushing and desire, ghusl becomes wajib. But if it exits without desire, as in the disease of jariyan (dribbling), then ghusl is not wajib; only wudu breaks. (2) The hadith indicates this: from Ali (RA) that the Prophet (PBUH) said to him: 'Do not do that. If you see madhi, wash your private part and perform wudu like for prayer. But if you gush water, then perform ghusl.' (A) [reference]. In Musnad Ahmad: 'If you gush it, then perform ghusl from janabah, and if you do not gush, do not perform ghusl.' (B) 'Hazafta' and 'fadahat' mean that if mani exits with gushing, perform ghusl; and this occurs when exiting with desire. (3) Madhi and wadi are also parts of maniy, but they do not exit with gushing, so ghusl is not required for them. Similarly, if maniy becomes thin like water due to illness and exits without pleasure and without gushing, like wadi, then it has no specificity of maniy, so ghusl is not wajib. As for Imam al-Shafi'i: He says that if maniy exits without pleasure and gushing, ghusl is still wajib. He argues that general hadiths do not restrict to gushing and desire, like 'Innama al-ma'u min al-ma'' (C) [reference]. So if maniy exits without desire, ghusl becomes wajib. And also that if a woman's maniy exits, ghusl is necessary for her. The proof is the hadith from Umm Salamah: '... Is there ghusl for a woman if she experiences a wet dream?' The Prophet said: 'Yes, if she sees water (i.e., maniy).' (D) [reference]. According to Imam Abu Hanifah and Imam Muhammad: If at the time of maniy separating from its place there is no desire, ghusl is not wajib. According to Imam Abu Yusuf: If at the time of maniy separating from its place and at the time of exiting there is no desire, only then ghusl is not wajib. (29) [The second cause] From the meeting of the private parts of man and woman without emission of maniy. Footnote: (A) The Prophet (PBUH) said to Ali: 'Do not do that. If you see madhi, wash your private part and perform wudu like for prayer. But if water gushes, then perform ghusl.' (B) If water gushes, perform ghusl of janabah; if it does not gush, do not perform ghusl. (C) Maniy exiting necessitates ghusl. (D) From Umm Salamah: She asked the Prophet if a woman has ghusl when she has a wet dream. He said yes, when she sees maniy.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, enumerating the causes that make ghusl obligatory (wajib). It opens by stating two primary causes: first, the emission of maniy (semen) characterized by dafq (gushing) and shahwa (desire) from both man and woman; second, the meeting of the two circumcised parts (i.e., the glans of the penis and the labia minora, or the entire private parts engaging in full sexual intercourse) even without emission. The author then elaborates on the first cause: for ghusl to become wajib, maniy must exit with both gushing and desire. If it exits without desire, as in cases of chronic illness (jaryan, madhi, wadi), only wudu is broken, not ghusl. This is supported by the hadith of Ali: the Prophet distinguished between madhi (which requires only washing and wudu) and maniy that gushes (which requires full ghusl). A hadith from Musnad Ahmad makes this explicit: 'If you gush it, then perform ghusl; if not, do not.' The author also notes that madhi and wadi are parts of maniy but do not gush, so they do not obligate ghusl. This condition of gushing and desire is the Hanafi position. The passage then reports the Shafi'i opposition: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that any emission of maniy, regardless of desire or gushing, obligates ghusl. His proof is the general hadith 'Innama al-ma'u min al-ma'' (Water comes from water), which he interprets broadly. The Hanafi response is not given in detail here, but the author implicitly supports the condition of dafq and shahwa by citing the hadith of Ali. An intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is also recorded: Abu Hanifah and Muhammad require the absence of desire at the time of separation from its place; Abu Yusuf requires the absence of desire at both separation and exit. The second cause (meeting of circumcised parts) is stated without further elaboration, as it is agreed upon and includes intercourse even without discharge.

Key Terms
منی (maniy): Semen or fluid that exits with gushing and desire, necessitating ghusl.
دفق (dafq): Gushing or forcefulness in the emission of maniy, indicating desire.
التقاء الختانين (al-tiqā' al-khatāmayn): The meeting of the two circumcised parts, i.e., full sexual intercourse where the male and female genitalia meet, even without emission.
مذي (madhi): Prostatic fluid that exits upon stimulation but without gushing; requires washing and wudu only.
ودي (wadi): Thick fluid that exits after urination; requires washing and wudu, not ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad), under which condition does the emission of maniy NOT require ghusl?
A) If it exits with gushing and desire.
B) If it exits in a dream without actual stimulation.
C) If at the time of separation from its place there is no desire.
D) If it exits after the age of 60.

Key Takeaway
Ghusl is wajib only due to two clear causes: intercourse (even without emission) and emission of maniy with gushing and desire—a Hanafi condition rooted in specific prophetic evidence.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
12 min
Three Causes of Ghusl: Mani, Genital Contact, and Hayd/Nifas
Ruling with proof and disputes on causes of ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three causes that obligate ghusl in the Hanafi school, identify the conditions for each cause, and explain the intra-madhhab and inter-madhhab disputes regarding emission of semen.

Core Idea
Ghusl is wajib by three causes: emission of semen with force and desire, genital contact without emission, and menstruation/postpartum bleeding.

In this lesson, we examine the classical Hanafi ruling on what makes ghusl obligatory. The author of al-Sharh al-Samari lists three distinct causes: the emission of semen (mani) under specific conditions, the mere meeting of the circumcised parts (genital contact) without emission, and the natural bleeding of menstruation (hayd) and postpartum (nifas). Each cause is supported by proof texts and accompanied by important disputes, including a well-known difference with Imam al-Shafi'i and a nuanced sub-dispute between the founding Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three causes
Read the passage to list the three causes that necessitate ghusl. The text numbers them as (28), (29), and (30).
Cause 1: mani emission with force and desire; Cause 2: genital contact (iltiqa' al-khitanayn) without emission; Cause 3: hayd and nifas.
2
Analyse the conditions for Cause 1
The passage specifies that for semen to obligate ghusl, it must be discharged with 'dafq' (gushing) and 'shahwah' (desire). Without these, only wudu is broken. Note the hadith from Ali (RA) that distinguishes madhi (wudu) from mani (ghusl).
The Arabic terms 'fadahat' and 'hazafat' indicate force/desire.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Within the Hanafi school, Abu Yusuf holds that for ghusl to be negated, desire must be absent both at the moment of separation and at exit. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say absence at separation alone suffices.
The mufta bihi is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
4
Trace the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that any emission of semen, with or without desire, obligates ghusl. His proof is the general hadith 'al-ma' min al-ma''. The Hanafi response is that this hadith is abrogated by the more specific hadith from Ali and others.
The thamarah (practical consequence) is that for Hanafis, a person with pathological discharge (e.g., jarayan) only needs wudu, while Shafi'is require ghusl.
5
Examine the second and third causes
For Cause 2, the text explains that insertion of the glans into the female circumcision area obligates ghusl even without ejaculation, based on the hadith 'when the circumcised parts meet'. For Cause 3, hayd and nifas are mentioned with Quranic verse and hadith commanding ghusl after purification.
The abrogation of the early rule 'al-ma' min al-ma'' is discussed in the context of Cause 2.

The explanatory text [Sharh al-Samari] Part One. Section: The Book of Purification. Fundamental principles (28) and the causes that necessitate ghusl: the emission of semen forcefully and with desire from a man and a woman (29) and the meeting of the two circumcised parts [genital contact] without the emission of semen. [...] Explanation: The woman's vagina has a membrane which the Arabs used to circumcise; this is the place of the woman's circumcision. When the man's circumcised part, i.e., the glans, enters that place, then ghusl becomes obligatory, even if there is no emission of semen. [...] (30) Menstruation and postpartum bleeding.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This is an expansion of the rulings on the causes necessitating ghusl. The text enumerates three causes: (1) emission of semen (mani) with force (dafq) and sexual desire (shahwah) from a man or a woman; (2) genital contact (iltiqa' al-khitanayn) without emission; and (3) menstruation (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas).

For the first cause, the author explains that if semen is discharged with force and desire, ghusl becomes wajib. If it flows without desire, as in the case of chronic illness (jarayan), ghusl is not required; only wudu is broken. This is supported by hadith from Ali (RA) where the Prophet distinguished between madhi (requiring washing the organ and wudu) and mani (requiring ghusl when it gushes). The author notes that both madhi and wadi are forms of seminal fluid but do not gush, so they do not necessitate ghusl. Similarly, if semen becomes thin due to illness and exits without pleasure or force, it does not obligate ghusl.

The text then discusses a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that ghusl is required for semen regardless of desire or force, citing the general hadith 'al-ma' min al-ma'' (water comes from water). Hanafis respond by pointing to the specific qualifying hadith. Within the Hanafi school, there is a sub-dispute: Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad say that if no desire is felt at the moment of separation of semen from its source, ghusl is not wajib; Abu Yusuf adds the condition that also at the time of exit there must be no desire.

For the second cause, the text explains that when the glans (hashafah) enters the female circumcision area, ghusl becomes wajib even without ejaculation. Initially in early Islam, the rule was 'al-ma' min al-ma'' (ghusl only if semen is emitted), but this was abrogated by the hadith from Aisha: 'When he sits between her four limbs and the circumcised parts meet, ghusl becomes wajib.' The abrogation was a concession due to scarcity of clothing, then later made obligatory.

For the third cause, menstruation and postpartum bleeding both necessitate ghusl. The verse (Q. 2:222) commands approaching women after they have purified themselves (tatahharna), which by consensus means after ghusl. A hadith from Aisha instructs a menstruating woman on how to perform ghusl. Postpartum bleeding is treated by analogy to menstruation. The author also mentions a hadith from Mu'adh in Mustadrak al-Hakim stating that a woman in nifas should wait seven days then bathe, but this is marked as a footnote.

Overall, the passage provides the Hanafi position with proof texts and clarifications on conditions.

Key Terms
الغسل (al-ghusl): Ritual washing of the entire body to remove major ritual impurity (janabah, hayd, nifas).
المني (al-mani): The thick fluid that gushes with orgasm from both sexes; its emission with force and desire makes ghusl wajib.
التقاء الختانين (iltiqa' al-khitanayn): The meeting of the two circumcised parts; refers to genital contact where the glans enters the female circumcision area, making ghusl wajib even without emission.
الحيض (al-hayd): The monthly menstrual discharge that flows from the womb; its cessation requires ghusl for purification.
النفاس (al-nifas): Postpartum bleeding following childbirth; treated analogously to hayd for ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, which of the following is NOT a cause that makes ghusl wajib?
A) Emission of semen with force and desire
B) Genital contact without emission
C) Seeing a wet spot without memory of a dream
D) Menstruation and postpartum bleeding

Key Takeaway
Ghusl becomes wajib in the Hanafi school only when semen exits with force and desire, when genital contact occurs, or when menstruation/postpartum bleeding ends.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Ghusl is obligatory from menses and postpartum bleeding
Explains the obligation of ghusl from menses and postpartum bleeding with Quranic and hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl from hayd and nifas and identify the Quranic and hadith proofs that establish the obligation.

Core Idea
Ghusl from menses and postpartum bleeding is fard, proven by Quran and hadith.

In this passage, the author establishes that ghusl (full-body wash) is obligatory for a woman after her menses (hayd) or postpartum bleeding (nifas) ends. The ruling is based on clear evidence from the Quran and the Sunnah, and it applies equally to both conditions. This lesson will walk you through the proofs and the reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify that the act discussed is ghusl from menses and postpartum bleeding. The ruling is fard (obligatory).
The author also uses the context of ghusl from intercourse to show consistency.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the Quranic verse (Surah al-Baqarah 2:222) and the hadith from Aisha (Bukhari and Muslim) cited as evidence.
The verse commands approaching women 'after they purify themselves,' interpreted as ghusl.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the evidence implies obligation: the verse uses an imperative form implying obligation, and the hadith explicitly describes how to perform ghusl from menses.
The hadith abrogated the earlier concession 'water is from water'.
4
Extend the ruling to nifas
Note that nifas is equated to hayd in the author's reasoning, so the same proofs apply.
A supplementary hadith from al-Mustadrak mentions ghusl after seven days if purity is seen.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
The Hanafi position is that ghusl from hayd and nifas is fard upon cessation of bleeding, with no fixed minimum duration for hayd beyond 3 days and maximum 10 days, and nifas up to 40 days.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the school.

(30) Menses and postpartum bleeding. Explanation: Inside the woman's private part there is a membrane which the Arabs used to circumcise; that is the place of the woman's circumcision. When the man's circumcision place, i.e., the glans, enters up to this point, ghusl becomes obligatory, even if no semen is discharged. (1) Because the place is hidden, it cannot be known whether semen came out or not. Therefore, the cause of discharge is placed in the position of discharge, and ghusl becomes obligatory. (2) It is in the hadith that at the beginning of Islam, it was that ghusl was not obligatory until semen came out, and this hadith was famous: 'Water is from water' (Muslim, chapter on statement that intercourse in early Islam did not necessitate ghusl unless semen is emitted, and its abrogation, and that ghusl is obligatory by intercourse, p. 155 no. 343). But later this ruling was abrogated, and there was consensus that merely by intercourse, ghusl becomes obligatory, even if no semen is emitted. In the same chapter is the hadith from Aisha: The Messenger of Allah said, 'When he sits between her four branches and the circumcision touches the circumcision, ghusl has become obligatory' (Muslim, p. 156 no. 349). (3) Abu Dawud (chapter on al-iksal, p. 32 no. 216) mentions the matter of abrogation in detail. The detail is that Ubayy ibn Ka'b informed him that the Messenger of Allah only made that a concession in early Islam due to scarcity of clothing, then he commanded ghusl and forbade that (Abu Dawud, no. 214). From this hadith it is known that merely by the disappearance of the glans, ghusl becomes obligatory even if no discharge occurs. (30) Ghusl becomes obligatory from menses and postpartum bleeding. (1) In the verse: 'They ask you about menstruation. Say: It is harm, so keep away from women during menstruation and do not approach them until they become pure. And when they have purified themselves, then come to them from where Allah has commanded you' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:222). The verse indicates that the menstruating woman should perform ghusl before intercourse. (2) In the hadith from Aisha: A woman asked the Prophet about her ghusl from menses; he commanded her how to perform ghusl: 'Take a piece of musk and purify yourself with it' (Bukhari, no. 314; Muslim, no. 332). From this hadith it is known that ghusl is fard upon the menstruating woman. Postpartum bleeding (nifas) is of the same degree as menses, so with all the proofs of menses, ghusl is also necessary in nifas. (1) However, a hadith is mentioned by al-Hakim in al-Mustadrak, which is in Kanz al-Ummal, from Mu'adh from the Prophet: 'When seven days pass for the woman in nifas, then she sees purity, let her perform ghusl and pray.' Footnotes: (a) He said: When a man sits on her four branches (i.e., private parts) and the circumcision meets the circumcision inside the woman's private part, ghusl is obligatory. (b) People ask you about menses. Say it is a harmful thing. So keep away from women during menses and do not approach them until they become pure. Then when they have purified themselves, have intercourse from where Allah has commanded you. (c) A woman asked the Prophet about ghusl from menses; he commanded her how she should perform ghusl. He said: Take a piece of musk and purify yourself with it. (d) Mu'adh (may Allah be pleased with him) narrated a marfu' report: When a woman in nifas passes seven days and then sees purity, she should perform ghusl and pray.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the obligation of ghusl (full-body ritual wash) from menses (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas). The author begins by establishing the foundational ruling that ghusl becomes obligatory due to sexual intercourse even without emission of semen, based on the hadith of Aisha and the abrogation of the earlier concession 'water is from water.' This foundational ruling is then applied to hayd and nifas. The author cites Quran 2:222, which implies purification (taharah) via ghusl, and the hadith where the Prophet instructs a menstruating woman on ghusl with musk, proving it is fard (obligatory). Nifas is equated with hayd in ruling, so similar proofs apply. The author also mentions a hadith from al-Mustadrak specifying ghusl after seven days of nifas upon seeing purity. This shows the Hanafi position that ghusl is mandatory for hayd and nifas, with evidence from Quran, hadith, and consensus (ijma).

Key Terms
حيض (hayd): Menses, the regular monthly blood discharged from a woman's uterus.
نفاس (nifas): Postpartum bleeding (lochia) after childbirth.
غسل (ghusl): Full-body ritual washing with water, obligatory after sexual intercourse, hayd, and nifas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Ghusl from menses and postpartum bleeding is fard, established by Quran (2:222) and hadith, and is required for the validity of worship and marital relations.
